201 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


C.C. v. A.B.


NO. Hd-5134


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Hampden


406 Mass. 679; 550 N.E.2d 365; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 74


September 13, 1989  
February 21, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Hampden Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on March 12, 1987.

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by David G. Sacks, J. The Supreme Judicial court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted an application for direct appellate review in plaintiff putative father action brought in the Hampden Division of the Probate and Family Court Department (Massachusetts) to establish his paternity when defendant mother was married to another man at the time of conception.


OVERVIEW: The mother asserted that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 209C, § 5(a) (1988) barred the putative father from bringing suit to establish paternity because it excluded the putative father from bringing suit since the mother was otherwise married. The putative father asserted that § 5(a) was unconstitutional in its denial of his standing to bring a paternity action. The court found that § 5(a) did not bar a putative father from attempting to establish paternity because the general equity jurisdiction of the Probate Court under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 215, § 6 provided for court access on that issue. Further, the court noted that the strict application of the presumption of legitimacy was no longer necessary. Thus, the court altered the standard of proof to require clear and convincing evidence. Because the trial record evidenced the requisite substantial parent-child relationship, the court concluded that the motion to dismiss should be denied so that the putative father could attempt to establish paternity. Because the putative father had a cause of action at common law, the court declined to decide whether Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 209C, § 5(a) (1988) denied him due process of law.


OUTCOME: The mother's motion to dismiss was denied, and the putative father was granted the opportunity to prove paternity under the general equity powers of the probate court.

 

202 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Johnson


No. 5166


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


406 Mass. 533; 548 N.E.2d 1251; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 53


October 3, 1989  
January 22, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENT found and returned in the Superior Court Department on September 8, 1988.

A motion to dismiss was heard by Cortland A. Mathers, J., and the case was heard by Robert W. Banks, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which convicted him of possessing a burglarious implement in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 49.


OVERVIEW: In the superior court, defendant pleaded guilty to the breaking and entering charged in the district court. Thereafter the Commonwealth sought and obtained an indictment charging him with possession of a burglarious tool during the breaking and entering that he pleaded guilty to. Defendant moved to dismiss both indictments and the motion judge dismissed the breaking and entering charge, but denied the motion as to the possession of a burglarious tool. Defendant was then convicted and sentenced to a term of imprisonment of from five to ten years. On appeal, defendant claimed, among other things, that his prosecution for possession of a burglarious tool violated both State and Federal prohibitions against double jeopardy because his prosecution was based on the same occurrence that resulted in his earlier guilty plea and conviction. The court on appeal affirmed defendant's conviction. The fundamental flaw in defendant's double jeopardy claim was that breaking and entering was not the same crime as possession of burglarious implements. The two were separate and distinct. Hence, there was no double jeopardy violation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for possessing a burglarious implement was affirmed.

 

203 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Lynn Teachers Union, Local 1037 v. Massachusetts Comm'n Against Discrimination


No. 4921


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Essex


406 Mass. 515; 549 N.E.2d 97; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 54; 59 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1819; 53 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P39,873


September 11, 1989  
January 22, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 28, 1985.

The case was heard by John T. Ronan, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court (Massachusetts) affirmed a ruling of the Massachusetts Commission Against Discrimination (the Commission), which found that appellant union engaged in illegal sex discrimination in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 4(1)(1988).


OVERVIEW: Female employees were forced to leave the school system once pregnant and were later rehired. Thus, their employment with the school system was not entirely consecutive, and, pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement, the union did not credit either employee for years of employment preceding pregnancy. Both employees filed charges of discrimination with the commission against the union, and the commission findings of discrimination in violation of § 4(1) were supported by the trial court. The union was ordered to credit the complainants for their pre-resignation seniority and the union challenged that ruling. On appeal, the court found that the seniority system credited the employees with fewer years of employment than they served solely because they became pregnant during their employment and were forced to resign. The refusal to credit the employees constituted a discriminatory act in violation of § 4(1), as the employees were discriminated against because of their sex. Because the union's violation was a continuing violation, the statute of limitations did not operate to bar the employees' claims.


OUTCOME: The trial court ruling was affirmed.

 

204 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Quincy City Hospital v. Rate Setting Com.


No. 4977


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


406 Mass. 431; 548 N.E.2d 869; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 42


October 2, 1989  
January 16, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTIONS commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on October 21, 1985, and April 17, 1986, respectively.

The cases were reported by Lynch, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospitals commenced an action in the Supreme Judicial Court for Suffolk County (Massachusetts), challenging defendant rate commission's assessment of the Medicaid reimbursement to which they were entitled for fiscal years 1983-1985.


OVERVIEW: The hospitals challenged the rate commission's assessment of the Medicaid reimbursement to which they were entitled for fiscal years 1983-1985. Specifically, the hospitals attacked the commission's use of a $ 70 per day rate for one component of the reimbursement formula in the superseded state statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6A, § 68, the codification of Mass. St. ch. 372 (1982), which controlled Medicaid payments in fiscal years 1983-1985. The court determined that the word "appeal" was a general descriptive term that had various meanings according to the circumstances in which it was used. Therefore, the court held that the Medicaid reimbursement rate for fiscal years 1983-1985 was computable by using the $ 70 per administratively necessary days rate, except where individual hospitals have contested the rate by appeal under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6A, § 36.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case and directed the trial court to enter a judgment that declared the Medicaid reimbursement rate for fiscal years 1983-1985 to be computed by using a $ 70 per administratively necessary days rate, except where individual hospitals contested the rate by appeal.

 

205 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Boston v. Keene Corp.


No. 5060


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


406 Mass. 301; 547 N.E.2d 328; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 416


October 2, 1989  
December 14, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 27, 1986.

The case was heard by John L. Murphy, Jr., J., on a motion for partial summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed an action against defendant manufacturers, seeking asbestos removal costs. The manufacturers sought a declaration under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231A that 1986 Mass. Acts 336, which extended the statute of limitations for actions brought by government entities, was unconstitutional, and filed a motion for summary judgment. The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) dismissed the motion and the manufacturers appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a city's action to recover asbestos removal costs, the court held that there existed a controversy over 1986 Mass. Acts 336 which required a prompt declaration of rights under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231A. The court held that 1986 Mass. Acts 336 was constitutional under Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 10, as it was not improper special legislation and was rationally related to a legitimate and permissive government objective. With respect to the revival claim, the court held that 1986 Mass. Acts 336 did not violate the manufacturers' substantive due process rights contained in Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights arts. 1, 10, and 12, insofar as the statute purported to revive claims already barred by the applicable limitations period. In so holding, the court concluded (1) the statute addressed an asbestos danger that related to the community's health, safety, and fundamental welfare; (2) the manufacturers' interest was a procedural bar that did not rise to the level of a vested right; and (3) the statute's scope was reasonable. The statute did not violate Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 30, as it did not alter the outcome of a completed judicial proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court held that, as a declaratory judgment was properly requested by the manufacturers, the order of the superior court dismissing their counterclaims was improperly entered. Accordingly, the judgment was vacated and a new judgment was entered declaring that the challenged statute violated no constitutional provisions raised by the manufacturers.

 

206 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Construction Industries of Massachusetts v. Commissioner of Labor & Industries


No. W-5013


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Worcester


406 Mass. 162; 546 N.E.2d 367; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 360; 29 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 1056; 114 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,188


October 4, 1989  
November 22, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 14, 1986.

The case was heard by James F. McHugh, III, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two trade associations and truck owners, brought an action against appellee, the commissioner of Labor & Industries, seeking an injunction that he had no authority to set wages under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 149, §§ 26-27F, for truck drivers who delivered concrete to public works construction sites. The Superior Court (Massachusetts) declared the statute unconstitutional and the trade associations sought review.


OVERVIEW: When the commissioner caused a criminal complaint to issue against the truck owners for failure to pay the posted wage, the trade associations and the truck owners sought to enjoin the pending and threatened criminal prosecutions. The court held that (1) usually a plaintiff had to exhaust his administrative remedies before seeking judicial relief, but where plaintiffs were essentially challenging the authority of a commissioner under the enabling statute and the resolution of this issue was in the public interest, declaratory relief was appropriate; (2) the commissioner was empowered to set wages for teamsters when there was a significant nexus between the work those teamsters perform and the site of the construction project; (3) the legislature could delegate to a board or officer the working out of the details of a policy adopted by the legislature; and (4) by requiring that the wages of employees on public works projects were not to be less than the wages paid in another segment of the economy, the statute had not improperly delegated legislative authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Superior Court was modified to declare that the commissioner had the authority to set wage rates for the drivers of trucks hauling bituminous concrete to public works projects.

 

207 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. O'Connor


No. 4968


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


406 Mass. 112; 546 N.E.2d 336; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 356


September 11, 1989  
November 20, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the Woburn Division of the District Court Department on December 22, 1987.

On appeal to the jury session of the Lowell Division a pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Isaac J. Borenstein, J., and the case was tried before him.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Massachusetts) convicted defendant of controlled substance offenses after denying his motion to suppress evidence of the contraband. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During a pat-search for weapons, a police officer seized controlled substances from defendant in what the commonwealth conceded was a violation of defendant's constitutional right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. When the police officer seized the drugs, he had already determined to "assist" defendant to the police station pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111B, § 8 (1988 ed.) because defendant was intoxicated. The commonwealth argued that because inevitably the drugs would have been found during a lawful inventory search of defendant at the police station, defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied. The court agreed, affirming the trial court's judgments. The court held that in the circumstances of this case, application of an inevitable discovery exception to the exclusionary rule was warranted. Under the inevitable discovery exception, premature discovery of evidence that would inevitably have been discovered by lawful means, without the need for a search warrant, did not render the evidence inadmissible, provided the commonwealth's case was not aided or the defendant's case harmed by the unlawful, premature discovery of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court denying defendant's motion to suppress and convicting him of controlled substance offenses.

 

208 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


McNamara v. Honeyman


No. 4790


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


406 Mass. 43; 546 N.E.2d 139; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 347


January 4, 1989  
November 13, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 10, 1983.

The case was tried before Raymond R. Cross, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a psychiatrist and the Commonwealth of Massachusetts, appealed a judgment from the superior court (Massachusetts) that, in a wrongful death suit by plaintiffs, a deceased patient's family, held the Commonwealth liable for the psychiatrist's negligence. The family appealed, among other things, a ruling that the psychiatrist was a public employee, under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258, a section of Massachusetts Tort Claims Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The decedent hanged herself while she was in the care of a Commonwealth hospital and under the direct supervision of the psychiatrist. After a jury trial in the family's negligence suit, which asserted claims against the Commonwealth and the psychiatrist (defendants) under the Act, the trial court left undisturbed the jury's finding that the psychiatrist was a public employee under the Act, entered judgment against the Commonwealth on the negligence claim, ruled that there was insufficient evidence to find the psychiatrist grossly negligent, and entered judgment notwithstanding the verdict in favor of defendants on the claims that they violated the decedent's federal civil rights. On appeal the court ruled, among other things: (1) that the psychiatrist was properly determined to be a Commonwealth employee and thus not liable for his own negligence; (2) because they owed a duty to the decedent duty to prevent the self-abusive or self-destructive acts, defendants were properly barred from asserting comparative negligence as a defense, and; (3) the Commonwealth was not a "person" under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and thus it was properly held not liable for alleged civil rights violations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The jury properly concluded that the psychiatrist was a public employee for purposes of the Act and that there was insufficient evidence to find that the psychiatrist was grossly negligent. The trial court did not err by directing a verdict for the family on the issue of comparative negligence of the decedent or by entering a judgment notwithstanding the verdict on the civil rights and pain and suffering claims.

 

209 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Cobb v. Cobb


No. M-5039


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


406 Mass. 21; 545 N.E.2d 1161; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 428


September 12, 1989  
November 8, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Ayer Division of the District Court Department on December 2, 1988.

Questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by Joseph T. Travaline, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife filed an application for direct review of the questions of law reported to the Appeals Court (Massachusetts) in her application for the issuance of an abuse prevention order against appellee husband pursuant to Mass. Gen. Law ch. 209A (1988).


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued an abuse prevention order in favor of the wife and against the husband pursuant to Mass. Gen. Law ch. 209A (1988) and reported questions of law to the appeals court. The wife filed an application for direct review of the questions of law. The court held that: (1) the case was moot because the order expired by its own terms and the husband did not violate the order, (2) it would decide the moot case because it involved the issue of the state's jurisdiction to enter an order that related to the federal government's property, (3) the issuance of the abuse prevention order was not precluded by the fact that the wife was a member of the armed services, (4) the order was effective against the husband on and off the army base, and (5) the order was effective on the confines of the army base.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the issuance of the abuse prevention order was not precluded by the fact that the wife was a member of the armed forces, the order applied to the husband's conduct on and off the army base, and the order was effective on the army base.

 

210 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Dockham


No. N-4865


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Norfolk


405 Mass. 618; 542 N.E.2d 591; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 242


May 3, 1989  
August 21, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended August 21, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: INDICTMENTS found and returned in the Superior Court Department on December 10, 1986.

The cases were tried before William H. Carey, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for rape, assault with intent to rape, child pornography pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A, and indecent assault and battery of two minor children. The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) convicted defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After having spoken to the minor child and reviewing the minor child's conduct in and out of the courtroom, the trial judge determined that the child was to testify by videotape. The court affirmed the convictions. The trial court's observations of the child justified the decision to videotape the testimony without the need for expert testimony under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 278, § 10. There was no abuse of discretion to admit the testimony of the child's fresh complaints even though such statements were made 11 days after the child was removed from the abusive setting. The expert testimony was admissible because it aided the jury in its determination of the ultimate issues. Testimony that the child lied was inadmissible where the lying was an isolated event. Because defendant did not object, the conviction under the child pornography statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A, was valid even though the statute was found to be unconstitutional in another case. Because defendant did not object at trial, the argument that the videotape testimony deprived him of a public trial under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 278, § 16D was not preserved for appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for rape, child pornography, and indecent assault and battery of two minor children.

 

211 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


English v. New England Medical Center, Inc.


No. 5015


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


405 Mass. 423; 541 N.E.2d 329; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 220


April 3, 1989  
July 20, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended August 21, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 17, 1983.

The case was tried before John C. Cratsley, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal injury complainants sought review of the decision of the superior court (Massachusetts) where the superior court granted defendant hospital's motion to reduce the jury verdict of $ 350,000 returned against defendant to $ 20,000 under the statutory liability cap for charitable institutions set forth in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 85K.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff personal injury complainants filed a medical malpractice action against defendant hospital and defendant physicians. The jury found liability only on the part of defendant hospital and assessed damages against it for $ 350,000. The trial court granted defendant hospital's motion to reduce the damages to $ 20,000, the liability cap set forth in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 85K. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The trial court held that § 85K was constitutional under both the United States Constitution and the Massachusetts Constitution. Section 85K did not violate plaintiffs' right to a jury trial because that right only arose with respect to issues made material by substantive law. Under Massachusetts law, plaintiffs had no right to a jury determination of damages in excess of the $ 20,000 cap set forth by statute. The court held that § 85K did not violate rights to equal protection and substantive due process. Section 85K did not burden a suspect group, and there was a legitimate purpose for the statute, namely to allow charitable institutions to use their funds toward their charitable purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that reduced the amount of plaintiff personal injury complainants' damages against defendant hospital to the statutory cap of $ 20,000 because the hospital was a charitable institution. The statutory cap did not violate plaintiffs' rights to a jury trial, nor did it offend constitutional rights to equal protection and substantive due process.

 

212 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Greenman v. Massachusetts Parole Bd.


No. 5014


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


405 Mass. 384; 540 N.E.2d 1309; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 210


March 7, 1989  
July 11, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 28, 1986.

The case was heard by Joseph S. Mitchell, Jr., J., on a motion to dismiss.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former inmate commenced a civil action, and the Superior Court Department, which dismissed the former inmate's civil action against defendant Massachusetts Parole Board for having refused to grant him parole, on four occasions. He claimed that the board deprived him of a liberty interest in a grant of parole. He had pleaded guilty to murder in the second degree and had been sentenced to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected the former inmate's arguments under the United States Constitution and the Massachusetts Constitution. The former inmate contended that, by virtue of the partial freedom afforded him under a supervised pre-parole program, he had a liberty interest in attaining the greater freedom of a parole. Upon appeal, the court stated that the former inmate's argument ignored the United States Supreme Court's distinction between being deprived of a liberty that one already had and being denied a conditional liberty that one desired. The court held that the individual characteristics of the Massachusetts statutory parole scheme did not give rise to a liberty interest under federal law. The court thus affirmed the trial court's judgment of dismissal of the former inmate's action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the former inmate's civil action since the Massachusetts statutory parole scheme did not give rise to a liberty interest under federal law.

 

213 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Freiberg


No. 4598


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


405 Mass. 282; 540 N.E.2d 1289; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 202


January 3, 1989  
July 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended July 24, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: INDICTMENT found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 18, 1986.

The case was tried before Robert A. Mulligan, J., and a motion for a new trial was heard by him.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Order denying motion for new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) for murder in the first degree on the basis that it was extreme atrocity or cruelty, and the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree on the basis of extreme atrocity or cruelty for the killing of a woman by severe blows to the head. He was identified by a witness who watched defendant attempt to bury the victim while she was still breathing. On appeal, the court affirmed. The retroactive application of another decision reached two weeks after the verdict which permitted a jury to consider evidence of mental impairment at the time of the crime in determining whether defendant had malice aforethought, did not create a substantial likelihood of a miscarriage of justice as defendant's behavior did not manifest signs of intoxication or mental impairment triggered by intoxication. The definition of extreme atrocity or cruelty provided satisfactory warning to potential defendants and was not void for vagueness. Viewing the evidence in a light most favorable to the prosecution, the court concluded that sufficient evidence existed for the jury to find extreme atrocity or cruelty. Defendant was not deprived of his right to an impartial jury by the requirement that he use peremptory challenges individually instead of after a full jury had been selected.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for murder in the first degree on the basis of extreme atrocity or cruelty was affirmed. The judgment and order denying defendant's motion for new trial was affirmed.

 

214 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. Board of Registration in Medicine


No. 4853


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


405 Mass. 103; 539 N.E.2d 50; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 174


March 8, 1989  
June 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on March 7, 1988.

The case was heard by Lynch, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A single justice of the court concluded that defendant Board of Registration in Medicine (board) did not have substantial evidence on the record to support its conclusion that plaintiff physician engaged in sexual misconduct and vacated the board's decision revoking the physician's registration to practice medicine. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board issued its final decision, revoking a physician's registration to practice medicine on the ground that he had engaged in sexual activity with his patient. On review, a single justice of the court concluded that the board did not have substantial evidence on the record to support its conclusion and vacated the board's decision. On further appeal, the physician argued that the board's decision denied him due process. The court held that the board abused its discretion in rejecting the administrative magistrate's determination of the credibility of the physician and the patient and in deciding that issue differently. The board failed to give substantial deference to the findings of the magistrate on matters of credibility. The board would have been justified in seeking a further explanation from the magistrate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment vacating the board's decision revoking the physician's registration to practice medicine and remanded to the board for further proceedings.

 

215 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Duarte v. Healy


No. 4893


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


405 Mass. 43; 537 N.E.2d 1230; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 161; 4 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 639


January 4, 1989  
May 10, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 25, 1985.

The case was heard by Joseph S. Mitchell, Jr., J., on motions for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff firefighter filed suit in the Superior Court of Middlesex County (Massachusetts) against defendants, the city manager and the fire chief, after the firefighter was fired for testing positive for cocaine. He claimed violations of the Massachusetts Civil Rights Act, Mass. Gen. Laws Ann. ch. 12, §§ 11H, 11I. The city manager alone was granted summary judgement on the basis of immunity. The firefighter and the fire chief both appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city of Cambridge implemented a drug testing policy, developed by the city manager and fire chief, for probationary firefighters. The fire chief set up the procedural aspects of the testing. The firefighter tested positive for cocaine and was fired. He filed suit against the city manager and the fire chief, alleging that his civil rights were violated and his right to privacy was violated. The trial court held that the city manager was immune from suit, but the fire chief was not. On appeal, the court held that both officials were immune. The immunities found in the Massachusetts Civil Rights Act included the standards of immunity for public officials developed under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The fire chief's involvement in the procedural aspects of implementing the drug testing policy was the type of discretionary action the immunity provisions were meant to cover. The court held that the functions were discretionary and there were no overriding federal or state constitutional, statutory, or regulatory provisions which controlled drug testing by urinalysis with which the city's policy interfered. The policy did not violate clearly established rights.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the firefighter's claims against the city manager and the fire chief..

 

216 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Wilczewski v. Commissioner of Dep't of Environmental Quality Engineering


No. 4907


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


404 Mass. 787; 537 N.E.2d 1204; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 154


December 7, 1988  
May 2, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 12, 1986.

The case was heard by James J. Nixon, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs brought an action against defendant, Commissioner of the Massachusetts Department of Environmental Quality Engineering (DEQE), to enjoin the DEQE from approving a revised plan for intervenor hospital's installation of a roadway, and for a declaration that the DEQE lacked jurisdiction to act on the revised plan. The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) dismissed the action and plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs opposed the hospital's proposed road through a wetland. Pursuant to the Wetland Protection Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 131, § 40 (1986), the hospital submitted a notice of intention to the local conservation commission outlining its plan for the roadway. The commission rejected the hospital's application. The hospital filed with the DEQE a request for a superseding order with conditions, pursuant to § 40. The hospital submitted a revised plan to the DEQE in support of its request for a superseding order. The DEQE stated that the revised plan might be approvable, but took no action on the plan. Plaintiffs then brought an action for injunctive relief. On plaintiffs' appeal from dismissal of their action, the court transferred the case from the court of appeals and affirmed. The court held that plaintiffs filed their action before the administrative process was completed and therefore had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The court held that judicial review of the DEQE action was available under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 30A, § 14 only after the DEQE issued a final order after an adjudication hearing on the request for superseding order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order dismissing plaintiffs' action against the DEQE in which plaintiffs sought to enjoin the DEQE from approving a revised plan for the hospital's installation of a roadway, and for a declaration that the DEQE lacked jurisdiction to act on the revised plan.

 

217 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Sasu


No. 4887


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


404 Mass. 596; 536 N.E.2d 603; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 105


January 3, 1989  
April 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] TRAFFIC CITATION issued on August 26, 1986.

The case was heard in the Cambridge Division of the District Court Department by Lawrence F. Feloney, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth sought review of the decision from the Appellate Division of the District Court (Massachusetts), which vacated a finding that defendant vehicle driver was responsible for failing to file a motor vehicle accident report as required by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 26 (1986), and ordered that a finding of "not responsible" be entered.


OVERVIEW: The police department notified the vehicle driver in August 1986 that he had failed to submit an accident report for the accident the previous June in which the vehicle driver killed a pedestrian. When the vehicle driver still failed to file the report, the police issued a motor vehicle traffic citation and assessed a fine. The vehicle driver was found guilty of vehicular homicide in December 1986. However, four months earlier, in September, the vehicle driver had filed the requested accident report with the police, claiming in the report his privilege against self-incrimination under the Fifth Amendment and Art. 12 of the Massachusetts Declaration of Rights. In October 1986 a magistrate entered a finding that the vehicle driver was "responsible' for failing to file the accident report. The trial court affirmed the magistrate's finding. The intermediate appellate court vacated the finding of "responsible." On appeal, the court determined that the vehicle driver had an absolute right to remain silent at least until the disposition of the criminal charges, and that his refusal to furnish an accident report could not be deemed a waiver of his privilege against self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the intermediate appellate court.

 

218 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Nissenbaum


No. Hd-4496


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Hampden


404 Mass. 575; 536 N.E.2d 592; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 106


April 4, 1988  
April 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENTS found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 15, 1981.

Pretrial motions to dismiss were heard by John F. Moriarty, J., and the cases were tried before William W. Simons, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On the court's own initiative the case against defendants who were found guilty of possession of marihuana with intent to distribute it unlawfully was transferred from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts).


OVERVIEW: Defendants, husband and wife, were found guilty of possession of marihuana with intent to distribute it unlawfully. Defendants appealed, contending that the conduct for which they were convicted was undertaken solely for their religious purposes and thus was protected under Mass. Const. art. II. The court transferred the appeals on its own motion. The court found that although defendants were members of the Ethiopian Zion Coptic Church, and Mass. Art. II protected the possession of marihuana and hashish for religious purposes, the Commonwealth could properly criminalize such conduct or practices without interfering with a right protected by the Mass. Const. The court concluded that religious freedom was not, and could not be, absolute under either the state of federal constitution. Balancing the competing interests, and giving significant weight and deference to the Legislature's determination that the possession, distribution, and cultivation of marihuana and hashish disturbed the public order, the court held that conduct in distributing marihuana was not protected by Mass. Const. art. II even if motivated by sincere religious purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants convictions for possession with intent to distribute marihuana.

 

219 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Great Atlantic & Pacific Tea Co.


No. Barn-4812


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Barnstable


404 Mass. 476; 536 N.E.2d 318; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 91


November 8, 1988  
April 4, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINTS received and sworn to in the Orleans Division of the District Court Department on July 25, 1985; August 15, 1985; and October 21, 1985, respectively.

On appeal to the jury session of the Barnstable Division the cases were heard by Richard P. Kelleher, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Orleans Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which entered convictions for unlawfully keeping open two of its stores in violation of the Sunday closing law.


OVERVIEW: The activity that formed the basis for the complaints was the sale of canned food items before noon on Sunday. On appeal, defendant argued that the first paragraph of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 136, § 6(50) (1986 ed.) provided the basis for its lawful sale on Sunday mornings of canned foods and other items not specifically mentioned in § 6. The court reversed the convictions, and remanded the action for findings of not guilty. In doing so, the court held that because defendant's literal reading of the statute was reasonable and without benefit of judicial interpretation, it was not adequately warned that its conduct violated the law. The court further held that the legislature intended in § 6(50) to allow stores to "open for business" on Sunday mornings only to sell those items made exempt by some other clause of § 6.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for unlawfully keeping open two of its stores in violation of the Sunday closing law was reversed. The action was remanded for findings of not guilty.

Commonwealth v. Feigenbaum


No. Barn-4797


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Barnstable


404 Mass. 471; 536 N.E.2d 325; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 92


November 8, 1988  
April 4, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the Barnstable Division of the District Court Department on May 19, 1986.

The case was tried before Richard P. Kelleher, J., in the jury session of that court.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the denial of his motion for a required finding of not guilty from the Barnstable Division of the District Court (Massachusetts), made at the close of the commonwealth's case in his trial for being a disorderly person in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53 (1986). The court transferred the case on its own initiative from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested during a protest when he blocked a roadway and refused to move. At his trial for being a disorderly person in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53 (1986), defendant moved for a required finding of not guilty. The motion was denied and he was convicted. Defendant appealed and the court reversed. The court held that the commonwealth failed to meet its burden of proof as to each of the essential elements of the crime. Although the commonwealth introduced evidence of defendant's conscious disregard of the risk of public inconvenience, annoyance, and alarm and his creation of a hazardous condition, it failed to prove that his actions were taken without legitimate purpose. Accordingly, the court reversed the conviction and entered judgment for defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of being a disorderly person and ordered judgment entered for defendant.

 

221 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Amirault


No. 4873


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


404 Mass. 221; 535 N.E.2d 193; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 65


December 6, 1988  
March 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENTS found and returned in the Superior Court Department on January 21, 1985, and September 19, 1985.

The cases were tried before Elizabeth J. Dolan, J., and a renewed motion for a new trial was considered by her.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed. Order denying motion for new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the appeals court (Massachusetts) affirming the denial of defendant's motion for a new trial following defendant's conviction of assault and battery on a child under the age of fourteen, rape of a child under the age of sixteen, and the sentencing of defendant to imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the lower court's decision affirming the denial of his motion for a new trial following defendant's conviction of assault and battery of a child and the rape of a child. The court held that it was not error to admit the fresh complaint of child witness and testimony corroborating that complaint. The trial judge properly instructed the jury concerning the evaluation of the complaint, and when there was no evidence the fresh complaint was not spontaneous, it was within the trial judge's discretion to admit the evidence. The court held that although the prosecutor's comments regarding defendant's post-arrest silence violated defendant's right to remain silent following his arrest, the judge's instruction was sufficient to cure the prosecutor's improper reference. The court held videotaped testimony of a child witness was properly admitted although the judge did not specifically find a "compelling need" for the procedure. There was ample evidence of a compelling need to avoid subjecting the child witness to emotional trauma of testifying in open court. The court held that additional information offered by defendant did not demonstrate juror prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant a new trial. New information offered by defendant did not demonstrate juror prejudice. Videotaped testimony of child witness was properly admitted based upon the compelling need of avoiding subjecting the child witness to emotional trauma. Trial judge's instructions were sufficient to cure prosecutor's improper remark referring to defendant's post-arrest silence.

 

222 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Cedeno v. Commonwealth


No. 4991


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


404 Mass. 190; 534 N.E.2d 293; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 57


January 6, 1989  
February 23, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended March 6, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on November 23, 1988.

The case was reported by Wilkins, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an action against the commonwealth in which he challenged the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(a), (c), which set forth somewhat inconsistent potential penalties for a conviction for the possession of cocaine with intent to distribute it.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the somewhat inconsistent potential penalties under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A (a), (c) for a conviction for the possession of cocaine with intent to distribute it made that statute unconstitutionally vague and that he could not have been properly convicted under either section. The court rejected defendant's argument. The court stated that there was no constitutional infirmity as to giving the prosecutor the discretion to bring a charge under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(a) or under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(c) because it was within the wide range of the prosecutor's discretion as to deciding if to bring criminal charges and in deciding which charges to bring. The court also held that the language of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A did not leave any doubt as to the legislature's intent, noting that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(a) proscribed conduct and prescribed a range of penalties for its violation and that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(c) proscribed conduct that also fell within the conduct that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(a) proscribed and prescribed a range of penalties.


OUTCOME: The court rejected the constitutional challenge that defendant raised as to the purported vagueness of two statutory provisions that provided for somewhat inconsistent potential penalties for a conviction for the possession of cocaine with intent to distribute it.

Department of Revenue v. Jarvenpaa


No. F-4897


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Franklin


404 Mass. 177; 534 N.E.2d 286; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 58


November 9, 1988  
February 23, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended March 6, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Orange Division of the District Court Department on October 9, 1986.

The case was heard by Allan McGuane, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action was commenced on behalf of the mother of an illegitimate child. Plaintiff Department of Revenue, child support enforcement division (DOR), was substituted for the Department of Public Welfare. The Orange Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) judge allowed defendant father's motion for summary judgment dismissing the action. The court on its own initiative transferred the case from the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The complaint sought a determination that the father was the minor's father, an order for suitable future support and health insurance for the child, and restitution of confinement expenses and of expenses since the child's birth. The father challenged the constitutionality of two provisions of a paternity act. He contended in the trial court that the proceeding was barred because in 1984, on a paternity complaint under Mass. The court also determined that the minor should not have been foreclosed by the prior judgment from presenting his own case for support. The court further concluded that the father had not shown that he was entitled to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment dismissing the action as to the DOR. The court vacated summary judgment dismissing the action as to the minor and remanded the case to the district court for further proceedings.

M & T Charters, Inc. v. Commissioner of Revenue


No. 4926


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


404 Mass. 137; 533 N.E.2d 1359; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 53


December 8, 1988  
February 14, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer, a company that chartered yachts, challenged the decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts), which denied an abatement of a use tax on a yacht purchased by the taxpayer under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 64I, §§ 2, 3, 8(f) (1986 ed.).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer purchased a yacht in Florida. The bill of sale listed Boston, Massachusetts as the documentation port. The boat was repaired at a Massachusetts shipyard, was chartered out of Massachusetts at least twice, and was docked in Massachusetts for at least two weeks each year. The taxpayer sought an abatement of the Massachusetts use tax, and claimed, among other things, that there was insufficient contact with Massachusetts to justify imposition of the use tax under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 64I. On appeal, the court concluded that the tax was properly assessed on the boat, but remanded the action back to the Appellate Tax Board for further proceedings to determine whether penalties were properly assessed, and for computation of interest and penalties. The court noted that the mere fact that a purchase was made out of state did not exempt a state with sufficient connection to the property from taxing the use or sale of that property.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the assessment of a Massachusetts use tax was proper on a yacht purchased in Florida but docked, repaired, and sailed out of Massachusetts, but remanded the case back to the Appellate Tax Board for proceedings to determine whether penalties should be assessed, and for calculation of interest and penalties.

Am. Dog Owners Ass'n v. City of Lynn


No. 4803


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Essex


404 Mass. 73; 533 N.E.2d 642; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 40


October 4, 1988  
February 9, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 22, 1986.

The case was heard by John P. Forte, J., sitting under statutory authority.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was before the court on its own motion to review the Superior Court, Essex County (Massachusetts) judgment, upholding two of three city ordinances restricting the ownership of "Pit Bulls" in appellant dog owners' action challenging the constitutionality of the ordinances and seeking damages and injunctive relief. They alleged the ordinances were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant dog owners filed an action, seeking damages and declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee city, alleging that city ordinances restricting the ownership and control of "Pit Bulls" were unconstitutional. The trial court upheld two of a series of three ordinances, but declared the third void for vagueness. Both sides sought review. The court transferred the case on its own motion and declared the case moot. Once the third ordinance became inoperable it did not revive the two prior ordinances. The third ordinance was itself impliedly repealed by a fourth ordinance that was not before the trial court. However, to conserve judicial resources and to guide future conduct of the parties, the court observed that if testimony regarding breed identification and the findings based thereon remain unchanged, then the fourth ordinance was as unconstitutionally vague as the third. Dog owners did not receive fair notice from the ordinance of the conduct proscribed or the dog "types" covered by the law. Such a law gave unleashed discretion to the dog officers charged with its enforcement and clearly relied on their subjective speculation of whether a dog was a "Pit Bull."


OUTCOME: The court declared the case moot and vacated the judgment with the notation that the decision was not on the merits. To conserve judicial resources, the court observed that a subsequent ordinance, not before the trial court, was as unconstitutionally vague as the ordinance that the trial court had invalidated in appellant dog owners' action against appellee city, challenging the constitutionality of city "Pit Bull" ordinances.

Waltham Tele-Communications v. O'Brien


No. 4762


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


403 Mass. 747; 532 N.E.2d 656; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 33


October 6, 1988  
January 9, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTIONS commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 7, 1986, October 9, 1986, and February 17, 1987, respectively.

The cases were consolidated and heard by Robert J. Hallisey, J., on motions for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted requests for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cable operators sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which was in favor of defendant property owners and which held that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 166A, § 22, was unconstitutional because it failed to provide for a jury determination of just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The cable operators brought complaints against the property owners seeking declaratory judgments as to their right of access to privately owned properties in order to install cable television facilities for residents living in multiple-dwellings units pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 166A, § 22 (1986). On cross-motions for summary judgment, the trial court held that § 22 was unconstitutional, and the court affirmed the decision. The court found that § 22 did not provide for a jury trial in compliance with Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 15. The court further found that nowhere in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 166A, § 22, was there any reference to a jury proceeding. The court held that it could not rewrite the statute to add the requirement of a jury trial omitted by the legislature. The court concluded that the suggestion that the legislature intended to provide for an alternative procedure through a mere statement of jurisdiction was implausible. The court refused to accept the strained conclusion that the comprehensive administrative compensation scheme crafted by the legislature could be ignored in its entirety by the property owners so as to pursue a jury trial right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the property owners and against the cable operators in the cable operators' action seeking access to the property owners' multiple-dwelling units.

Horsemen's Benevolent & Protective Asso. v. State Racing Com.


No. 4759


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


403 Mass. 692; 532 N.E.2d 644; 1989 Mass. LEXIS 12; 4 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 147


September 14, 1988  
January 9, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended January 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on December 23, 1986.

On transfer to the Superior Court Department the case was heard by George A. Sullivan, Jr., J., sitting under statutory authority, and was considered by him on a statement of agreed facts.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state racing commission sought review of an order from the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) ruling that its human drug testing of plaintiff licensees was unconstitutional and permanently enjoining further testing.


OVERVIEW: Licensees, race horse owners and trainers, filed suit against the state racing commission and alleged that the commission's human drug testing was unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that the testing violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and enjoined further testing. On review, the court affirmed the ruling below, but on the ground that the testing violated Mass. Const. art. XIV. The court held that the commission's drug testing program did not fall under the administrative search exception. Consequently, it assessed the reasonableness of the regulation by balancing the commission's need to conduct a random search against the invasiveness of the search and seizure.The court concluded that the commission's desire to deter the use of illegal drugs in Massachusetts race tracks, and its concern that the use of illegal drugs by licensees, whether on or off licensed premises, compromised the safety and integrity of the industry, could not justify random drug testing because the testing reached too far into the personal lives of the licensees. Additionally, testing upon "reasonable suspicion" was also found to be unconstitutional unless the requisites of probable cause were met.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the state racing commission's drug testing program was unconstitutional. The court held that testing upon "reasonable suspicion" could only occur if the requisites of probable cause were met.

Newspapers of New England, Inc. v. Clerk-Magistrate of Ware Div. of Dist. Court Dep't


No. Hs-4811


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Hampshire


403 Mass. 628; 531 N.E.2d 1261; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 302; 16 Media L. Rep. 1457


September 13, 1988  
December 22, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended December 19, 1988; As amended January 17, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Ware Division of the District Court Department on July 14, 1987.

The case was heard by Ann M. Gibbons, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Division of the District Court (Massachusetts) upheld an impoundment order issued in the state district court. The court had, on its own initiative and at the request of a newspaper and others, transferred the case from the appellate court. At issue before the court was whether the trial judge had abused her discretion in impounding an affidavit that had been used to support a search warrant in a murder case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted, and ultimately convicted, of murder in the first degree. The newspaper wanted access to the search warrant and the affidavit that had been used prior to the indictment. The court found that the trial judge did not abuse her discretion in impounding the affidavit. Notably, it was not defendant or the newspaper who asked for the decision in the case. The court decided, because of the strong public interest in the matter, to address the issue. Although the search warrant affidavit was a public record, the trial court had discretion to impound the affidavit when justice so required. In the instant case, the trial judge did not balance the competing interests of publicity against privacy. Rather, she balanced publicity against defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a fair trial. The trial judge appropriately took into consideration that the murder took place in a small rural community where the murder, the year-long investigation, and the arrest of defendant all received extensive news media coverage. Therefore, there was good cause for impounding the affidavit, and there was no common law or statutory impediment to the action of the trial judge.


OUTCOME: The court decided that, at the time the impoundment order was issued, the trial judge did not abuse her discretion in impounding the affidavit.

Bronstein v. Board of Registration in Optometry


No. 4662


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


403 Mass. 621; 531 N.E.2d 593; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 300


November 7, 1988  
December 20, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended December 23, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on October 30, 1987.

The case was reported by Wilkins, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant optometrist challenged the judgment from appellee, the Massachusetts Board of Registration in Optometry (board), which concluded that the optometrist violated Mass. Regs. Code tit. 246, § 5.06 (1986), Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 73B (1986), and Mass. Regs. Code tit. 246, § 5.07(3) (1986).


OVERVIEW: The board determined that the optometrist's leases were a fee-sharing arrangement in violation of applicable law. On appeal, the court remanded the case to the trial court for entry of a judgment reversing the portion of the board's order that found a violation of Mass. Regs. Code tit. 246, § 5.06 (1986). The court held that the optometrist's leases did not constitute a fee sharing arrangement merely because the lease called for percentage payments. The court held that unless, under the guise of a rental percentage lease, a lessor controlled the optometry practice or shared in income from particular patients because of referrals or consultation, percentage leases did not constitute fee sharing. The court remanded for dismissal those portions of the board's order concerning purported violations of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 73B (1986), which prohibited the practice of optometry on premises not separate from premises in which eyeglasses were sold. The court agreed with the parties to vacate the portions of the board's order concerning Mass. Regs. Code tit. 246, § 5.07(3) (1986), which prohibited advertising in affiliation with an optical company.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the board finding a violation of the prohibition against fee sharing. In addition, the court remanded the board's order concerning violations of the prohibition against practicing optometry on premises not separate from premises in which eyeglasses were sold. Lastly, the court agreed to vacate the board's order concerning the prohibition against advertising in affiliation with an optical company.

Edgar v. Edgar


No. N-4831


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Norfolk


403 Mass. 616; 531 N.E.2d 590; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 298


November 8, 1988  
December 19, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINT for divorce filed in the Norfolk Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on March 18, 1983.

A proceeding for contempt, commenced on February 2, 1987, was heard by David H. Kopelman, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former husband challenged the judgment of the Norfolk Division of the Probate and Family Court Department (Massachusetts), which entered a judgment of contempt against him for an arrearage of child support.


OVERVIEW: The former husband argued that the notice of a hearing on charges of criminal contempt against him was inadequate under due process standards and that the denial of a jury trial on the charges of criminal contempt for failure to pay child support violated his right to equal protection of the laws. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court stated that there was no doubt that the former husband was served with a copy of the complaint, which indicated that it could be treated as a complaint for either civil or criminal contempt. The court rejected the former husband's argument that once a state had provided for jury trial in some courts regardless of the length of the potential term of imprisonment, it had to permit jury trials in all courts. The court concluded that there was a rational basis for the distinction which permitted jury trials in some courts but not in others. The court reasoned that there was no provision for a jury trial in the probate courts but that the legislative classification was not purely arbitrary, did not create an invidious discrimination, and therefore did not violate the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which held the former husband in criminal contempt for failure to pay child support.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurers appealed an order of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) that granted defendant insurance commissioner summary judgment in suit by plaintiffs challenging Mass. OVERVIEW: Defendant insurance commissioner issued Mass. Regs. Code tit. 211, § 36.00 et seq. (1987) which prohibited certain insurance company practices pertaining to testing prospective insureds for exposure to AIDS. Plaintiff insurer sued challenging the regulations. The court reversed and ruled that defendant lacked authority, express or implied, to adopt the regulations challenged. Cherubino v. Board of Registration of Chiropractors


No. 4663


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


403 Mass. 350; 530 N.E.2d 151; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 262


September 12, 1988  
November 9, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on February 6, 1986.

The case was heard by Wilkins, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chiropractor challenged a judgment from the Supreme Judicial Court, Suffolk County (Massachusetts), which affirmed a decision by appellee Board of Registration of Chiropractors that the chiropractor had overutilized therapies in his practice of chiropractic medicine and had made improper charges. The Board suspended the chiropractor's license, stayed the suspension, and imposed a period of probation.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor claimed that the Board's decision was unsupported by substantial evidence; that Mass. Regs. Code tit. 233, § 4.06 (1986), proscribing overutilization of practice, was unconstitutionally vague; the Board did not have authority to impose sanctions for violations of § 4.06; the Board's decision was arbitrary and capricious; and the Board erred in refusing to admit in evidence a typewritten version of the chiropractor's handwritten patient progress notes and a chart summarizing the patient's treatment schedule. The court affirmed the decision of the Board because it concluded that there was no error. Among other reasons, the Board's decision was supported by substantial evidence. Persons of common intelligence could have concluded easily that the chiropractor repeatedly treated his patient with the same three costly supportive procedures without furnishing sufficient justification and a person of common intelligence would have known that such behavior was within the scope of activity proscribed by § 4.06.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter is to the lower court to enter a judgment affirming the decision of the Board that sanctioned the chiropractor for overutilizing therapies in his practice and making improper charges.
