La Grant v. Boston Housing Authority


No. 4835


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


403 Mass. 328; 530 N.E.2d 149; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 321


September 13, 1988  
November 7, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended November 10, 1988; As amended November 16, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 26, 1984.

The case was tried before John Paul Sullivan, J.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Boston Housing Authority appealed a judgment of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the jury verdict in favor of plaintiffs, minor and parents, in their personal injury suit.


OVERVIEW: The minor was injured in an accident, and his parents filed suit against the housing authority individually and on behalf of their minor son. The housing authority appealed an unfavorable verdict, which was affirmed. On further review, the court affirmed, holding that (1) the housing authority was a "public employer" within the meaning of the Massachusetts Tort Claims Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258, § 4 (Supp. 1986, 1987); (2) the cause of action arose prior to the effective date of 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 343, § 3, which provided that the Massachusetts Tort Claims Act did not apply to any civil action brought against a housing authority in a cause of action that arose prior to the effective date of 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 343, § 3; (3) the housing authority had standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 3 as a legislative encroachment on judicial power in violation of Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 30; (4) 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 343, § 3 was constitutional because it did not disturb a final judgment in the case; and (5) 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 343, § 3 properly operated in favor of the minor and his parents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the minor and his parents in their personal injury action against the housing authority.

 

234 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Gos v. Brownstein


No. Hd-4741


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Hampden


403 Mass. 252; 526 N.E.2d 1267; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 243


May 2, 1988  
August 17, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 3, 1982.

The case was heard by John F. Moriarty, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appeals Court (Massachusetts) dismissed a medical malpractice action for failure to attend a deposition and denied plaintiff patient's application pursuant to G. L. c. 261, § 27C(1) for payment of transportation expenses of counsel of defendant doctor and hospital to be incurred in taking the patient's deposition in Poland. Plaintiff patient sought review. The court transferred the case on its own motion.


OVERVIEW: A resident of Poland, while visiting in Massachusetts, underwent a laparoscopic tubal ligation performed by defendant doctor employed by defendant hospital. The patient returned to Poland and later brought an action against the doctor and the hospital alleging, inter alia, that she became pregnant, underwent an abortion and thereby suffered physical, emotional, and economic damages. She claimed negligence and breach of contract. The doctor noticed the patient's deposition. The patient sought a protective order on the grounds of indigency and her undergoing psychiatric care in an institution. The judge allowed her time in which to provide affidavits concerning her health and claim of indigency. Eventually the patient sought to have her deposition taken in Poland. The motion was denied and the substantive action dismissed. On appeal the order was affirmed. The court found that due process requirements could limit the sanction of dismissal. Where there was an inability to comply, it was necessary for an appellate court to know if the judge's action was predicated on a finding of willfulness, bad faith, or fault, unless it was clear that such a determination was implicit and warranted.


OUTCOME: The court vacated that part of the order that dismissed the action. As it did not appear on the record whether the appellate court ascertained if the judge's action was predicated on a finding of willfulness, bad faith, or fault, the court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

235 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Yankee Atomic Electric Co. v. Secretary of Commonwealth


No. 4794


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


403 Mass. 203; 526 N.E.2d 1246; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 239


May 5, 1988; August 3, 1988  
August 11, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 27, 1988.

The case was reported by Lynch, J.

The case was submitted on briefs.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff power company sought relief in the nature of certiorari and mandamus against defendant Attorney General challenging the certification of an initiative petition concerning nuclear power plants.


OVERVIEW: Power company challenged Attorney General's certification of an initiative petition pursuant to Art. 48, The Initiative, II, § 3, which would prohibit generation of electric power by nuclear power plants in the Commonwealth. Power company maintained that the petition, if enacted, would constitute a taking of property. The court affirmed the certification because Attorney General's summary contained all the facts implicit in the petition's language and subject to judicial notice, he did not arbitrarily omit facts apparently subject to his official notice, no permanent physical occupation or confiscation of property was proposed, but instead a regulation of use of property and no regulatory taking was established.


OUTCOME: The Attorney General's certification of the initiative petition was affirmed.

 

236 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. John G. Grant & Sons Co.


No. N-4634


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Norfolk


403 Mass. 151; 526 N.E.2d 768; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 224; 18 ELR 21474


May 5, 1988  
August 3, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the Quincy Division of the District Court Department on June 10, 1985.

On transfer to the jury session of the Dedham Division, the case was tried before Charles E. Black, J.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commonwealth sought review of an order of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which set aside a guilty verdict and a fine against defendant for filling or altering a fresh water wetland subject to flooding in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 131, § 40. The appeals court had determined that the penalty provisions of the statute were impermissibly vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a corporation that demolished buildings, moved large piles of scrap metal and rubbish onto its property, including a wetland. The trial court ruled that the offense had been a continuing one and that, once fill was deposited, its continued presence had allowed imposition of a daily fine. On final appeal, the court vacated the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, finding first that the fine provisions in § 40 and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 131, § 90 had not rendered the statute impermissibly vague, because limitations were placed on the range of fines that could have been imposed and the statute clearly defined the prohibited conduct and potential fines for violations. Since the continued presence of unauthorized fill was not a crime under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 131, § 40, the court held that the jury verdict had been based upon the trial court's improper ruling that the time fill was deposited on the wetland had not mattered because the complaint had charged a continuing offense. The court noted that the two-year limitations period in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 131, § 91 barred some of the Commonwealth's claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appeals court's decision that the verdict had to be set aside in the commonwealth's action against defendant for filling or altering a fresh water wetland subject to flooding. The court also vacated the judgment against defendant and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

237 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Santos


No. 4263


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


402 Mass. 775; 525 N.E.2d 388; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 206


March 8, 1988  
July 11, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENTS found and returned in the Superior Court Department on January 11, 1984.

Pretrial motions to suppress evidence were heard by John P. Forte, J., and the cases were tried before Sandra L. Hamlin, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) convicted defendant of murder in the first degree on a theory of felony-murder, armed robbery, assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon, and armed assault with intent to rob. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that a victim's one-on-one identification of defendant was not constitutionally permissible because the identification procedure was unconstitutionally suggestive and violated defendant's due process rights. The state argued that defendant waived his constitutional rights by assenting to the one-on-one confrontation. However, the court determined that the trial court failed to determine whether defendant's waiver was knowingly made. The trial court also should not have allowed the officers to corroborate the victim's identification. The trial court correctly determined that the witnesses' identification of defendant was constitutionally permissible and admissible as evidence and that the state's evidence was sufficient to withstand defendant's motion for a required finding of not guilty. Thus, the court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for murder in the first degree on a theory of felony-murder, armed robbery, assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon, and armed assault with intent to rob. The remanded for a new trial.

 

238 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Yankee Atomic Electric Co. v. Secretary of Commonwealth


No. 4794


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


402 Mass. 750; 525 N.E.2d 369; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 192


May 5, 1988  
July 7, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As amended October 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 27, 1988.

The case was reported by Lynch, J.

The case was submitted on briefs.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, electric company and 11 voters, filed a complaint seeking relief by way of certiorari and mandamus, respectively, to challenge defendant attorney general's certification of an initiative petition pursuant to Mass. Const. art. XLVIII. c. II, § 3. Plaintiffs also sought to prevent defendant secretary of the commonwealth from having the initiative placed on the ballot in the upcoming election.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general certified a petition entitled "The Stop Nuclear Waste Act" and sent it to the secretary of the commonwealth to be put on the ballot in an upcoming election. Plaintiffs, who owned and operated nuclear reactors in the state, argued that the petition effected a taking of their property, failed to provide for compensation making it inconsistent with the right to just compensation, and the attorney general should not have certified the petition. The court entered an order directing the attorney general to reexamine the petition and to determine whether he would affirm his certification. The court reasoned the attorney general should have considered the petition's factual impact when certifying that it did not contain excluded subjects. The court stated that based on the record it was not clear that the attorney general considered the facts implicit in the petition's language and the facts susceptible to official notice. The court remanded the matter to him to consider such facts and determine which were not within these categories.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order remanding the matter back to the attorney general and directed him to reexamine the matter to consider the facts implicit in the petition's language and the facts susceptible to official notice and to determine whether he would affirm his certification.

 

239 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Nigro v. Attorney Gen.


No. 4746


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


402 Mass. 438; 523 N.E.2d 467; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 149


May 5, 1988  
May 25, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on November 4, 1987.

The case was reported by Wilkins, J., on a stipulation of agreed facts.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens brought an action under Mass. Const. art. 48 to quash defendant commonwealth's certification of an initiative petition to repeal the prevailing wage law for the commonwealth and its cities and towns. The citizens contended that the certification violated article 48 because the title to the petition was not in the proper form for submission to the people for a vote.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth certified an initiative petition that purported to repeal the prevailing wage law for the commonwealth and its cities and towns, and the citizens brought an action to quash the certification on the ground that the petition was not in proper form for purposes of Mass. Const. art. 48. The court upheld the certification and found that article 48 did not require the proposed law's title to describe the law to any particular degree, or to be wholly accurate so far as it was descriptive. The court ruled that the proper form requirement in article 48 related to avoiding drafting errors and that the form requirement was not intended to become an inquiry into the proposed law's substance. Because titles to proposed laws tended to be short, the court found that they were not practical vehicles for conveying detailed information about the law's content, especially if the measure was complex, and an accurate summary could correct any harm caused by a misleading title. The court also rejected the citizens' argument that a sufficiently descriptive title was required for the benefit of the legislature because it often dealt with non-descriptive titles in proposed legislation.


OUTCOME: The court rejected the citizens' complaint and held that the commonwealth correctly certified the petition for a vote by the people.

 

240 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Eagleton


Nos. W-4534, 3575


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Worcester, Suffolk


402 Mass. 199; 521 N.E.2d 1363; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 126


January 4, 1988  
April 19, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINTS received and sworn to in the Worcester Division of the District Court Department on October 28, 1983.

In the jury session of that division, the cases were tried before Anthony J. Tomasiello, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.

CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on April 26, 1984.

The case was heard by Lynch, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Worcester Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) that convicted him of storing flammable fluids without a license and refusing to allow an authorized officer to conduct an inspection pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 66 (1986 ed.). Defendant also sought review of a judgment from a single justice of the court that denied interlocutory relief under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a licensed auto body shop and used car business. Defendant was convicted of storing flammable fluids without a license in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 148, § 13 (1986 ed.) and violating Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 67 (1986 ed.) by refusing to allow an authorized officer to conduct an inspection pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 66 (1986 ed.). On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction and the judgment by a single justice of the court that denied interlocutory relief with respect to the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint. The court determined that the police officers were constitutionally entitled to conduct a warrantless inspection of defendant's business premises. The court found that defendant's body shop business was a "closely regulated" business for U.S. Const. amend. IV purposes. The court determined that the police officers were lawfully on the premises and properly sought complaints for defendant's failure to be licensed once the fact came to their attention. The court ruled that defendant waived his appeal with respect to the single justice's denial of pretrial relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of storing flammable fluids without a license and refusing to allow an authorized officer to conduct an inspection. The court also affirmed the judgment by the single justice that denied interlocutory relief.

 

241 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Shields


No. W-4515


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Worcester


402 Mass. 162; 521 N.E.2d 987; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 94


December 7, 1987  
April 14, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the Spencer Division of the District Court Department on January 12, 1987.

On appeal to the jury session of the Worcester Division questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by Thomas F. Sullivan, Jr., J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court was required to decide if the state was required to prove that there was no less intrusive alternative to a sobriety roadblock, which would have been effective to accomplish the legitimate public safety goals of the state, as a prerequisite to the admission of evidence obtained as a result of the roadblock under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Mass. Const. art. 14.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped at a sobriety roadblock, field sobriety tested, and arrested and charged with operating his vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. During his trial, defendant moved to suppress the evidence obtained as a result of the roadblock, and the trial court sent a question to the court. The court held that the state was not required to prove, as a prerequisite for admission of the evidence, that there was no less intrusive alternative to a sobriety roadblock which would have been effective to accomplish the legitimate public safety goals of the state. The court held that admission of the evidence without that proof did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV and Mass. Const. art. 14.


OUTCOME: The court held that the state was not required to prove, as a prerequisite for admission of evidence obtained as a result of a sobriety roadblock, that there was no less intrusive alternative which would have been effective to accomplish the legitimate public safety goals of the state.

Commonwealth v. Vieira


No. Br-4354


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 828; 519 N.E.2d 1320; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 64


November 3, 1987, Argued  
March 10, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Bristol.

 [***1] Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 16, 1983.

The cases were tried before William G. Young, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which convicted defendants of aggravated rape pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 22(a) (1986). The court denied the defendants' motions for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The defendants argued that their due process rights were violated by the prosecution's failure to provide timely disclosure of certain inconsistent pretrial statements made by the victim. The court held that there was no prejudice. The court held that because there was thorough cross-examination, no prejudice resulted from the judge's denial of voir dire, an alternative form of relief requested in defendants' motion for dismissal with prejudice. The court held that there was no prejudice with regard to preparation of a defense theory. The court held that none of defendants' asserted grounds for new trials related to delayed disclosure of inconsistent statements or warranted reversal of the convictions. The defendants challenged various evidentiary rulings made during the course of trial and argued, that the rulings deprived them of a full and fair opportunity to present their defense. The court held that the defendants received a full opportunity to present their defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendants of aggravated rape.

 

243 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Glass


No. S-4022


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 799; 519 N.E.2d 1311; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 60


December 7, 1987, Argued  
March 9, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Glass v. Bissonnette, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26110 (D. Mass., Feb. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk.

 [***1] Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on September 23, 1983.

The cases were tried before Sandra L. Hamlin, J., and a motion for a new trial was heard by her.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) of murder in the first degree, three counts of assault with intent to murder while armed, and three counts of assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon. Defendant appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant testified that he was threatened by four men acting together and argued that he acted reasonably in self-defense. The Commonwealth's evidence tended to show that defendant could have easily fled the scene after one of the victims had pushed him off the front steps of a house. Instead, defendant drew a knife and successively stabbed the four victims, chasing the last two into their house in order to do so. Defendant contended that the self-defense instruction was defective because it implied that the self-defense defense arose only as to victims who actually, personally assaulted him. He argued that self-defense applied to all the victims although only one of them pushed him off the porch. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that the trial court was correct in instructing the jury to consider self-defense victim by victim because a factual middle ground concerning defendant's state of mind was not obvious. The jury could have believed defendant's version that four men collectively threatened him and he reacted in self-defense, or the jury could have believed that the defendant successively attacked four men, three of whom never threatened him in any way.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for murder in the first degree, assault with intent to murder while armed, and assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon were affirmed.

 

244 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Stamboulis v. Stamboulis


No. W-4536


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 762; 519 N.E.2d 1299; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 59


October 6, 1987, Argued  
March 7, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Worcester.

 [***1] Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 20, 1985.

The case was heard by Barbara J. Rouse, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, daughter and father, sought review of an order of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) granting defendant mother's motion for summary judgment, in the daughter and father's negligence action.


OVERVIEW: The mother operated a restaurant, and took her minor daughter to work with her. When the mother went to answer the phone, the daughter got her hand caught in the dough rolling machine, and was injured. The father and daughter brought suit against the mother for negligence. The superior court granted summary judgment to the mother, finding that she was immune from liability, under the theory of parent-child immunity. The court ruled that the mother was not entitled to immunity. In so ruling, the court rejected prior decisions carving out a special exemption for motor vehicle tort actions. The court held that the status of the tortfeasor did not, in and of itself, warrant immunity in vehicular, or any other type of tort, actions. While determining that the superior court erred in granting the mother immunity, the court noted the mother's relationship to the victim was relevant to a determination of the duty of care the mother owed to her daughter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's order granting the mother's motion for summary judgment. The court remanded for further proceedings.

 

245 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Fine v. Contributory Retirement Appeal Bd.


No. S-4461


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 639; 518 N.E.2d 1151; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 31


October 9, 1987, Argued  
February 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk.

 [***1] Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 20, 1980.

The case was heard by Elbert Tuttle, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Contributory Retirement Appeal Board (board) appealed a decision from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which held that plaintiff employee's classification as a group four employee, which subjected him to retirement at age 65 under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 3(2)(g) (1986), violated the employee's constitutional right to equal protection under the law. The matter was transferred to the court on its own motion.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a supervising hearing officer. The employee claimed that his classification as a group four employee deprived him of rights secured by the equal protection clause of the fourteenth amendment and by the Massachusetts Declaration of Rights. The trial court agreed, and ordered that the employee be classified as a group one employee, which subjected the employee to mandatory retirement at age 70. The board appealed, and the court reversed the decision of the trial court, and remanded the case. The court held that § 3(2)(g) was constitutional because the employee could not prove that the statute could not be supported upon any rational basis of fact. The court found that assuring the high quality of supervising hearings officers was a legitimate, rational objective. The fact that the group four designation was somewhat over-inclusive or under-inclusive, or perhaps not entirely coextensive with similar positions, was not fatal to an equal protection analysis. The court found the fact that group four was not entirely homogenous could have been the result of an incremental process of legislative definition, which did not offend equal protection principles.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which held that the employee's classification as a group four employee deprived him of his rights under the equal protection clause and under the Massachusetts Declaration of Rights. The court remanded the case for entry of a judgment affirming the board's decision.

 

246 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Oakes


No. W-4289


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 602; 518 N.E.2d 836; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 29


February 3, 1987, Argued  
February 1, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Worcester.

 [***1] Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on January 9, 1985.

A pretrial motion to dismiss was heard by Robert V. Mulkern, J., and the case was tried before John J. Irwin, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the verdict set aside. The indictment is to be dismissed. So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court Department, Worcester County (Massachusetts), which found him guilty of child pornography under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A. defendant permitted his 15-year-old stepdaughter to pose with her breasts exposed for photographs he took of her in their home.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of knowingly permitting a child under 18 years of age to pose or be exhibited in a state of nudity for purpose of visual representation or reproduction under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A. He sought review, challenging the law's constitutionality. Upon review, the court reversed his conviction and dismissed the indictment, holding that § 29A was unconstitutional. The court found that the statute was overbroad because it criminalized conduct that virtually every person would regard as lawful. The court held that for example, the law made a criminal of a parent who took a frontal view picture of his or her naked one-year-old running on a beach or romping in a wading pool. The court held that the First Amendment protected that kind of activity, thus, the law was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for knowingly permitting a child under 18 years of age to pose or be exhibited in a state of nudity for purpose of visual representation or reproduction.

 

247 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


New York & Massachusetts Motor Service, Inc. v. Massachusetts Com. against Discrimination


No. Hd-4428


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 566; 517 N.E.2d 1270; 1988 Mass. LEXIS 24; 49 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1267; 47 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P38,356


September 11, 1987, Argued  
January 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Hampden.

 [***1] Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 23, 1985.

The case was heard by Elizabeth A. Porada, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant employee brought an action against respondent employer under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 4 and Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, alleging religious discrimination. Respondent Massachusetts Commission against Discrimination (commission) found for the employee and awarded him lost wages and interest. The Superior Court (Massachusetts) affirmed. The court granted the employer's request for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a member of the Worldwide Church of God, and he observed several holy days during which time he could not work. The employer required 12 drivers to operate its business and observed a one-man-off vacation policy. The employee requested, in advance, a certain time off to observe a holy day. The employer denied the requests. The employer discharged the employee when he returned to work from the holy day. The employer argued that the commissioner's findings were deficient. The court held that: (1) substantial evidence support the finding that the employer could have accommodated the employee by redistributing his duties with other drivers in that the employer was given a substantial amount of time to respond to the request had flexibility in reassigning its employees; (2) redistribution did not impose an undue hardship on the employer because its staffing levels did not fall below the 12 employees needed to operate the business did not incur more than a de minimis cost during the employee's absence; and (3) the commissioner failed to deduct the unemployment compensation that the employee had received for the backpay award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the employee. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for remand to the commission for recalculation of the backpay award and the interest thereon.

 

248 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Tenneco, Inc. v. Commissioner of Revenue


No. S-4546


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 380; 516 N.E.2d 1164; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1538


November 6, 1987, Argued  
December 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision of the Massachusetts Appellate Tax Board (board) which affirmed the refusal of the Commissioner of Revenue (commissioner) to abate additional taxes assessed against the corporation pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 63, § 52A, for the years 1977, 1978, and 1979. The corporation claimed error as a matter of law, and state and federal constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: The corporation challenged the denial of its request for abatement of additional tax assessments. The corporation argued that its corporate activities had become so diverse that only a portion of its activities could properly be classified as utility related. Therefore, the company asserted, it should be taxed as a business corporation, or, at a minimum, its non-utility operations should be taxed under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 63. The court found that the mere labeling of the source of dividend income as foreign did not preclude the state from including that income in the pre-apportionment tax base. The court held that the corporation failed to demonstrate, before the board, the absence of a rational relationship between the dividend income from its non-pipeline subsidiaries and values connected with its Massachusetts operations. The court concluded that inclusion of the dividend income in the pre-apportionment tax base did not violate due process. The court held that the challenged taxing scheme did not discriminate against utility corporations, including the corporation, since such corporations were able to utilize the abatement procedure in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62C, § 37.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's decision that affirmed the commissioner's decision to abate additional taxes assessed against the corporation.

 

249 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Aronson v. Commonwealth


No. Hd-4268


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 244; 516 N.E.2d 137; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1525


February 5, 1987, Argued  
December 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 20, 1985.

The case was heard by Elizabeth A. Porada, J., on motions for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer requested a declaratory judgment that the tax differential in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62, §§ 2(b) and (4) (1986 ed.) was unconstitutional and a refund of any tax collected unlawfully. The Massachusetts superior court denied the taxpayer's motion for summary judgment and concluded that the differential tax rates were not unconstitutional under the United States Constitution or Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 44.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that the tax violated the Equal Protection and Commerce Clauses of the United States Constitution and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 44. On appeal, the court held that the Commonwealth was not entitled to summary judgment on the Commerce Clause claim. The savings deposits involved interstate commerce because the state's resident and out-of-state banks were involved. The doubling of the tax rate solely because of the location of the taxpayer's deposits clearly had a protectionist effect in favor of local financial institutions. Facially, the statute discriminated in favor of in-state banks in the competition for state deposits, and thereby foreclosed tax-neutral decisions. The collection and verification difficulties, which were not controverted on the record, constituted actual underlying differences between in-state and out-of-state interest income. Thus the grant of summary judgment for the Commonwealth as to the Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 44 claim was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied the taxpayer's motion for summary judgment. The court reversed the judgment in favor of the Commonwealth and remanded for a trial limited to the commerce clause claim.

 

250 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Therriault


No. Br-4406


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 237; 515 N.E.2d 1198; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1520


November 2, 1987, Argued  
December 10, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Taunton Division of the District Court Department on January 21, 1985.

On appeal to the jury session of the Fall River Division, the case was heard by Robert L. Anderson, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Fall River Division (Massachusetts), which convicted defendant of homicide by motor vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant contended that the mandatory sentencing provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24G(A) (1984) violated provisions against cruel and unusual punishment, violated his rights to due process, and offended the doctrine of separation of powers.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was drinking alcohol and drove his vehicle into the rear of a van. Defendant's passenger was killed and defendant was charged with homicide by motor vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss and the trial court denied the motion. Defendant was found guilty, and the trial court imposed the minimum statutory penalty of imprisonment in a house of correction for one year. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court held that the statute under which defendant was convicted, § 24F(a), was not unconstitutional. The court reviewed the nature of the offense and the offender in light of the degree of harm to society, a comparison of the challenged punishment with other punishments imposed within the state, and a comparison of the challenged punishment with punishments imposed for the same or similar crimes in other jurisdictions. Based on this review, the court upheld the conviction and further held that defendant failed to meet the burden of demonstrating that the statute lacked a rational basis. Finally, the court found that there was no violation of the separation of powers doctrine in the one-year minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for homicide by motor vehicle while intoxicated.

 

251 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices to House of Representatives


No. S-4476


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 1211; 515 N.E.2d 1169; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1513



December 7, 1987 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] We answer questions 1, 2, and 3, "No." We therefore, answer question 4, "No."


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Massachusetts House of Representatives submitted an order adopted by the body containing six questions regarding the constitutionality of Mass. Senate Bill No. 3, a pending measure to restructure the savings bank life insurance system governed by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 178.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner Massachusetts House of Representatives presented six certified questions regarding the constitutionality of Mass. Senate Bill No. 3 (Bill), proposed legislation restructuring the savings bank life insurance system that provided low-cost insurance in the state. The court responded, first, that the assumption by the Savings Bank Life Insurance Company of Massachusetts (company) of the assets and liabilities of the insurance departments of banks would not deprive banks or policyholders of property rights without due process of law. Savings and insurance banks did not have a property interest in most insurance department assets and a bank's property right to invested money would not be denied without due process protections provided in the Bill. The court also held that the due process and contract rights of insureds would not be violated by the company's assumption of their policies. Policyholders would not be materially disadvantaged by the company's management of their policies. Further, the court found no substantive due process infirmity in the method for creating the company and allocating the stock under the Bill.


OUTCOME: The court responded in the negative to six questions submitted by petitioner Massachusetts House of Representatives regarding the constitutionality of a pending measure to restructure the savings bank life insurance system. On all questions, the court found that the bill would not violate contract or due process rights guaranteed under the Massachusetts Constitution or the United States Constitution.

 

252 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices to Senate


No. S-4495


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


401 Mass. 1201; 514 N.E.2d 353; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1489



October 19, 1987 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The undersigned Justices answer the question, "Yes."


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Senate of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts posed a question to the court as follows: Would said § 1 of Senate No. 1893, if enacted into law, violate the provisions of Mass. Const. § 2, art. 46 (Art. of Amend.)? The question concerned only § 2 of art. 46 of the Articles of Amendment, known as the "anti-aid" amendment, not whether Senate No. 1893 would violate the U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Mass. Const. § 2, art. 46 (Art. of Amend.), the "anti-aid" amendment, prohibited the appropriation or use of public money for the purposed of maintaining or aiding a primary or secondary school which was not publicly owned and controlled. Senate No. 1893 involved a "grant, appropriation or use of public money" within the meaning of art. 46, § 2. The court noted that the fact that the expenditure took the form of a tax deduction rather than a direct payment out of the treasury did not alter the result, for tax subsidies or tax expenditures of this sort are the practical equivalent of direct government grants. There are three criteria for testing the sufficiency of a statute under art. 46, § 2: (1) whether the purpose of the challenged statute is to aid private schools; (2) whether the statute does in fact substantially aid such schools; and (3) whether the statute avoids the political and economic abuses which prompted the passage of art. 46. The court found that the purpose of the challenged bill was to give aid to private schools in an indirect form; substantial assistance to private schools would be given, and the bill would have violated the general purpose of art. 46 § 2.


OUTCOME: The court held that the proposed senate bill, if enacted, would have violated the state constitution, at least in so far as it authorized a tax deduction for amounts expended on tuition and textbooks for students of private elementary and secondary schools.

Commonwealth v. Repoza


No. M-4308


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


400 Mass. 516; 510 N.E.2d 755; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1416


March 2, 1987, Argued  
July 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 11, 1978.

A motion for postconviction relief, filed on August 17, 1984, was assigned to and considered by Hiller B. Zobel, J.

After review by the Appeals Court the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.

The case was submitted on briefs.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Appeals Court the Supreme Judicial Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed defendant's conviction of murder in the second degree and denied his motion for a new trial. Defendant was, however, granted leave to obtain further appellate review for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether new case law required the court to grant defendant's request for postconviction relief, following the affirmance of his conviction of murder in the second degree. In his brief on appeal, he argued that the jury instructions, part of which were erroneous because they created impermissible mandatory presumptions, failed to explain the erroneous language sufficiently, thereby violating the requirements of a case decided after defendant's motion was denied. Defendant's case was affirmed on direct appeal since it was decided that the other language of the charge cured the erroneous instruction. A case was decided that held that the other language in the charge did not cure language in the instructions which impermissibly shifted the burden. The court noted that judicial holdings concerning impermissible burden-shifting language in instructions were generally applied retroactively. The court concluded that that the judge's charge impermissibly shifted the burden of proof to defendant contrary to principles and that a new trial was required.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's request for post-conviction relief and ordered a new trial following the prior court's affirmance of his conviction of murder in the second degree. The court concluded that the affirmance was based on principles contrary to new case law, that the judge's charge impermissibly shifted the burden of proof to defendant, which was not cured by other language in the instruction.

Solimeno v. State Racing Com.


No. S-4199


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


400 Mass. 397; 509 N.E.2d 1167; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1401


November 3, 1986, Argued  
July 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 17, 1985.

The case was heard by Haskell C. Freedman, J., sitting under statutory authority.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: The judgment as to Ross is reversed, and the case is remanded to the Superior Court for the entry of a judgment affirming the commission's decision as to him. The judgment as to the other plaintiffs is affirmed. So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, licensed kennel owners, greyhound trainers, and assistant trainers, sought review of a decision from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed in part a decision of the State Racing Commission, which upheld defendant park's exclusion of plaintiffs from its premises and suspended the licenses of some plaintiffs. The park filed a cross-appeal as to the superior court's reversal of the decision as to one plaintiff trainer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs refused to enter their greyhounds for racing at the park and thus the park issued ejection notices to them pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 128A, § 10A (1984). Plaintiffs appealed their ejections to the commission, which upheld the park's action and also suspended the licenses of some plaintiffs. Plaintiffs sought further review and the superior court affirmed the commission's decision except as to one plaintiff trainer. The court affirmed in part the superior court's decision and reversed in part as to the one plaintiff, holding that: 1) § 10A authorized the exclusion of any person whose presence was detrimental to the orderly conduct of racing, including persons licensed under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 128A, § 9A to participate in horse and dog racing; 2) plaintiffs failed to demonstrate that their boycott constituted speech entitled to First Amendment protection; 3) plaintiffs were on notice that the commission's hearing could result in license suspensions and even if such notice was defective, they demonstrated no prejudice; and 4) the commission's suspension of the one plaintiff trainer's license was supported by evidence that he knowingly joined the boycott.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment and reversed as to the one plaintiff trainer, remanding the case to the superior court with instructions to enter a judgment suspending his license, thus affirming completely the commission's decision upholding the park's exclusion of all the plaintiffs from its premises and suspending the licenses of some plaintiffs for refusing to race their greyhounds at the park.

Bromfield v. Commonwealth


No. P-4337


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


400 Mass. 254; 508 N.E.2d 842; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1357


April 8, 1987, Argued  
June 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth.

Petition filed in the Superior Court on March 1, 1971.

A motion for relief from judgment, filed on February 6, 1986, was heard by Augustus F. Wagner, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Order denying relief from judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review from a Plymouth Superior Court (Massachusetts) judgment, which denied their request to reopen a judgment in their favor in their suit against appellee state.


OVERVIEW: A group of taxpayers filed suit and received a satisfied judgment on their claim for damages and interest in connection with the taking of their land by the state. Later, they sought to reopen the judgment to recover prejudgment interest at the rate of 10 percent instead of an earlier rate of six percent, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 79, § 37 (1981). When the lower court denied their motion for entry of a second partial and final judgment, the taxpayers appealed. The court held that (1) the taxpayers would have been entitled to the benefit of the interest statute had their case not gone to judgment; (2) relief from the judgment pursuant to Mass. R. Civ. P. 60(b)(1) on the grounds of a mistake on the part of the lower court in computing the prejudgment interest because such relief had to be sought within one year of the judgment, and the taxpayers had failed to comply with that requirement. Because there had been no demonstration of any abuse of discretion, the lower court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order denying the taxpayers' request for relief from the judgment against the state.

258 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Blood


No. E-4137


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


400 Mass. 61; 507 N.E.2d 1029; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1326


October 9, 1986, Argued  
May 20, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 27, 1981.

A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Robert J. Hallisey, J., and the cases were tried before James D. McDaniel, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: The order denying the defendants' motions to suppress is set aside. An order allowing the motions is to be entered in the Superior Court. The judgments of conviction are reversed and the verdicts set aside. So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were found guilty of conspiracy to break and enter a building and conspiracy to commit larceny. The Superior Court (Massachusetts) denied their motions to suppress evidence gathered through electronic surveillance. The court granted a request for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: As part of an investigation, an informant concealed a transmitter during his meetings with defendants. No warrant was obtained by the police prior to those meetings. A number of those recorded conversations were admitted into evidence at their trial. On appeal, the court found that the warrantless electronic surveillance of defendants violated their state constitutional rights. In the absence of a warrant, electronic surveillance was prohibited by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 99B4 and Mass. Gen. Laws Ch. 272, § 99 C1, unless it was performed by an officer who was a party, or who had the consent of a party, to the conversation. However, surveillance that was statutorily authorized could still be proscribed by the search and seizure provision of the state constitution, Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 14. Because there was a reasonable expectation of privacy in conversations that occurred in private homes, the court concluded that the invasion of that privacy pursuant to warrantless electronic surveillance was a violation of that constitutional provision. Moreover, the statute's "one party consent" provision failed to eliminate the need for a warrant under article 14.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order, which denied defendants' motions to suppress evidence, was set aside. The trial court was directed to enter an order granting those motions. The judgments of conviction were reversed and the verdicts set aside.

Tyree v. Keane


No. M-4176


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


400 Mass. 1; 507 N.E.2d 742; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1292


January 6, 1987, Argued  
May 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 29, 1982.

The case was tried before Mel L. Greenberg, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an action against defendant officers alleging that they violated his civil rights. The jury returned verdicts against one officer on the federal civil rights claim with nominal damages for the invasion of privacy and trespass claims; a verdict for the officer on the state civil rights and the conversion claims; and for the second officer on all claims. The case was transferred from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts).


OVERVIEW: The defendant alleged that the officers violated his civil rights when they searched his home without a warrant after the murder of his wife. The first officer argued that under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 38, §§ 6, 4.7, he was not in charge of the investigation and as a state police officer he did not have authority to obtain a warrant. It was not unreasonable for him to assume that his search under the authority of another officer was not a civil rights violation. The qualified immunity claim was only defeated if an officer knew that the action taken in his sphere of official responsibility would violate the constitutional rights of the defendant. The officer should have been allowed to present evidence on the statutory support. The court found that a search conducted without a warrant issued upon probable cause was per se unreasonable and that the prosecution bore the burden of proving that the search was justified. The judge properly excluded testimony of questioning as to the murder weapon and made no error in failing to suppress evidence seized during an unconstitutional search. The court found that the defendant failed to present any evidence of actual damages suffered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments as to the second officer and the judgments for nominal damages against the first officer on the invasion of privacy and trespass claims. The court concluded that as to the federal civil rights claims, the first officer was entitled to a new trial or, at his option, the entry of a judgment for the defendant in the amount of $ 1.

M.C. v. Commissioner of Correction


No. 4346


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 909; 507 N.E.2d 253; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1285


March 5, 1987, Argued  
May 13, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 31, 1983.

The case was heard by Robert A. Barton, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commissioner of corrections appealed an order of the Superior Court, Suffolk County (Massachusetts) that denied its motion for summary judgment in a civil action brought by plaintiff ex-prisoner for a declaration that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 127, §§ 83A, 83B, and 129C (1984 ed.) violated the Declaration of Rights of Mass. Const. art. 1, as amended by the Equal Rights Amendment, Mass. Const. Amend. art. 106.


OVERVIEW: When the ex-prisoner brought the action, she was serving two concurrent three-to-five-year prison sentences. She requested a transfer to the forestry prison camp, but her request was denied because the camp was an all-male facility. She argued that since there were no prison camps in Massachusetts for female prisoners, she had no opportunity to earn the two and one-half days of extra good time credits to which prison camp inmates were entitled under Mass. The court found that the dispute became theoretical when she was released because she was the only individual interested in the outcome, and the issue was not likely to recur because the women's prerelease center offered more program opportunities than the male prison camps.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order that denied summary judgment to the commissioner and remanded the case to the superior court to enter judgment for the commissioner in an action by the ex-prisoner for a declaration of rights under the Equal Rights Amendment.

Manning v. New England Mut. Life Ins. Co.


No. 4395


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 730; 506 N.E.2d 870; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1275


March 3, 1987, Argued  
April 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Land Court Department on January 17, 1986.

The case was heard by Marilyn M. Sullivan, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents sought review of a judgment of a land court judge denying specific enforcement of restrictions in deeds to a parcel of land owned by defendant insurance company. The appeal was transferred from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts).


OVERVIEW: The company purchased land in an area where residential lots were later sold by the Commonwealth with certain restrictions. The residents sought to enforce those restrictions against the company. The land court judge held that the restrictions were never brought forward as required by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 184, § 28 for restrictions of a certain age, and therefore could not be enforced against the company. The residents appealed and the court affirmed, holding that enforcement was barred by § 28 because notice of the restrictions was not re-recorded. The legislative history surrounding an amendment to § 28 did not establish that § 28 did not apply to restrictions in land sold by the Commonwealth. An amendment which may have supported the argument was deleted the year after its enactment. Section 28 did not violate the contract clause of the United States Constitution because it did not extinguish preexisting rights but only required that the beneficiary of restrictions record them. Section 28 was a reasonable method of achieving the Commonwealth's goals of preserving the marketability of real estate titles and ensuring they were not clouded by obsolete and uncertain restrictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the land court.

Dighton v. Federal Pacific Electric Co.


No. 4247


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 687; 506 N.E.2d 509; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1265; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,393


January 8, 1987, Argued  
April 21, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 18, 1983.

After the cases were consolidated for trial, motions to dismiss were heard by John J. Irwin, Jr., J., and questions of law were reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and third-party plaintiff circuit breaker manufacturer sought direct appellate review of a decision of the Superior Court (Massachusetts) denying defendant's motion to dismiss and granting third party defendant design firm's motion to dismiss. This appeal was consolidated with review of certified questions regarding the applicability of the statute of repose set forth in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 260, § 2B.


OVERVIEW: In a wrongful death action brought by plaintiff administrators, defendant circuit breaker manufacturer appealed the trial court's decision dismissing its third-party complaint against an architectural firm and its denial of defendant's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court granted direct review. The court affirmed the dismissal under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 260, § 2B. As to the questions of law reported by the lower court, the court held that § 2B, which placed a six-year limitation on tort actions for deficiency or neglect in the design, planning, construction or general administration of an improvement to real property, did not violate Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art.11 and was constitutional even if construed to exclude persons or firms such as architects. The court held that the statute was not intended to apply to mere suppliers of standardized products but only to entities who performed acts of individual expertise. The court held that defendant was a producer and seller of goods whose liability was governed by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 106, § 2-318, the Uniform Commercial Code, rather than under ch. 260, § 2B. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court answered the two questions reported by the superior court in the negative. The court also affirmed the lower court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss as well as its decision granting third-party defendant's motion to dismiss.

 

263 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Powers v. Wilkinson


No. 4099


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 650; 506 N.E.2d 842; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1261


October 8, 1986, Argued  
April 16, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Suffolk Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on July 12, 1985.

The case was heard by Mary C. Fitzpatrick, J., on a statement of agreed facts and was reported by her to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellant trustee's action for a declaratory judgment that a child born out of wedlock to the donor's granddaughter was issue for purposes of the trust, the Suffolk Division of the Probate and Family Court Department (Massachusetts) granted appellee beneficiaries' joint motion for reservation and report of the case to the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The trust instrument provided for payment to the donor's surviving children in equal shares for the duration of their lives and then to the children's issue by right of representation. The instrument itself contained no indication of the donor's intent to use the word "issue" so as to include or exclude nonmarital descendants. On appeal, the court held that, in the absence of anything indicating a contrary intent, precedent, at the time the trust instrument was executed, required the court to presume that the donor intended the term "issue" meant only persons of the class who were born in lawful wedlock and excluded nonmarital descendants. Although the court announced the rule that, absent clear expressions of a contrary intent, the term "issue" included all biological descendants, the court concluded that the ruling applied prospectively only because of concern for litigants and others who relied on existing precedents, particularly in the areas of property and contract law.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for entry of a declaration that, under the law applicable when the trust instrument was executed, the unexplained word "issue" was presumed to encompass only lawful lineal descendants of the donor.

Hull Municipal Lighting Plant v. Massachusetts Municipal Wholesale Electric Co.


No. Pl-4343


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 640; 506 N.E.2d 140; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1224


February 4, 1987, Argued  
April 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 23, 1986.

A motion for preliminary injunction was heard by Robert L. Steadman, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electric power plant (plant) brought an action against defendant wholesale electric supplier (wholesaler) arising from four agreements between the parties concerning the wholesaler's investment in nuclear power plants. The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) granted the wholesaler's motion for a preliminary injunction requiring the plant to continue making payments to the wholesaler pending arbitration. The plant sought review.


OVERVIEW: According to the agreements the parties executed to finance the nuclear power plant acquisitions, payments owed by the plant were due regardless of whether the projects were undertaken, completed, or became operational. In addition, each agreement required the plant to continue making payments during the pendency of arbitration proceedings. The court found that the plant's failure to make its payments would interfere with the wholesaler's ability to provide low cost, efficient service to its customers. While the court acknowledged that economic loss was generally insufficient on its own to warrant an injunction, it noted that recoverable monetary loss could constitute irreparable harm where the loss threatened the very existence of the party seeking the injunction. The court found if the plant were allowed to avoid payment by challenging the agreements, other municipal lighting companies might seek to avoid payment and further inhibit the wholesaler's ability to provide service, and that this type of economic loss threatened the wholesaler's business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

265 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


City of Boston v. Aetna Life Ins. Co.


No. 4174


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 569; 506 N.E.2d 106; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1219


December 1, 1986, Argued  
April 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on December 30, 1983.

Motions for partial summary judgment were heard by George N. Hurd, Jr., J., and questions of law were reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed the Superior Court's denial of its motion for partial summary judgment and the allowance of defendant insurers' motions for partial summary judgment in an action in which plaintiff sought to recover from defendants amounts that they were allegedly obliged to pay as benefits under their health insurance policies.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city sought to recover from defendant insurers amounts that they were allegedly obliged to pay as benefits under their health insurance policies. Plaintiff challenged the lower court's decision to allow defendants' motions for partial summary judgment. The court vacated the lower court's orders allowing defendants' motions for partial summary judgment on the standing issue because plaintiff met the requirement that it had to have engaged in the conduct of any trade or commerce. The court held that the lower court properly denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment on the rate setting issues insofar as it determined that nothing in the rate setting regulatory pattern required an insurer to pay a hospital charge not covered by the applicable insurance policy. The court concluded if an insurer promised to pay a hospital's charges without any limiting language, and the hospital was entitled to collect those charges from a charge paying patient, the insurer might have had an obligation to pay those lawful charges. The court also modified parts of defendants' motions for partial summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that plaintiff city had standing to assert its patients' claims against the defendant insurers. The court held that the lower court properly denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment on the rate setting issues insofar as it determined that nothing in the rate setting pattern required defendants to pay a hospital charge not covered by the applicable insurance policy.
