Leigh v. Board of Registration in Nursing


No. 4173


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 558; 506 N.E.2d 91; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1216


January 9, 1987, Argued  
April 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on February 23, 1984.

After review by this court, 395 Mass. 670 (1985), and remand for further proceedings before the Board of Registration in Nursing, the case was reported by Wilkins, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nurse appealed an order from defendant Board of Registration in Nursing (Massachusetts), which suspended the nurse's license as a registered nurse for practicing midwifery in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 80C (1984 ed.).


OVERVIEW: The board suspended the nurse's license to practice as a registered nurse when she engaged in midwifery without the certification required of nurse midwives under of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 80C (1984 ed.). The nurse appealed the suspension challenging, inter alia, the constitutionality of the statute. The court affirmed the suspension. The court held that neither the statute nor its implementing regulations deprived the nurse of her constitutional right to equal protection of the laws because the distinction drawn between lay and nurse midwives was justified on the ground that the public expected a nurse to have undergone a higher level of training than a law midwife. The court determined that the statute did not violate pregnant women's due process rights because by the statute did not interfere with a fundamental right in requiring nurses who practiced in the expanded role of midwife to be licensed and to practice in a licensed facility as part of a health care team. The court also found that the regulatory scheme rationally furthered the state's legitimate purpose of setting minimum standards for nurses on which the public could rely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's suspension of the nurse's license for practicing midwifery without the requisite certification under relevant state statute.

 

267 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Board of Selectmen v. County Comm'rs of Norfolk


No. N-4226


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 507; 505 N.E.2d 182; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1210


December 5, 1986, Argued  
March 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 15, 1984.

The case was heard by Katherine Liacos Izzo, J., on a statement of agreed facts.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Board of Selectmen (board) sought review of an order from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which denied the board an injunction to keep defendant commissioners from using a building which was part of a hospital as a correctional facility.


OVERVIEW: The commissioners wanted to use the land at issue as a correctional facility because of overcrowding at other facilities. The court reversed the decision and remanded case for entry of judgment enjoining the use of the nurses' quarters as a correctional facility, effective at such reasonable time after rescript as would permit the orderly transfer of the prisoners to other facilities. While the use of the hospital as a chronic disease hospital might have been consistent with the original use as a tuberculosis hospital, use as a correctional facility was not. The fact that the hospital would continue to operate was not controlling. The use was entirely different and could not be accomplished without legislative authority. The commissioners could not take part of the land used as a hospital for use as a correctional facility, absent specific legislative authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court denying an injunction to the board in a case challenging a decision by the commissioners to use the use of nurses' quarters as a correctional facility was reversed and remanded.

 

268 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Blinn


No. 4175


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 126; 503 N.E.2d 25; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1115


November 5, 1986, Argued  
January 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Salem Division of the District Court Department on September 27, 1984.

In the jury session of that division, the case was tried before Joseph A. Furnari, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Salem Division of the District Court (Massachusetts), which found him guilty of refusing to produce a motel register when requested to do so by a state trooper. Defendant argued that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 27 (1984) violated the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 14. Defendant's petition for direct appellate review was allowed.


OVERVIEW: A state trooper had went to a motel and requested that defendant, the manager of the motel, produce the motel's guest register for inspection. Defendant refused to allow the trooper to see the register without a search warrant. The trooper returned with a copy of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 27 (1984) and demanded again to see the register. Defendant again refused. Defendant eventually produced the register. In affirming the decision, the court found that defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the motel's guest register. The guests of the motel had no legitimate expectation that their names in the register could be withheld from the police. Further, when the trooper was seeking the register to ascertain whether a criminal suspect was registered at the hotel, defendant's expectation of privacy in the register was significantly diminished, if it existed at all. Defendant had no legitimate expectation of privacy in the motel register.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

269 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Redgrave v. Boston Symphony Orchestra, Inc.


No. 4089


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


399 Mass. 93; 502 N.E.2d 1375; 1987 Mass. LEXIS 1112


May 7, 1986, Argued  
January 21, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Questions of law certified to the Supreme Judicial Court by the United States Court of Appeals for the First Circuit.



DISPOSITION: We answer, "Yes" to the first certified question, and "No" to the second certified question.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the First Circuit certified two questions of law pertaining to the interpretation of the Massachusetts Civil Rights Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 12, §§ 11H and 11I (1984), to the state court.


OVERVIEW: The first question asked whether actions taken in the face of pressure from third parties violated Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 12, §§ 11H and 11I (1984). The second question asked whether it was a defense to liability for acquiescence to third-party pressure for the defendant to show that its actions were independently motivated by additional concerns, such as fear of business disruption, fear for economic loss, or fear for physical safety. The supreme court determined that §§ 11H and 11I contained no state of mind prerequisite for recovery. Sections 11H and 11I did not require that the defendant's actions have been wilful. Also, fear of business disruption, fear for economic loss, or fear for physical safety were not justifications under §§ 11H and 11I.


OUTCOME: The supreme court answered "yes" to the first certified question and "no" to the second certified question posed.

 

270 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Nashawena Trust v. Board of Assessors


No. S-4138


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 821; 501 N.E.2d 506; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1577


October 9, 1986, Argued  
December 17, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of assessors (assessors) challenged a decision of the Appellate Tax Board (board) (Massachusetts), which held that certain lands owned by appellee trust were agricultural or contiguous thereto and were correctly classified as such for tax purposes under Mass. Gen. Laws. Ch. 61A. The trust had petitioned the board after the assessors denied its application to classify parts of its land as agricultural or contiguous.


OVERVIEW: The land in question was part of an island. The trust, which owned the island, maintained a small farming operation there. In its appeal of the board's decision, the assessors argued that they properly denied the trust's applications because Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 61A, § 4 exceeded the authorization of the Commonwealth's constitution. The assessors also argued that the amount of land involved in agricultural use was greater than that claimed by the trust and that they properly denied the applications under the minimum revenue requirements of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 61A, § 3. The court affirmed the board's decision, holding first that it did not have to address the assessors' constitutional argument because the assessors lacked standing to raise such a claim. The court also held that the board's decision was supported by substantial evidence. Even though illegal slaughtering activities occurred on the island, the revenues derived from these activities were gross sales under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 61A, §§ 1 and 3, and the court agreed with the board that the trust was engaged in a regular business and that sales to individuals were sales in the regular course of business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the board, which held that certain lands owned by the trust were agricultural or contiguous thereto and were correctly classified as such for tax purposes.

 

271 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Hallett v. Wrentham


No. N-4102


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 550; 499 N.E.2d 1189; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1512


September 11, 1986, Argued  
November 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 20, 1980.

The case was tried before George N. Hurd, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff widow's wrongful death action against defendant town, the Norfolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) reduced the judgment for the widow based on the $ 100,000 cap in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258, § 2, but allowed plaintiff children's awards for loss of parental society to stand. The widow, the children, and the town appealed.


OVERVIEW: The widow's husband was killed when his car collided with a truck driven by the town's employee. In a wrongful death action, the widow and the children separately sought damages. The damages awarded to the widow for loss of income and consortium were decreased to the cap provided by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258, § 2. The damages awarded to the children were allowed. The court held that the statutory damage cap applied to all claims under the wrongful death statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 229, § 2, and had to be applied to the sum of all recoveries. The wrongful death statute provided for a single action in which the claims of all beneficiaries were made; only one plaintiff could assert damage claims. As the cap was rationally related to the legitimate state purpose of protecting public funds from unlimited liability, it did not violate equal protection. The town was not entitled to a new trial as the trial court was not required to instruct the jury that emergency conditions were factors to consider in determining the reasonableness of the action taken. Further, the trial court did not err in excluding expert testimony because evaluation of the facts did not call for particular expertise.


OUTCOME: The damage awards for the widow and the children were reversed and the case was remanded for entry of a single judgment for the widow in the amount of the statutory damage cap, in satisfaction of all claims. The children's independent claims were dismissed.

Department of Youth Services v. A Juvenile


No. 4053


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 516; 499 N.E.2d 812; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1508


May 6, 1986, Argued  
November 4, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth.

Application for review of an order to extend commitment, filed in the Brockton Division of the District Court Department on October 5, 1984.

On appeal to the jury session of that division, the case was tried before Robert A. Welsh, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: The judgment extending the commitment order is vacated, and the case remanded to the jury of six for a new trial. So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a judgment from the Brockton Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which entered a judgment extending the juvenile's commitment order to a secure facility run by appellee Department of Youth Services. A jury had determined that the juvenile would be physically dangerous to the public because of his mental disorder or abnormality under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 120 §§ 16-20 (1984).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile alleged that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 120 §§ 16-20 (1984) were unconstitutional, that it was error for a psychiatrist to testify when the juvenile was not warned that his statements could be used against him, that it was error to admit a doctor's opinion based on hearsay, that the judge erred in quashing a summons, and that it was error to deny a motion to appoint an expert psychiatrist to assist in the defense. The court found (1) the constitutional challenges failed because the state validly exercised its police power to confine persons who were adjudicated mentally ill and dangerous, and the juvenile was found to be mentally ill and dangerous; (2) the juvenile should have been provided warnings that his conversations with the doctor could be used against him, which created a substantial risk of a miscarriage of justice; (3) an expert could base an opinion on facts not in evidence if the facts were independently admissible and a permissible basis to consider in formulating an opinion; (4) the lower court did not err in quashing a summons; and (5) there was no evidence that a fee established by the lower court in providing an expert for the defense was inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's judgment, which had extended the juvenile's commitment order, and remanded the case for a new jury trial because the juvenile was not provided warnings that his conversations with the doctor were not confidential and could be used against him.

Planned Parenthood Fedn. of Am. v. Problem Pregnancy of Worcester


No. M-4071


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 480; 498 N.E.2d 1044; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1504; 1 U.S.P.Q.2D (BNA) 1465


April 9, 1986, Argued  
October 16, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 24, 1984.

The case was heard by Elbert Tuttle, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant organization sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted a permanent injunction, attorney fees, and costs to plaintiff abortion clinic in its action for service mark infringement and unfair and deceptive acts.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff abortion clinic filed an action against defendant organization that arose from a dispute over defendant's use of the initials "PP" on the front door to its office. The trial court issued a permanent injunction against defendant and awarded attorney fees and costs to plaintiff. On appeal, the court reversed the award of attorney fees and costs and affirmed the remainder of the judgment against defendant. The court held that the trial court did not err in granting the injunction because defendant's use of the initials constituted a common law service mark infringement. The trial court's finding of secondary meaning was not erroneous because the initials were strongly associated with plaintiff's organization. The court held that the award of attorney fees and costs on the plaintiff's claim for unfair and deceptive business practices was improper because the evidence did not warrant a finding that defendant was engaged in trade or commerce. The court found that defendant was not protected by U.S. Const. amend. I because there were numerous ways in which it could advertise and attract clients without infringing on plaintiffs' service mark.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of attorney fees and costs to plaintiff abortion clinic because the evidence did not warrant a finding that defendant was engaged in trade or commerce. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment against defendant organization for alternatives to abortion. The trial court did not err in granting the injunction because defendant's use of certain initials constituted a common law service mark infringement.

Miga v. Holyoke


No. Hd-4114


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 343; 497 N.E.2d 1; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1494


May 5, 1986, Argued  
September 2, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on December 31, 1981.

The case was heard by Elizabeth A. Porada, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, police officers and city, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which awarded damages to plaintiff decedent's mother in plaintiff's wrongful death and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action that was brought after decedent committed suicide while in defendants' protective custody.


OVERVIEW: After police picked up decedent, who was drunk, decedent became unconscious, and the police made no attempt to obtain medical attention. Instead, decedent was taken into protective custody where, contrary to the rules, no attempt was made to contact a treatment center and decedent, who had known suicidal tendencies, was put in a cell. While in the cell, decedent committed suicide, and consequently, plaintiff decedent's mother brought a wrongful death and a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against defendants, police officers and city. When plaintiff was awarded damages, review was sought, and the court affirmed. In applying U.S. Const. amend. VIII to determine the protections decedent, as a pretrial detainee, had under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, the court held decedent's substantive due process rights had been violated because defendants had acted with deliberate indifference to decedent's medical needs. The court also held the availability of a state remedy for the wrongful death had not precluded the § 1983 action because the federal remedy was supplementary to the state remedy and the availability of a post-deprivation remedy was irrelevant to the substantive due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment awarding damages to plaintiff decedent's mother in plaintiff's wrongful death and civil rights action brought after decedent committed suicide while in the protective custody of defendants, police officers and city, because defendants' deliberate indifference to decedent's medical needs violated decedent's substantive due process rights and the civil rights action was not foreclosed by the wrongful death remedy.

Commonwealth v. Helfant


No. M-4056


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 214; 496 N.E.2d 433; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1453


April 7, 1986, Argued  
August 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on October 1, 1983.

The cases were tried before Elizabeth J. Dolan, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which convicted defendant of rape and of drugging a person for unlawful sexual intercourse. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the appeals court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in (1) denying his motions for the required findings of not guilty, (2) prohibiting defense counsel from rehabilitating defendant on a critical portion of testimony, (3) allowing testimony of prior misconduct, (4) and denying motions to sever the indictments. The trial court properly concluded that prejudice, if any, to defendant did not outweigh the interests of the trial court, the Commonwealth, and the public in a shortened adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of rape and of drugging a person for unlawful sexual intercourse.

278 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Jaffe


No. M-4115


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 50; 494 N.E.2d 1342; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1406


April 8, 1986, Argued  
July 15, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Complaints received and sworn to in the Newton Division of the District Court Department on January 16, 1985.

The cases were heard by Arthur Sherman, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landlords appealed an order of the District Court of Middlesex County (Massachusetts), which convicted them of violating a city zoning ordinance, Newton, Ma., Rev. Ord. § 30-5(a) (1984), by arranging and using their eight-bedroom house as a dwelling for more than one family. The court transferred the case to this court on its own motion.


OVERVIEW: The house contained two kitchens and was rented to eight unrelated adults. There were several mailboxes, few interior locks, and each tenant had a key. The lease provided that any one tenancy could be terminated without affecting the other tenancies. The trial court found a lack of communal living in violation of the ordinance. On appeal, the landlords contended that § 30-5(a) was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to define "family" and that it violated Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 10. They urged the court to adopt the notion of a "single housekeeping unit" rather than that of a "biologically related family." The court affirmed. Section 30-5(a) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the landlords. The use of a house by eight unrelated adults with no communal living and who could be independently evicted was not a "family." Similarly, because the first and second floors of the house each contained a kitchen, bathroom, bedrooms, and a common room, the house was not a one-family dwelling under Mass. Regs. Code tit. 780 § 201.3, at 53 (1980). Moreover, the living arrangement had no cohesiveness as implied by the term "single housekeeping unit."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's conviction of the landlord for violating the zoning ordinance.

Massachusetts Taxpayers Foundation, Inc. v. Secretary of Admin.


No. S-4215


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


398 Mass. 40; 494 N.E.2d 1311; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1394


June 10, 1986, Argued  
July 10, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on April 16, 1986.

A question of law was reported by Liacos, J.

The case was submitted on briefs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) reported to the court for a decision, in the taxpayers' declaratory judgment action against the secretary and the commissioner, whether the provision of the Massachusetts personal income tax that established a graduated system of exemptions violated the proportionality requirement or the uniformity requirement of the state constitution.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed a declaratory judgment action against the secretary and the commissioner to determine that the provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 593, § 6 (1985), violated the proportionality requirement of Mass. Const. art. IV, § 1, ch. 1, pt. II, and the uniformity requirement of Mass. Const. amend. art. 44. The trial court reported the question for a decision on the constitutional questions. The court held that: (1) the statute contained graduated personal income tax exemptions that were contingent upon the amount of the taxpayer's gross income, marital status, and filing status; (2) the statute was intended to tax the same class of income at different rates rather than to provide reasonable exemptions from the tax so that the tax burdens would rest as nearly equally as possible among those able to bear them; (3) although art. 44 authorized an income tax subject to reasonable exemptions, such a tax had to be levied at a uniform rate throughout the Commonwealth upon incomes derived from the same class of property; and (4) the court's prior advisory opinions were not binding authorities, but were open to reconsideration and revision.


OUTCOME: The court held that the provision of the personal income tax that contained graduated personal exemptions contingent on gross income, marital status, and filing status, was unconstitutional.

Commonwealth v. Barry


No. S-4017


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 718; 493 N.E.2d 853; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1340


February 3, 1986, Argued  
June 12, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 7, 1981.

The cases were tried before James J. Nixon, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) for three counts of armed robbery. Defendant had also been charged with murder in the first degree but was found not guilty on that count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove two other men to a restaurant and then waited in an alley while they robbed employees of the restaurant and shot one of them. Defendant and the two other men attempted to leave in the van, but it crashed into a parked automobile when they tried to start it. The court affirmed defendant's conviction on appeal, holding that: (1) the trial court did not err in refusing defendant's request for a required finding of not guilty because the evidence was sufficient for the jury to find that he knowingly assisted in the perpetration of the armed robbery; (2) the exception in Mass. Super. Ct. R. 6 (1974) for trials on indictments for crimes punishable by death applied to trials for murder in the first degree, so the trial court did not err by requiring defendant to exercise his peremptory challenges before all the jurors had been declared indifferent; and (3) the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury that if they acquitted defendant on the murder indictment, they had to also acquit him on the armed robbery charges, because to do so would have taken from the jury the factual finding of whether the homicide occurred in the course of the robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for three counts of armed robbery.

 

281 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices to Senate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 1201; 493 N.E.2d 859; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1346



June 12, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Senate of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts requested an advisory opinion concerning a bill pending in the Senate regulating the management of low-level radioactive waste. The Senate asked the court to determine the constitutionality of the proposed legislation, Senate No. 1763, § 29.


OVERVIEW: The court found that § 29 sought to implement legislation, which would have required legislative certification and voter approval of the construction and operation of a proposed low-level radioactive waste facility. The court determined that under § 29, one branch of the legislature, by failing to certify its approval, could potentially block the construction and operation of a licensed facility already found by the executive branch to warrant a license. The court ruled that such a one-house veto provision was not within the legislative power. The court answered the Senate's question as to the encroachment of the legislative certification requirement upon the powers of the executive in the affirmative. The court further determined that § 29 did not ask the voters to consider a law enacted by the legislature but instead would have asked the voters whether the commonwealth was authorized to permit the construction and operation of a particular low-level waste facility. The court concluded that the voter approval requirement did not conform to the voter approval requirements under the state constitution, therefore, the voter approval process under § 29 was not permissible.


OUTCOME: The court answered the Senate's questions as to whether the bill's voter approval requirement and legislative certification process were unconstitutional in the affirmative. The court opined that the proposed bill did not conform to the state constitution.

 

282 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Chappee


No. M-4029


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 508; 492 N.E.2d 719; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1296


February 4, 1986, Argued  
May 12, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on August 3, 1983.

A motion to suppress evidence was heard by John J. Irwin, Jr., J., and the cases were heard by Alan J. Dimond, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment on Indictment 83-1827 (trafficking) affirmed. Indictment 83-1828 (possession with intent to distribute) remanded to the Superior Court for the entry of an order of dismissal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action initiated by the Plaintiff commonwealth, defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), that convicted and sentenced him for trafficking in cocaine, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E (b)(2) (1984), and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A (a) (1984).


OVERVIEW: An affidavit stated that a trooper saw trash bags being placed in front of defendant's driveway on land owned by the town. It also stated that the trooper took the bags without a warrant and found a letter to defendant, bags with a white powder residue, and drug paraphernalia. The powdery substance later tested as cocaine. The trooper testified that when he searched defendant's home with the warrant obtained with the affidavit, he found a substance used to "cut" cocaine and newspaper packaging consistent with the packing of cocaine. The lower court convicted defendant for violating Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E (b)(2) and § 32A (a). The court affirmed the conviction for trafficking. The placement of the bags showed that defendant had no expectation of privacy as to them. The test results and testimony as to what was found in defendant's home were sufficient to show that the powder was cocaine. The sanction on defendant's counsel for bringing experts, whom the judge had disallowed as undisclosed, into to the courtroom was proper because the commonwealth was unprepared for their sophisticated scientific testimony. The possession conviction was remanded to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for trafficking in cocaine. The court remanded for dismissal the indictment for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute.

Lyons v. Labor Relations Com.


No. S-3927


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 498; 492 N.E.2d 343; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1295


January 9, 1986, Argued  
May 8, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Labor Relations Commission.

A motion to require the Labor Relations Commission to assemble the record for purposes of appeal was heard in the Appeals Court by Frederick L. Brown, J.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee, who was a teacher in a public school, and defendant Labor Relations Commission filed cross-appeals from a decision of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts) that affirmed the commission's dismissal of the employee's complaint objecting to the amount of an agency fee assessed against him by intervenor union as a nonunion employee within the collective bargaining unit represented by the union.


OVERVIEW: The commission dismissed the employee's complaint without a hearing because he did not file it within 45 days as required by Mass. Regs. Code tit. 402 § 17.06(2). The employee alleged that the 45-day limitation period was unconstitutional. The appeals court granted the employee's motion to direct the commission to assemble a record on appeal but affirmed the dismissal. The court held § 17.06(2) unconstitutional and remanded the case to the commission for hearing. The employee's complaint was grounded in his First Amendment right to prevent the union from using part of his required fee to support or express political views unrelated to its duties as bargaining representative. The dismissal of his complaint effectively determined the outcome of his constitutionally based challenge and was therefore a final order subject to judicial review. The 45-day limitations period for challenges to agency fees violated the employee's equal protection rights because other prohibited practice complaints were subject to 6-month limitation periods, thus impairing the exercise of a fundamental right. The shorter limitation period was not necessary to promote a compelling state interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court's decision affirming the commission's dismissal of the employee's complaint objecting to the amount of the agency fee assessed against him, held the regulation challenged unconstitutional, and remanded the case to the commission to consider the employee's complaint on the merits.

Nationwide Mut. Ins. Co. v. Commissioner of Ins.


No. S-3912


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 416; 491 N.E.2d 1061; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1281


January 10, 1986, Argued  
April 28, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on April 2, 1981.

On transfer to the Superior Court Department the case was heard by George W. Cashman, J., sitting under statutory authority.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, insurance commissioner and agents, sought review of an order from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which held that new rates established in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 175, § 162D did not apply to appellee insurance company and its agents.


OVERVIEW: The motion judge ordered entry of a judgment which provided that the 1980 rates established by the commissioner did not apply to the insurance company and that 1981 rates established did not apply to until a hearing has been held by the commissioner regarding the expense base. On appeal, the court held that the 1980 amendment applying the commissioner's rate to "any other system" had to be considered an extension, rather than a clarification, of the original statute. The insurance company therefore was not subject to the 1979 statute and the 1980 commission rates promulgated thereunder. The insurance company clearly fell within the language of a July, 1980, amendment, and was subject to the commission rates promulgated by the commissioner after that date.The words used by the legislature evidenced an intent to make the 1980 amendment to § 162D, retroactive. Therefore, the statute and the commissioner's 1981 rate decision promulgated thereunder applied to the insurance company, despite the outstanding contract between the company and its agents.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court for the insurance company was proper in a suit involving appellants.

 

285 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth Electric Co. v. Department of Public Utilities


No. S-3913


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 361; 491 N.E.2d 1035; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1280


October 10, 1985, Argued  
April 22, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on October 8, 1982.

The case was reported by Lynch, J.



DISPOSITION: Therefore, the relief sought by Commonwealth Electric Company is denied, and a judgment is to enter in the county court affirming the orders of the DPU. So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff power company appealed an order from the Department of Public Utilities (Massachusetts), which imputed the imprudence of an operator of a nuclear power station, which was out of service for several months, to them and required them to refund, with interest, the portion of costs previously allowed to the ratepayers.


OVERVIEW: When the station was being built, the company had contracted to purchase 11 percent of its capacity. After the operator shut the station down, the company had to buy power elsewhere at a greater cost. The DPU authorized a quarterly fuel adjustment charge subject to refund, with interest, pending the outcome of proceedings. The court accepted the argument of the DPU that while the company did not have an ownership share in the station, its life-of-the-unit contract was in all relevant respects the same as partial ownership. The court determined that in return for its shelter from the uncertainties of the competitive market place, a public utility assumes the responsibility to provide adequate service at reasonable rates. This duty was imposed by statute and, though its performance may be delegated, the duty may not. The DPU had authority under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 164, § 94G(a)(1984) to impute the imprudence of the operator to the company. The court concluded that the DPU did not act beyond its statutory authority, and federal law limited the federal role to regulation of sales of electricity at wholesale, and left regulation of sales at retail to the states.


OUTCOME: The court entered a judgment affirming the orders of the DPU.

G.J.T., Inc. v. Boston Licensing Bd.


No. S-3849


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 285; 491 N.E.2d 594; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1270


December 3, 1985, Argued  
April 14, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 5, 1982, June 16, 1982, and April 6, 1983, respectively.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on July 2, 1982.

The four cases were heard together in the Superior Court Department by George N. Hurd, Jr., J., and questions of law were reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted requests for direct review.



DISPOSITION: The order and supplemental order of the Superior Court are vacated. The cases are remanded to the Superior Court for entry of judgment declaring the rights of the parties in a manner consistent with this opinion. So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a licensing division of the mayor's office and a licensing board, filed applications for direct appellate review of a decision by the trial court (Massachusetts), which granted the board's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff licensee's motion for declaratory judgment to determine which party had authority to grant public entertainment licenses.


OVERVIEW: The licensee sought a permit for the use of video game machines. The licensee filed an action for declaratory judgment to determine whether the division or the board had the authority to grant the license. The court then granted the board's and division's applications for direct appellate review. On appeal the court vacated the trial court's order. The court held that legislature delegated the overall authority for the licensing of entertainment to the mayor, with authority over a few specifically designated types of entertainment resting with the board. The court stated that the term licensing authorities as used in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 1 referred to those authorities generally charged with amusement licensing and not those charged with licensing a narrow and specific class of entertainment. The court found that the division's authority to regulate the licensing of general entertainment stemmed from the city's charter, and was not in sharp conflict with subsequent statutory provisions. The court held that absent a clear legislative intent to the contrary the provisions of the charter generally prevailed over conflicting provisions of the subsequently enacted general law.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the board. The court remanded the case to the trial court for entry of judgment declaring the rights of the parties in a manner consistent with the court's opinion.

 

287 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Pope


No. E-3910


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 275; 491 N.E.2d 240; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1275


December 4, 1985, Argued  
April 11, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 24, 1982.

The cases were tried before Francis W. Keating, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted him under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 274, § 2 as an accessory before the fact to his girlfriend's murder in the first degree of her former boyfriend and for unlawfully carrying a firearm. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in allowing his girlfriend's suicide note to be admitted in evidence as a statement against penal interest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant acquired a gun and gave it to his girlfriend. Testimony indicated that defendant showed the gun to his co-worker and told him that it was for his girlfriend to use to shoot her former boyfriend. Defendant's girlfriend and her former boyfriend were later found in an apparent murder-suicide. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawfully carrying a firearm. However, the court reversed his conviction as an accessory before the fact to murder in the first degree. The court found that the trial court erred in admitting the girlfriend's suicide note under the exception to the hearsay rule for admissions against penal interest and that the admission was prejudicial. The court determined that the suicide note was not an admission against penal interest because a person who was about to commit suicide faced no penal consequences for any statements made before death. The prosecution had to show that defendant's girlfriend killed her former boyfriend with deliberately premeditated malice aforethought. The suicide note was a particularly persuasive element of the case against defendant because it suggested the requisite premeditation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of unlawfully carrying a firearm. The court reversed defendant's conviction as accessory before the fact to murder in the first degree and remanded for a new trial.

Commonwealth v. Two Juveniles


No. S-3968


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


397 Mass. 261; 491 N.E.2d 234; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1229


December 3, 1985, Argued  
April 10, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Dorchester Division of the District Court Department on December 24, 1984.

On appeal to the appeals session of the Boston Division of the Juvenile Court Department, questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by Paul D. Lewis, J. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: First question, affirmative, second question cannot be answered in the abstract.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appeals session of the Boston Juvenile Court (Massachusetts) submitted two certified questions on the issues of whether the absolute prohibition of Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 233, § 20J, against disclosure by a sexual assault counsellor of confidential communications received from a victim of sexual assault prevented in camera inspection of such reports, and if so, if it violated the confrontation clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Two juveniles were charged with the aggravated rape of an 18 year old woman, who sought medical assistance and counseling after the incident through the emergency unit of a local hospital. The juveniles filed motions for in camera inspection of communications protected from disclosure by Mass. Gen. Laws. Ch. 233, § 20J. The trial court denied the motions, and the juveniles appealed. The appeals court submitted two certified questions to the higher court, on whether § 20J prevented a court from permitting an in camera inspection of communications between a sexual assault counselor and an alleged victim of a sexual assault, and if so, if it violated the confrontation clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The reviewing court held that that in certain circumstances the absolute privilege expressed in § 20J must yield at trial to the constitutional right of a criminal defendant to have access to privileged communications. The court ruled that before any in camera inspection of the privileged material can be justified, the defendant must show a legitimate need for access to the communications. It is insufficient to request such information merely for an attack on credibility.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court answered that if a defendant can demonstrate that the protected information is likely to be useful to his defense, the judge should review the communications in camera. The court declined to answer the constitutional question because it presented a question of constitutional law that could not be answered in the abstract.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner health insurance company sought review of a decision of respondent Commissioner of Insurance (commissioner) (Massachusetts) disapproving filings proposing an increase in nongroup rates. The insurance company contended that the commissioner's decision contained several errors of law and was based upon findings that were unsupported by substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: The health insurance company filed proposed rates for nongroup subscribers. The commissioner disapproved the proposed increase in nongroup rates. The court transferred the case to its docket on its own motion.


OVERVIEW: The husband filed a complaint requesting an annulment of the parties' marriage on the ground that, contrary to the representations that the wife made to him at the time of their marriage, the wife had previously been married and her previous marriage had never been dissolved. Cepulonis v. Registrars of Voters


N No. 3879


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 808; 488 N.E.2d 1166; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1175


December 6, 1985, Argued  
February 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 11, 1982.

Following the decision of this court in 389 Mass. 930 (1983), a motion for attorney's fees was heard by Richard S. Kelley, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant registrars appealed a judgment of the Superior Court (Massachusetts) awarding plaintiff inmates attorney fees and costs under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 after the inmates had prevailed in their action challenging voter registration practices.


OVERVIEW: The registrars contended on appeal that the record did not establish that any inmate was a domiciliary of the registrars' city, that the inmates' claim had been decided on state constitutional grounds, and that "special circumstances" warranted the denial of attorney fees in the case. The court affirmed the judgment. The court stated that at most, a colorable claim of domicile was needed to justify joinder of the registrars as defendants, and it pointed out that the statement of agreed facts showed sufficient circumstances to raise the question whether one inmate was a resident of the registrars' city at the time he sought to register. The court concluded that the inmates' federal constitutional claim was sufficient to bring their action within 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and thus to justify an award of fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The court stated that adherence to statutory requirements did not relieve the registrars from liability for attorney fees under § 1988.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court awarding attorney fees to the inmates in their action against the registrars claiming constitutional violations in the registrars' voter registration practices.

Commonwealth v. Neiman


No. M-3894


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 754; 488 N.E.2d 772; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1178


November 5, 1985, Argued  
February 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on February 17, 1983.

A motion to dismiss was heard by Robert A. Mulligan, J., and the case was tried before Elbert Tuttle, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Middlesex Superior Court (Massachusetts) denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment that charged him with possession of cocaine with intent to distribute in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(a), as appearing in 1980 Mass. Acts ch. 436, § 4, as amended by 1981 Mass. Acts ch. 522. Defendant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: A grand jury returned four indictments against defendant charging him with cocaine "trafficking," possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, assault and battery on a police officer, and possession of marihuana. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the two indictments involving cocaine on the grounds that the penalty provisions in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32A(a) and § 32E(b)(1) were facially inconsistent and unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous. The trial court granted the motion as to the trafficking indictment and denied the motion as to the indictment involving possession with intent to distribute. A jury acquitted defendant on the assault and battery and possession of marihuana charges and convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. The court affirmed. The legislature had not intended the unlettered paragraph of § 32A to apply to § 32A in its entirety. The court construed the unlettered paragraph, which allowed for probation, to apply to § 32A(c) alone. Thus, there was no inconsistency amongst the provisions of § 32A. An intention to enact a barren and ineffective provision was not lightly to be imputed to the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the denial of defendant's motion dismiss.

295 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Acen


Nos. S-3909, S-3914


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 472; 487 N.E.2d 189; 1986 Mass. LEXIS 1122


October 8, 1985, Argued  
January 6, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 14, 1984.

A motion to dismiss was heard by James P. Donohue, J., and the cases were tried before him.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on April 6, 1984.

A motion to dismiss was heard by Andrew G. Meyer, J., and the case was tried before him.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which convicted him of distributing cocaine, was consolidated with the appeal by another defendant from a judgment of the same court, which convicted him of robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged convictions claiming that the requirements of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 234A, § 4 (1984) that jurors speak English and that a jury consist entirely of citizens of the United States violated the state and federal constitutions, and that the notice to jurors deprived defendants of a fair trial. The court affirmed the convictions. The right to trial by jury de medietate linquae anciently allowed in England for the trial of an alien was not a right of constitutional magnitude under the state constitution. Even if originally part of the state common law, the legislature had a right to abrogate it by the challenged statute. Individuals who cannot speak English and noncitizens were not discrete groups within the community entitled to protection from discrimination under Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. XI. Groups based solely on language or citizenship were not groups protected by U.S. Const. amend. VI that a state could not rationally exclude from jury duty. By grouping language and citizenship disqualifications together with disqualification based on prior criminality or insanity, the notice given to potential jurors did not deprive defendants of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgments convicting one defendant of distributing cocaine, and the other of robbery, were affirmed.

Southview Co-operative Housing Corp. v. Rent Control Bd.


No. M-3825


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 395; 486 N.E.2d 700; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1792


May 8, 1985, Argued  
December 17, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Cambridge Division of the District Court Department on June 4, 1982.

On appeal to the Superior Court Department the case was heard by Edward M. Ginsburg, J., sitting under statutory authority.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Rent Control Board of Cambridge (board) appealed from the decision of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which held that certain charges were not authorized. Plaintiffs, owners of real property, sought a declaration that charges assessed against them by the board in connection with petitions for individual rent adjustments were unlawful, and that the owners were entitled to reimbursement of the sums paid.


OVERVIEW: The owners argued that 1976 Mass. Acts 36 (Act) did not manifest a legislative intent to grant the board authority to establish filing fees for individual rent adjustment petitions commensurate with the cost to the board occasioned by the petitions. The owners also argued that the charges imposed pursuant to a fee schedule were unrelated to the cost of services occasioned by the petitions, and thus the charges constituted unlawful taxes. The board argued that the Act authorized them to impose filing fees, or fees commensurate with the cost of the services occasioned by the filing, and that the regulation operated to impose only fees, not taxes. The court held that the board was vested with broad authority to effectuate the purposes of the Act, and thus the validity of a regulation promulgated thereunder was to be sustained if it reasonably related to the purposes of the enabling legislation. The court held that it could not have been reasonably contended that the regulation did not promote the purposes of the Act. The court held that the board was authorized to charge fees in connection with the services it performed, and that the charges were fees and not taxes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court and held that the board was authorized to charge fees in connection with the services it performed, and that the charges were fees and not taxes. The court held that the filing fees were lawful.

Chicopee Lions Club v. District Attorney for Hampden Dist.


No. Hd-3759


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 244; 485 N.E.2d 673; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1737


September 12, 1985, Argued  
November 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 17, 1983.

A motion to dismiss was heard by George J. Hayer, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff club appealed the decision of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which granted the motion to dismiss of defendants, district attorney, county, and commonwealth, in the club's civil rights action against defendants pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 12, § 11I (1984).


OVERVIEW: The club filed a civil rights action against defendants, which charged the district attorney with negligent interference with contractual relations and defamation. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss, which the trial court granted. The court affirmed, concluding that the district attorney's activities of threatening to send in state troopers and raid the club's fundraiser were quasi judicial and absolutely immune from suit. The court concluded that the district attorney evaluated the information presented to him regarding the club's fundraiser and reached the conclusion that the fundraiser would be in contravention of the law. The court concluded that it was within his duties as an advocate and officer of the court to render such an opinion however erroneous or ill-informed it may have been. The court concluded that the district attorney's threat constituted a warning that he intended to gather evidence and initiate prosecutions if the event took place as scheduled. The court concluded that this type of discretionary decision regarding whether and when to initiate and maintain a prosecution was protected by immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the club's civil right's action against defendants.

 

298 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Metros v. Secretary of Commonwealth


No. M-3921


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 156; 484 N.E.2d 1015; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1786


September 12, 1985, Argued  
November 6, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 16, 1984.

The case was heard by George W. Cashman, J., sitting under statutory authority.

The Supreme Judicial Court, on its own initiative, transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, voter and candidate, challenged an order from the Superior Court, Middlesex County (Massachusetts), which dismissed their action against the Secretary of the Commonwealth that sought injunctive and declaratory relief requiring the candidate's name to be placed on a ballot. Plaintiffs also challenged an order from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which denied their request for a stay of judgment and injunctive relief pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 53, § 48 (1984), which prohibited a person who was a member of a political party within the preceding 90 days from being listed on the ballot as an unenrolled candidate for election. The trial court dismissed the action. On appeal, the appellate court denied plaintiffs' motion for a stay and injunctive relief pending appeal. Plaintiffs challenged both decisions. The court transferred the case on its own initiative and consolidated the appeals. The court vacated the dismissal of plaintiffs' action and held that plaintiffs' constitutional rights had not been denied. The candidate chose to join the Democratic Party. A benefit of that choice was her opportunity to participate in the nominating process of the party. A burden of that choice was her disqualification from seeking office as a candidate unaffiliated with that party. The closed party primary did not violate the constitutional rights of otherwise eligible voters not members of the party. The voter was not denied the opportunity to vote in the Democratic Party primary election and could have written in the name of the candidate if she had not qualified for the ballot.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the dismissal of plaintiffs' action and entered judgment that the election laws did not violate the rights of the voter or the candidate. The court dismissed plaintiffs' appeal from the denial of their request for an injunction and stay.

 

299 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


John S. Lane & Son, Inc. v. Commissioner of Revenue


No. S-3696


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 137; 484 N.E.2d 1005; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1724


September 13, 1985, Argued  
November 4, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Appellate Tax Board reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner of Revenue sought review of the decision of the Appellate Tax Board (board) (Massachusetts), which had ruled that appellee taxpayer was not entitled to an investment tax credit under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 63, § 31A (1984). However, the board ruled that the commissioner lacked the authority under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 58, § 2 (1984) to change the taxpayer's classification for prior tax years.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was classified as a foreign manufacturing corporation by the commissioner under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 58, § 2 (1984). Inter alia, the commissioner informed the taxpayer that its classification was being revoked and that it would be classified as a business corporation. The commissioner notified the taxpayer under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62C, § 26(b) (1984) that deficiencies in the corporate excise it paid for three prior years were being assessed. On appeal, the board determined that, while the taxpayer was not entitled to classification as a manufacturing corporation, the commissioner could not change the taxpayer's classification for the prior years, and determined that the taxpayer was entitled to abatements on the additional tax assessed. On review, the court reversed. The court determined that if the commissioner had made a mistake in determining the classification of a corporation, unless specifically prohibited by statute or constitutional principles, he should not have been estopped from correcting that mistake and from assessing a tax that was otherwise lawfully due. The commissioner of revenue was permitted to retroactively revoke the taxpayer's classification.


OUTCOME: The court disagreed with the legal conclusions of the board and reversed its decision that the commissioner could not change the taxpayer's classification for certain prior tax years.

 

300 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices to Senate


No. S-3963


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


396 Mass. 1201; 484 N.E.2d 95; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1762



October 21, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Senate of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts sought the court's opinion on whether a proposed bill relative to the financing and operation of convention and civic centers in Massachusetts was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The bill was proposed with an eye to operating and maintaining convention and civic centers. The court first noted that the Senate's questions did not refer to any specific constitutional provision perceived as raising doubts as to the bill's constitutionality, and that the court generally declined to answer vague questions regarding proposed bills' constitutionality. However, the court noted that Mass. Const. amend. art. 63, which required that monies received on account of the Commonwealth be paid into its treasury, was meant to place the fiscal operations of the Commonwealth as far as possible on a strict budget plan. While there were exceptions to its requirements, the court found that to avoid the strictures of art. 63, the proposed bill had to allow disbursement of funds only in compliance with carefully prescribed legislative conditions. The court held that the bill's empowerment of a convention center authority to spend revenues provided insufficient supervision or control by the legislature and by state and local governments, and thus violated the requirements of art. 63.


OUTCOME: The court advised the Senate that a portion of the bill violated specific constitutional requirements. The court requested to be excused from answering the questions as propounded.

Fitchburg Gas & Electric Light Co. v. Department of Public Utilities


No. S-3876


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 836; 483 N.E.2d 76; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1798


May 9, 1985, Argued  
September 12, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on April 12, 1985.

The cases were reported by O'Connor, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, several investor-owned utilities and a municipal electric company, appealed from an order of respondent, the Department of Public Utilities (department), which denied the financing application of each petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Each petitioner had at least one financing case pending before the department when they filed a joint petition requesting that the department conduct a single investigation of the cost and schedule for the completion of the nuclear project in question. Petitioners sought findings of fact on those issues and requested that the findings be incorporated into the pending individual applications by which each sought authorization and approval of stock and bond issuances related to the nuclear plant's construction costs. The department denied the financing application, finding that petitioners' failure to present a reasonable range of possible cost estimates supported by reviewable and realistic construction schedules was fatal. It also found that the issuances proposed in the individual financing cases could not be determined to be reasonably necessary based on an economic analysis of the project and that the degree of risk associated with increased costs and potential future abandonment precluded a finding that the plant was reasonably necessary. The court affirmed these findings.


OUTCOME: The department's decision and orders, in so far as they concerned the financing applications related to the nuclear facility in question, were affirmed. The court remanded to the department for further consideration the applications of the investor-owned utilities for approval of other financing.

 

302 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Adamowicz v. Ipswich


No. S-3785


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 757; 481 N.E.2d 1368; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1686


May 7, 1985, Argued  
August 22, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Certification of questions of law to the Supreme Judicial Court by the United States Court of Appeals for the First Circuit.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the First Circuit (Massachusetts) certified questions concerning the proper interpretation of the Zoning Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 40A, § 6 (1984), in an action by landowners that requested a mandatory injunction ordering the Town of Ipswich, Massachusetts to issue building permits.


OVERVIEW: The town refused to issue building permits to the landowners asserting that the lower court's interpretation of the Zoning Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 40A, § 6 (1984) was incorrect. The court ruled that the lower court's determination that the word "recording," as it appeared in the statute did not necessarily refer to the recording of a plan was proper because Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 4, § 7 (1984), defined "recorded" as applying to plans, deeds, or other instruments affecting land. The court found that the status of the lot immediately prior to the zoning change controlled the interpretation of the statute's common ownership requirement because the purpose of the statute was to protect a once valid lot from being rendered unbuildable for residential purposes. The court held that a lot met the requirement in the statute language if the most recent instrument of record prior to a restrictive zoning change revealed that the lot was separately owned, even though a previously recorded subdivision plan may reveal that the lot was at one time part of land held in common ownership because there was no contrary indication that the legislature intended the statute to operate prospectively.


OUTCOME: The court held that the language of the zoning statute protected the landowners because the proper interpretation of the statute referred to the recording of any instrument affecting land in accordance with the status of the lot immediately prior to the zoning change.

 

303 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Leigh v. Board of Registration in Nursing


No. S-3857


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 670; 481 N.E.2d 1347; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1680


May 8, 1985, Argued  
August 15, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on February 23, 1984.

The case was heard by Wilkins, J., and was reserved and reported by him after further proceedings before the Board of Registration in Nursing.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nurse sought review of a decision by the Board of Registration in Nursing (board) (Massachusetts), which sustained its earlier decision to suspend the nurse's license, on the grounds that the nurse's practice of midwifery without the board's authorization was in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 80B-D and the board's regulations promulgated thereunder, and constituted gross misconduct in the practice of nursing.


OVERVIEW: The nurse contended that the board did not have jurisdiction to suspend her license, that she had been deprived of due process of law under both the federal and state constitutions, and that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 80C (1984), as interpreted by the board, was unconstitutional as violating the guarantees of due process of law and the equal protection of the laws. The court held that the board had the power to discipline the nurse because she violated § 80C and board regulations at Mass. Regs. Code tit. 244, § 4.00. The board could have concluded that such violation constituted gross misconduct in the practice of nursing under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 61. However, the board was not warranted in disciplining the nurse on any other basis; the mere practice of midwifery itself was not ground for discipline. The nurse had not demonstrated that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 80C violated the constitutional requirements of due process. The court set aside the suspension because the board shifted ground during the proceedings as to the basis of its claim of power to discipline the nurse, and the board might have determined its sanction on the theory that midwifery itself was illegal.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the suspension of the nurse's license and remanded the matter to the board for reconsideration in light of the opinion of the court.

Lee v. Commissioner of Revenue


No. Hd-3725


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 527; 481 N.E.2d 183; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1719


April 1, 1985, Argued  
August 1, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 7, 1983.

The case was heard by Raymond R. Cross, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by appellee taxpayers against appellant, the Commissioner of Revenue (the Commissioner), in which the taxpayers challenged the constitutionality of a statute which granted real estate tax abatements to certain property owners, Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 59, § 5, the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) found the provision unconstitutional. The Commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers challenged the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 59, § 5, which granted real estate tax abatements to persons over the age of seventy who owned and occupied their homes for at least ten years. The taxpayers claimed this was an unconstitutional infringement of their right to travel, and the trial court agreed. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the exemption at issue did not rise to a level of interference with the right to travel that justified the application of strict scrutiny, as was applied by the trial court. Rather, the state action in question did not affect the right to travel in any significant way. Additionally, the court found that the statutory provision had a fair and rational relationship to the object sought to be accomplished, and that the taxpayers' fundamental right to travel, as guaranteed by the United States Constitution, was not infringed. The court entered a judgment in favor of the Commissioner accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court ruling in favor of the taxpayers and entered judgment in favor of the Commissioner.

Champagne v. Commissioner of Correction


No. N-3610


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 382; 480 N.E.2d 609; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1636


March 6, 1985, Argued  
July 11, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 14, 1982.

The case was heard by Roger J. Donahue, J., on motions for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a complaint which sought declaratory and injunctive relief, money damages, and attorneys' fees for alleged violations of his speech and due process rights and his constitutional rights of access to the courts and assistance of counsel. The inmate appealed the decision of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which granted defendant prison official's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that the prison officials censored and confiscated his incoming publications, thereby violating his speech and due process rights under both the Federal and Massachusetts Constitutions and that he was denied his constitutional rights of access to the courts and assistance of counsel by the prison officials' mishandling of his legal correspondence. The court held that the prison officials' initial failure to deliver incoming books to the inmate was in accordance with permissible prison policy and did not violate the inmate's constitutional rights. Therefore, the court held that the prison officials were entitled to summary judgment on this count, as well as on the inmate's claim concerning his legal correspondence. However, the court agreed with the inmate that one of the prison regulations governing the censorship of incoming mail was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Therefore, the court allowed his motion for summary judgment on that issue, and directed the entry of an appropriate declaration of rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judge's order of summary judgment for the prison officials with respect to the inmate's claim that they withheld incoming books as well as his claim of unconstitutional interference with his legal correspondence. The court ordered that declarations were to be entered that the statute which allowed for the censorship of incoming mail was unconstitutional.

Commonwealth v. Williams


No. S-3746


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 302; 479 N.E.2d 687; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1585


April 3, 1985, Argued  
July 3, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Roxbury Division of the District Court Department on December 2, 1983.

On transfer to the jury session of the Boston Municipal Court Department the case was heard by George A. O'Toole, Jr., J., on a statement of agreed facts.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Boston Municipal Court (Massachusetts), which found defendant guilty of loitering pursuant to Boston, Mass., City Code, Ordinance tit. 14, § 286.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his loitering conviction. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court concluded that the ordinance, as written, was unconstitutionally vague within the meaning of the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment in that it failed to give sufficient warning and definition of the proscribed conduct, and promoted arbitrary enforcement. The language failed to provide a person of common intelligence with sufficient notice of the offending conduct. The court found that it was unclear what conduct a person might engage in before it rose to the level of obstructing a traveler. Furthermore, the ordinance failed to set minimal guidelines to govern law enforcement.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court finding defendant guilty of loitering was reversed.
