Petition of Catholic Charitable Bureau of Archdiocese, Inc., etc.


No. E-3809


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 180; 479 N.E.2d 148; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1566


April 4, 1985, Argued  
June 11, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex.

Petition filed in the Essex Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on December 14, 1981.

The case was heard by Edward J. Rockett, J.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother sought review of a judgment from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the trial court's grant of petitioner archdiocese's motion to dispense with parental consent for the adoption of the mother's minor child.


OVERVIEW: The mother voluntarily placed two of her children in foster care with the archdiocese. The older child was eventually returned to the mother, but the younger child thrived in foster care. The archdiocese filed a petition to dispense with the need for parental consent to adopt, which the trial court granted, and the appellate court affirmed. On further appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court's judgment. The court held that the critical issue was whether the natural parents were currently fit to further the welfare and best interests of the child. The court further held that the instability of the mother's living condition had a deleterious effect on the child. The mother's participation in join mother-child therapy was irregular and of short duration. During a visit to the mother's apartment, a social worker observed broken windows, lack of heat and electricity, and a constant urine odor. In addition, the mother had serious emotional problems and she was so overwhelmed with her own problems that she was unable to provide the parenting necessary for the child's growth and development.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that granted the archdiocese's request to dispense with parental consent for adoption.

 

309 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Zeller v. Cantu


No. W-3711


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 76; 478 N.E.2d 930; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1550; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P10,604


March 4, 1985, Argued  
June 5, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court on April 25, 1975.

Following the decision of the Appeals Court reported in 15 Mass. App. Ct. 919 (1983) and entry of judgment, a motion for enforcement of contribution was heard by Robert V. Mulkern, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor appealed an order from the Superior Court (Massachusetts) directing him to pay a pro rata contribution of 50 percent of a judgment entered for plaintiff patient. The doctor argued that his share of the damages should be based upon his degree of fault because the comparative negligence act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 85 (1984), modified the Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act (Act), Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231B (1984).


OVERVIEW: The doctor also argued that the principles of equity were applicable to contribution and, therefore sanctioned the apportionment of damages by comparative fault. Finally, the doctor argued that to the extent the Act required pro rata contribution without consideration of relative fault, it violated the due process and equal protection provisions of the Massachusetts and United States Constitutions. The court found that nothing in § 85 undermined the system of pro rata contribution mandated by the Act. Therefore, the court agreed with the trial court that the Act barred any consideration of the relative fault of a codefendant in assessing his or her pro rata share of the damages. Further, the court found that the fact that a more equitable method of apportioning liability might exist did not render the Act unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below ordering the doctor to pay a pro rata contribution of 50 percent of the judgment entered for the patient.

Petition by Massachusetts Bar Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


395 Mass. 1; 478 N.E.2d 715; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1519



May 23, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition filed in the Supreme Judicial Court for the Commonwealth on June 26, 1984.

The matter was considered on briefs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bar associations sought the establishment of an Interest on Lawyers' Trust Accounts (IOLTA) program, appointment of an implementation committee to oversee the development and execution of an IOLTA plan, if authorized, and designation of the organization or organizations that were eligible to receive the funds that were generated by any such plan.


OVERVIEW: The bar associations filed a petition to amend Mass. Sup. Jud. Ct. R. 3:07, Canon 9, DR 9-102 to establish an IOLTA program, to appoint an implementation committee to oversee an authorized program's development and execution, and to designate the organization(s) that could receive the funds that any such plan generated. The court granted that petition. The court reasoned that interest on nominal or short-term trust deposits was not property for constitutional purposes because income was being created where there was not any before and the created income would not have benefited the client under any circumstances. The court also held that the program did not contravene any relevant ethical considerations because only funds that were not currently earning interest for the attorney or the client were involved and that the client could not require the payment of any interest on the funds to himself or herself because that interest was likely to be less than the fees for administering the earnings.


OUTCOME: The court granted the bar associations' petition to amend the Massachusetts Supreme Judicial Court Rules to create an IOLTA program, to appoint an implementation committee to oversee an authorized program's development and execution, and to designate the organizations that were eligible to receive funds from the plan.

Guardianship of Hurley


No. Hs-3676


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


394 Mass. 554; 476 N.E.2d 941; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1448


February 4, 1985, Argued  
April 16, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampshire.

Petition filed in the Hampshire Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on August 21, 1980.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on September 29, 1980.

The cases were consolidated for trial in the Probate and Family Court Department and were heard by Sean M. Dunphy, J.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual by his next friend and guardian and defendants, city election officials, state officials, and the probate and family court (probate court) sought additional appellate review of an order from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts) that required the probate court to determine a reasonable attorney's fee to be awarded to the individual as a prevailing party under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OVERVIEW: The individual, by his next friend and guardian, filed an action with the probate court to modify and limit the individual's guardianship because of improvements in his condition. While that matter was pending, the individual filed an action in the supreme judicial court seeking relief after the city election officials declined to register the individual to vote. The cases were consolidated in the probate court and the probate court determined that only the individual's estate was under guardianship, and that the individual was capable of exercising his right to vote. Thereafter, the individual filed a motion for attorney's fees that was denied by the probate court. The court of appeals remanded the action to the probate court and the court granted further review before the remand. The court held that the individual was a prevailing party under § 1988 and was entitled to attorney's fees. The individual clearly alleged a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because his claims went to an essential constitutional right concerning his right to vote. The court delineated specific actions that were recoverable under § 1988 so that the probate court could calculate a reasonable fee upon remand.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter to the probate court with instructions to determine a reasonable attorney's fee for the individual in his action against defendants to restore his right to vote.

 

312 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Petition of Thompson


No. S-3620


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


394 Mass. 502; 476 N.E.2d 216; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1443


January 7, 1985, Argued  
April 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Petition filed in the Superior Court Department on July 18, 1979.

The case was heard by John J. Irwin, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Order denying petition affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from an order of the Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which denied his request, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 9, for discharge from his commitment to a treatment center for sexually dangerous persons. The inmate argued that the trial court erred in refusing to consider evidence that he alleged would have established that confinement in a less restrictive facility was warranted.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was confined to a treatment center for sexually dangerous persons. He filed a petition for discharge and sought to present evidence concerning the possibility of confinement to a less restrictive facility. The trial court concluded that the evidence was inadmissible at a § 9 hearing. It found that the inmate continued to be a sexually dangerous person, and denied the petition for discharge. On appeal, the court affirmed, ruling that because the trial court determined that the inmate was a sexually dangerous person, any consideration of alternatives to confinement at the treatment center would have been improper. The court reasoned that § 9 hearings were restricted to the sole issue of determining whether or not a petitioner was a sexually dangerous person. The court further held that the court's holding that § 9 did not permit consideration of alternatives to the treatment center was not an unconstitutional interference with the inmate's right to be free from undue restraint. The court ruled that because the inmate was eligible to apply for parole, he was afforded an ample opportunity to be heard on the issue of alternative, less restrictive, modes of confinement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the inmate's petition to be discharged as a sexually dangerous person from the treatment center.

 

313 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Upton


No. Barn-2941


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


394 Mass. 363; 476 N.E.2d 548; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1398


October 2, 1984, Argued  
April 1, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Barnstable.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department, three on October 7, 1980, and two on March 10, 1981.

Following review by this court reported in 390 Mass. 562 (1983), there was a rehearing pursuant to an order of the Supreme Court of the United States.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the trial court, which denied his motions to suppress evidence seized pursuant to a search warrant. The state supreme court (Massachusetts) held that the search violated the U.S. Const. amend. IV. The Supreme Court of the United States reversed. It held that probable cause was shown under the "totality of the circumstances" and remanded the case for further proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth argued that evidence seized pursuant to a search warrant should be admissible, regardless of whether there was probable cause, because the court had never accepted the concept of an exclusionary rule under the state constitution when a search violated Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 14. Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 276, § 2B, provided a statutory prohibition against the admission of such evidence. The court rejected the "totality of the circumstances" test espoused by a majority of the United States Supreme Court and held that the principles developed under the Aguilar-Spinelli standard provided a more appropriate structure for probable cause inquiries under art. 14. The court determined that probable cause was not shown on the affidavit in the case because the veracity of the informant was not shown. The Commonwealth argued that the search was justified as a warrantless search under an automobile exception to the requirement of a search warrant. However, as a matter of Massachusetts's constitutional law, the court declined to admit the evidence seized from defendant's motor home under an exception to the warrant requirement of art. 14.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case subject to prior orders. The court concluded that (1) there was a statutory exclusionary rule requiring the exclusion of evidence seized without a showing of probable cause; (2) the test for determining probable cause was stricter under the Massachusetts Constitution than under the Fourth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution; and (3) the application for the search warrant did not demonstrate probable cause.

 

314 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Doherty


No. M-3503


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


394 Mass. 341; 476 N.E.2d 169; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1394


November 6, 1984, Argued  
March 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court on December 11, 1973.

Following review by this court reported in 371 Mass. 412 (1976), a motion for a new trial, filed May 18, 1982, was heard by Thomas R. Morse, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which denied defendant's motion for a new trial after his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the second degree and armed assault in a dwelling house with intent to rob. After his convictions were affirmed, defendant filed a motion for a new trial. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion. The court found that defendant had no constitutional right to a judicial grant of immunity to defense witnesses. The court noted that the decision whether to grant immunity was for the prosecutor. Further, defendant failed to show that any unique circumstances existed which would have warranted granting immunity to a prospective witness, who was an actual or potential target of prosecution. There was no newly discovered evidence regarding an alleged deal that warranted a new trial. Moreover, the trial judge did not err in failing to admit certain affidavits regarding the alleged deal. The court noted that defendant failed to establish that any suppressed materials were clearly exculpatory or that they were material. Defendant was accorded a reasonable cross-examination, despite the fact that the trial judge limited certain questions. Finally, the court determined that the jury instructions on reasonable doubt and felony murder were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny defendant's motion for a new trial.

Gurry v. Board of Public Accountancy


No. S-3499


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


394 Mass. 118; 474 N.E.2d 1085; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1368


November 5, 1984, Argued  
February 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 14, 1983.

Upon transfer to the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk, the case was reported by Nolan, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accountant appealed the decision by defendant Board of Public Accountancy (board), which suspended the accountant's license to practice for two years. The matter was transferred from the Superior Court (Massachusetts) to the court for review. The accountant contended that the board exceeded its authority under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 87C(a) and that the regulation proscribing "discreditable conduct" was impermissibly vague.


OVERVIEW: After a complaint was filed against an accountant by a company, the accountant's license to practice was suspended for two years by the Board of Public Accountancy (board). The board concluded that the accountant made an unauthorized appropriation of funds from the company, which constituted discreditable conduct for a certified public accountant in violation of Mass. Regs. Code tit. 252 Code § 3.05(1). Thereafter, the accountant filed an appeal with the superior court. Upon review, after transfer of the matter from the superior court, the court affirmed the board's order suspending the accountant's certificate and license for two years. The court held that the board acted within its authority under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 87C(a) in suspending the accountant and that the board's regulatory standard proscribing "discreditable conduct," as was applied in this case, was not impermissibly vague in violation of due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court concluded that the board's application of § 3.05(1) to discipline the accountant was rationally related to accomplishing the legislative purpose of protecting the public welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the Board of Public Accountancy in its suspension of the accountant's license to practice for two years.

Commonwealth v. Campbell


No. M-3626


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


394 Mass. 77; 474 N.E.2d 1062; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1331


November 9, 1984, Argued  
February 19, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 29, 1983.

The case was tried before John Paul Sullivan, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted defendant of homicide by a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicating substance in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24G(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a required finding of not guilty because there was insufficient evidence of either defendant's negligence or a causal relationship between his actions and the victims' deaths. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and found that there was sufficient evidence for the jury to convict him under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24G(a). In so holding, the court found that 1) the commonwealth presented sufficient evidence for the jury to have concluded that, independent of driving under the influence of an intoxicating liquor, defendant negligently operated his motor vehicle; 2) the trial court erred in allowing the jury to have elected a foreperson, rather than appointing one for them, but the error was not prejudicial to defendant; 3) there was no merit in defendant's claim that the trial court judge did not fully explain the "endanger the lives and safety" aspect of the jury instructions to the jurors; and 4) the trial court judge properly refused to instruct the jury as to the alleged contributory negligence of the victims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for homicide by a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicating substance.

 

317 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Tuitt


No. Hd-3506


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 801; 473 N.E.2d 1103; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1312


October 4, 1984, Argued  
January 31, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 15 and 16, 1982.

The cases were tried before Robert L. Steadman, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant sought review of a decision by the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which rendered judgment on a jury verdict convicting defendant of armed robbery, and carrying a firearm without a permit. Defendant was subsequently sentenced under the habitual offender statute and sentenced to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On the day of trial, defendant made a motion to discharge his court appointed attorney as inefficient, and after hearing defendant's arguments, the lower court denied the motion. Defendant appealed his conviction and alleged several errors. The court held that: (1) a motion to discharge counsel when made on the eve of trial was in the discretion of the judge after a reasonable inquiry into the defendant's reasons for discharge; (2) a breakdown in the attorney-client relationship alone was not grounds for discharge where the attorney represented that the breakdown would not affect his ability to defend his client, and the record did not reveal any adverse effects on the trial; (3) defendant was not entitled to proceed pro se where he unequivocally refused to waive his right to counsel; and (4) the explicit legislative determination that habitual offenders be sentenced under the "maximum term provided by law" which was a life sentence in defendant's case, precluded the lower court's discretion in reducing defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction against defendant.

Commonwealth v. Turner


No. N-3455


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 685; 473 N.E.2d 679; 1985 Mass. LEXIS 1210


November 6, 1984, Argued  
January 21, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court on January 13, 1975.

The cases were tried before Henry H. Chmielinski, Jr., J.

After review by this court, reported in 371 Mass. 803 (1971), a motion for a new trial, filed on June 10, 1981, was heard by Andrew R. Linscott, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Order denying motion for new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Norfolk County (Massachusetts) convicted defendant of murder in the first degree, assault, unlawfully carrying a weapon, and using a motor vehicle without authority. The court affirmed the judgment. Defendant then successfully filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in a federal court. A federal appellate court reversed. Defendant then filed a motion for a new trial, which the trial court denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Each of the convictions arose out of the armed robbery of a convenience store during which a customer was fatally shot. In his petition for federal habeas relief, defendant contended that his confrontation rights under the Sixth Amendment were violated when the trial court refused to strike the direct testimony of two accomplices to whom the Commonwealth had granted immunity, and who had invoked their privilege against self-incrimination during cross-examination about prior armed robberies of the same store. In his motion for a new trial, defendant set forth the same arguments he had presented to the federal court. The trial court denied the motion as no reason was offered why the points presented were not raised before the trial court or on appeal. The court agreed and held that defendant did not the issue at his trial, or before the court on his initial appeal. The court further held that allowing the accomplices to plead the Fifth Amendment on cross-examination, while refusing to strike their direct testimony, did not create a substantial likelihood of a miscarriage of justice against defendant. The court noted that the accomplices' testimony was both collateral and cumulative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Board of Assessors v. Commissioner of Revenue


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 580; 472 N.E.2d 658; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1887


October 5, 1984, Argued  
December 20, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Massachusetts Commissioner of Revenue (commissioner) appealed from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts) (board), which modified a determination by the commissioner of the value of lands owned by plaintiff town on the ground that the commissioner had failed to comply with Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 58, § 13 (amended by 1978 Mass. Acts ch. 514, §§ 43, 44).


OVERVIEW: The town filed an action against the commissioner. The town claimed that the commissioner had improperly valued land owned by the town. The board found that the commissioner had failed to comply with § 13 and modified the commissioner's determination of value. On appeal, the court reversed the board's decision and remanded the case to the board for further proceedings. The court held that the board was not permitted to determine the most appropriate method of valuation. The court ruled that the board's role was to determine whether the method used by the commissioner was reasonably designed to achieve the statute's objectives and whether that method was properly implemented. The court held that if the method adopted by the commissioner was not arbitrary and capricious, then the board should have upheld the commissioner's determination. The court determined that the board had exceeded its authority by modifying the commissioner's determination of value.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the board's decision modifying the commissioner's determination of the value of the town's land. The court remanded the case to the board for further proceedings.

 

320 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Petition for Revocation of Judgment for Adoption of a Minor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 556; 471 N.E.2d 1348; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1885


October 1, 1984, Argued  
December 19, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Petition filed in the Suffolk Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on October 29, 1982.

The case was heard by Mary B. Muse, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court, on its own initiative, directed appellate review of an order of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which denied petitioner grandmother's request for a revocation of adoption, thus allowing the child to be adopted by respondent foster parents.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother sought to have the child's adoption by its foster parents revoked. The trial court and the appellate court denied her request. The court, on its own initiative, directed appellate review. The court affirmed the order of the appellate court, holding that the grandmother could not rely on a lack of notice argument because respondent Department of Social Services did not have to notify grandparents of adoptions under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 210, § 2. Additionally, the grandmother did not have to be notified merely because she filed a guardianship petition. The applicable language of § 2 no longer required notice to a guardian. Furthermore, the grandmother had merely applied for guardianship, but it had not been granted. Finally, the grandmother was not entitled to notice as the next of kin because the child was not parentless. In addition, the grandmother waited longer than the maximum one year after actual notice of the adoption before she petitioned for revocation of the judgment. Thus, her petition could not have been considered even if she was entitled to notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court which denied the grandmother's petition for a revocation of the child's adoption by the foster parents.

 

321 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Polaroid Corp. v. Commissioner of Revenue


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 490; 472 N.E.2d 259; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1873


October 4, 1984, Argued  
December 11, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on September 19, 1983.

The case was reported by Liacos, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed an action seeking a declaration that defendant Commissioner of Revenue's action in redetermining corporate excise taxes for 1979 and 1980 based on a worldwide unitary apportionment of the combined income of plaintiff and its various subsidiaries was unlawful.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporation and its subsidiaries had conducted a unitary business in the United States and in numerous foreign countries. Well after plaintiff had filed their corporate excise returns for the years 1979 and 1980, defendant commissioner redetermined their corporate excises for those years based on a worldwide unitary apportionment of the combined income of plaintiff and its various subsidiaries. Plaintiff paid the additional assessments with interest. The court held that because no rules had been promulgated regarding reasonable rules of apportionment defendant could not make additional assessments of plaintiff's corporate excises. In addition, defendant lacked statutory authority to use the "unitary business" approach in the circumstances of this case. Because plaintiff and defendant agreed that all the transactions between plaintiff and its subsidiaries were arms-length, the method followed by defendant would conflict with the due process of law requirements of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, in measuring one corporation's excise by reference to property or income not belonging to the corporation that defendant sought to be taxed.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant commissioner's actions in redetermining plaintiff corporation's corporate excise taxes were unlawful and remanded the case to the county court for entry of a declaratory judgment.

Martin v. School Committee of Natick


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 430; 472 N.E.2d 231; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1871


September 12, 1984, Argued  
December 10, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 29, 1980.

The case was heard by Paul G. Garrity, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, superintendent and school committee, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which declared that Mass. Gen. Laws ch.71, § 42D was unconstitutional. Plaintiff teacher cross-appealed the decision of the trial court, which ruled in favor of defendants that the thirty-day suspension was proper.


OVERVIEW: On January 18, 1980, the superintendent suspended the teacher for a period of five days. In a letter dated January 21, 1980, the teacher was notified that the committee intended to vote on his suspension for unbecoming conduct or other good cause at a meeting scheduled for January 29, 1980. The committee voted to suspend the teacher for an additional thirty days. The teacher filed a civil action challenging both suspensions. The trial court concluded that Mass. Gen. The court reversed the trial court's decision with regard to the two-day suspension and affirmed its decision that the thirty-day suspension was proper. The court found that the statute was constitutional as applied. The court concluded that the committee imposed the suspensions in accordance with both the statutory procedures and the requirements of due process, and that the record supported a finding that the charges were substantiated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment with respect to the five-day suspension and entered judgment in favor of defendants. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of defendants with respect to the validity of the teacher's thirty-day suspension.

Commonwealth v. Crowley


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 393; 471 N.E.2d 353; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1834


September 10, 1984, Argued  
November 28, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 12, 1982.

A hearing on the defendant's competency to stand trial was held before Raymond R. Cross, J., and the case was tried before him.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction of assault with intent to commit rape from the Superior Court (Massachusetts) after the trial court found defendant competent to stand trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with assault with intent to commit rape, and after a competency hearing in which experts offered conflicting testimony, the trial court ruled that defendant was competent to stand trial. Defendant was convicted and challenged the judgment. The court reversed the trial court's finding of competency, holding that while the experts disagreed on whether defendant was ultimately competent, both experts' testimony that defendant lacked the capacity to communicate effectively with his lawyers suggested that defendant was not competent. The court further held that the record suggested that the trial court may have improperly placed the burden of proving incompetence on defendant, noting that an exchange on the record between attorneys indicated that counsel were proceeding under that assumption, and where defense counsel called his witnesses before the commonwealth called its own witnesses. The court concluded that on retrial, a finding of competency would have to satisfy the preponderance of evidence standard pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123, § 15(d) because competency was not an element of the offense with which defendant was charged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of assault with intent to commit rape, set aside the verdict, and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings in a case alleging assault with attempt to commit rape.

 

324 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices to House of Representatives


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 1209; 471 N.E.2d 1266; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1863



November 28, 1984 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Question 1(a), "Yes"; Question 1(b)(i), "Yes"; Question 1(b)(ii), "Yes"; Question 2, "No"; Question 3, "No"; Question 4, "No"; Question 5, "No" as to debt; "Yes" as to pledge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Massachusetts House of Representatives presented an order to the court setting forth questions concerning the constitutionality of H.R. 6140 (Mass. 1984), entitled "An act establishing Massachusetts development bank and providing revenue sources therefor." The court submitted its answers to the questions.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the assessment established by H.R. 6140 was a tax because it would constitute a corporate excise. The court found that benefit to private parties was an incident essential to accomplishment of the bill's important public purpose and would not, by itself, render the bill unconstitutional. The court further found that there was no constitutional impediment to delegating to the Commissioner of Revenue the power to adjust rates in accordance with the detailed directions set out in the bill. The court concluded that the revenues to be received would not be subject to the requirements of art. 63 of the Amendments to the Massachusetts Constitution because the funds would be impressed with a trust established to secure the debt obligations of the bank, which could disburse funds only in accordance with specific legislative conditions and within carefully defined limitations. The court concluded that neither the Commonwealth's commitment of revenues to secure payment of the bank's debt obligations nor the covenant with purchasers thereof would convert a debt of the bank to a debt of the Commonwealth, but they would result in a pledge of the Commonwealth's credit.


OUTCOME: The court answered the questions presented by the Massachusetts House of Representatives concerning the constitutionality of H.R. 6140.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff college sought review of a decision of the land court (Massachusetts), which affirmed defendant city's board of appeal's dismissal of the college's application to change the use of a building from a multi-family residence to a 50 student dormitory and declared that the Boston Zoning Code and Enabling Act (Act), 1956 Mass. Lambeth Corp. v. Commissioner of Revenue


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 237; 470 N.E.2d 793; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1793


September 12, 1984, Argued  
November 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Appellate Tax Board affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts), which upheld the determination of defendant, the Commissioner of Revenue, that the taxpayer was required to pay use tax based on the full purchase price of a new boat purchased by the taxpayer from a Connecticut boat dealer who was not a vendor registered under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62C, § 67.


OVERVIEW: As partial payment for the new boat, the taxpayer traded in a boat. The taxpayer paid a use tax to the Commonwealth of Massachusetts based on the difference between the purchase price of the new boat and the trade-in value of the old boat. The Commissioner demanded payment on the full purchase price based upon the fact the dealer did not hold a valid vendor's registration as required by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 64I, § 28 (1969) (as amended by 1969 Mass. Acts ch. 558, § 5). The taxpayer argued that § 28 was unconstitutional as a burden on interstate commerce. In affirming the decision, the court found that there was no discrimination against out-of state vendors that was apparent on the face of the statute or as applied. More than 1,500 out-of-state vendors were registered in the Commonwealth under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62C, § 67. The court held that any effects on interstate commerce by the Commonwealth's statutory scheme were not show to be more than incidental. The registration process was not shown to be burdensome, expensive, or discriminatory against out-of-state vendors. The taxpayer did not show that the payment of the higher tax was an impermissible burden on interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's decision.

 

328 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Spinelli v. Commonwealth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 240; 470 N.E.2d 795; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1790


September 13, 1984, Argued  
November 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Barnstable.

Petition filed in the Superior Court on March 18, 1965.

Following enactment of St. 1982, c. 251, and allowance of the Commonwealth's motion to strike the restoration of the case to the docket, the matter was reported to the Appeals Court by Elizabeth J. Dolan, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condemnee sought eminent domain damages. The case was dismissed as "inactive." The case was later restored to the active list, but a rescission of that order was later granted. Seven years later, pursuant to 1982 Mass. Acts ch. 251, the case was restored to active, but a superior court (Massachusetts) granted the Commonwealth's motion to rescind the restoration. The court accepted direct appellate review at the condemnee's request.


OVERVIEW: 1982 Mass. Acts ch. 251, which was passed 17 years after the condemnee's damages action was instituted, provided that notwithstanding any judicial decision to the contrary, the case of the condemnee was to be restored to its original status. In affirming the trial court's rescission of the clerical action, pursuant to the statute, that restored the condemnee's case to active, the court ruled that ch. 251 was unconstitutional. The statute violated Mass. Const. art. 30 of the Declaration of Rights because it attempted to nullify a court judgment through legislation. The court ruled that a judgment of a court was to stand as final. It could be reversed, modified, or superseded only by judicial process. It was wholly under the control of the judicial department of government. The Legislature could not "supersede" a judgment of a court by its direct declaration to that effect. The invalid statute was an attempt by the Legislature to exercise a power that was exclusive to the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

 

329 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Chelmsford Trailer Park, Inc. v. Chelmsford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 186; 469 N.E.2d 1259; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1784


June 4, 1984, Argued  
October 25, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 12, 1984.

A motion for a preliminary injunction was heard by Jeremiah Sullivan, J., sitting under statutory authority. Upon transfer to the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk, the case was reported by Nolan, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants town and tenants association appealed the decision of the Supreme Judicial Court for Suffolk County (Massachusetts), which denied their motion to vacate a preliminary injunction issued by the lower court in plaintiff mobile home park owner's action challenging the town's rent control and eviction by-law and its enabling act, 1983 Mass. Acts ch. 449 (Act), as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The town adopted a by-law under the Act to control rents and evictions in mobile home parks. The owner claimed that the Act and the by-law were unconstitutional. The appellate court denied a motion to vacate the trial court's injunction against implementing the by-law. On appeal, the court vacated the injunction, ruling that the by-law and the Act were constitutional. The court ruled that, although it was less detailed than other rent control laws, the Act provided sufficient guidance for the rent board's eviction and rent adjustment policies and did not unlawfully delegate legislative authority. The court found that the statutes governing evictions and rent adjustments provided safeguards against arbitrary action or abuse of discretion by the rent board. The court ruled that the Act did not allow the rent board to interfere with the judicial function by issuing orders used in defense of an eviction action because the owner could seek review of the rent board's decisions. The court concluded that the Act was not an ex post facto law as it only penalized charging future rents above a statutory ceiling and imposed no retroactive penalties for rents past charged.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's order granting the injunction and remanded the case for the entry of judgment in favor of the town and the tenants' association.

 

330 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Colon-Cruz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 150; 470 N.E.2d 116; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1888


May 7, 1984, Argued  
October 18, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on June 14, 1983.

Questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by John J. Irwin, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In each of defendants' first degree murder cases, the Worcester Superior Court (Massachusetts) granted the commonwealth's motion under Mass. R. Crim. P. 34 to report to the appeals court questions as to whether amendments to the death penalty statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 279, §§ 4, 57-71 and Mass. Laws ch. 265, § 2, were constitutional. Thereafter, the court granted the commonwealth's request for direct review.


OVERVIEW: The Massachusetts Legislature enacted 1982 Mass. Acts ch. 554 (Act), providing for capital punishment in certain cases of first degree murder. The Act applied to defendants' first degree murder cases. The Act amended the death penalty statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 2 and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 279, §§ 4, 57-71, to allow the death penalty only after a jury trial. As such, those who pled guilty in cases in which death was a possible sentence after trial avoided the risk of the death penalty. The court held that such legislation violated the Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 12 because it impermissibly burdened the right against self-incrimination and the right to a jury trial guaranteed by article 12. The court held that the legislation in issue discouraged defendants from asserting their right not to plead guilty and their right to demand a jury trial. The court found that if the trial court was not allowed to penalize a defendant for asserting his right to trial or his right not to plead guilty by imposing a harsher sentence than he otherwise would have received, the legislature was also not allowed to authorize such legislation.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question negatively and held that the amendments to the death penalty statute violated the Massachusetts Constitution Declaration of Rights. As such, the court did not find it necessary to answer the question as to whether the statutes in question violated the United States Constitution.

 

331 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Cabaret Enterprises, Inc. v. Alcoholic Beverages Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


393 Mass. 13; 468 N.E.2d 612; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1729


April 4, 1984, Argued  
September 11, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 11, 1982.

The cases were heard by Andrew G. Meyer, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant alcoholic beverages control commission (commission) sought review of the decisions of a superior court department (Massachusetts), which determined that the commission's application of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 138, § 12B that revoked plaintiff alcoholic beverage license holders' (license holders) all-alcoholic beverage licenses was unconstitutional under Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 16.


OVERVIEW: The commission revoked the all-alcoholic beverage licenses after police observed nude dancing at the lounges operated by the license holders. The license holders filed complaints against the commission that challenged the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 138, § 12B and sought relief against the statute's enforcement. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 16 did not permit the prohibition of non-obscene nude dancing on licensed premises in the absence of a demonstrated countervailing state interest. The court noted that there was no contention that the performances were obscene, no crime had been committed, the patrons had been forewarned, and there was no mingling between the patrons and the dancers. The court determined that the restraint was impermissible in the absence of a demonstration in the record or by legislative history that there was a rational basis to have concluded that the restraint was required for the protection of the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that determined that the application of the statute by the commission that resulted in the loss of the alcoholic beverage licenses was unconstitutional.

International Organization of Masters, etc. v. Woods Hole, Martha's Vineyard & Nantucket S.S. Authority

Gen. Laws ch. 150C, § 2 and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231A, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The union, as a bargaining representative of certain employees of the authority, commenced negotiations with the authority to reach a new agreement as an existing agreement was due to expire. The parties were unsuccessful in resolving certain issues that would enable them to execute the new agreement. 333 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Cass


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


392 Mass. 799; 467 N.E.2d 1324; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1726


October 5, 1983, Argued  
August 16, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Barnstable.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Barnstable Division of the District Court Department on November 26, 1982.

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Shea, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Review of a matter was transferred from the District Court, Barnstable Division (Massachusetts) to determine whether the term "person" in Mass. Gen. Law ch. 90, § 24G, the vehicular homicide statute, applied to a viable fetus, which died as a result of an impact with a motor vehicle driven by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with homicide by motor vehicle under Mass. Gen. Law ch. 90, § 24G(b). While operating a motor vehicle, defendant struck a female pedestrian who was eight and one-half months pregnant. The fetus died in the womb, and it was determined that the fetus was viable at the time of the accident and that it died as a result of the impact from the vehicle operated by defendant. The question addressed by the court was whether a viable fetus was within the meaning of the term "person" as used in the statute. In light of prior judicial decisions and the plain ordinary meaning of the words in the statute, the court concluded that a viable fetus was within the ambit of the term "person" as used in the statute. However, due to the unforeseeability of this specific consequence of defendant's conduct, the court ruled that its decision should be applied prospectively.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that a viable fetus was within the ambit of the term "person" in the vehicular homicide statute, but due to the unforeseeableness of this consequence, the court held that its decision be applied prospectively.

 

334 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Mattapoisett v. Director of Div. of Employment Sec.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


392 Mass. 546; 466 N.E.2d 125; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1664


April 5, 1984, Argued  
July 18, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth.

Civil action commenced in the Fourth Plymouth Division of the District Court Department on March 29, 1982.

The case was heard by Leonard, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee part-time police officer's claim for unemployment compensation was granted by appellee, the Massachusetts Division of Employment & Security, on the basis of a finding that the officer was partially unemployed under Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 151A, § 1(r)(1). A review examiner, a board of review, and the Wareham District Court (Massachusetts) upheld the award. Appellant town appealed.


OVERVIEW: The town employed the officer as a part-time employee. Under the terms of his employment contract, he was to work whenever he was needed. The officer understood that if no work was available in a given week, he would not work. There were weeks when he worked up to 72 hours and other weeks when he did not work at all. The officer did not refuse any work offered to him. On appeal, the town argued that because the claimant was hired as a part-time police officer with the understanding that his hours would be varied, he was not entitled to compensation, even though he worked less than 40 hours in certain weeks. In reversing the judgment from the district court, the court ruled that the review examiner's interpretation of the statute would grant partial unemployment status to every part-time employee, even though the contract of employment contemplated that the hours of work would fluctuate and that no work would be available at all in some weeks. The court ruled that the Legislature did not intend a part-time employee whose hours varied from week to week to be considered in partial unemployment for any week in which he did not work as many hours as a full-time employee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment.

Axelrod v. Board of Assessors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


392 Mass. 460; 466 N.E.2d 517; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1657


March 5, 1984, Argued  
July 12, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Appellate Tax Board affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts), which denied the taxpayer an abatement on property taxes imposed by defendant town board of assessors.


OVERVIEW: The town board of assessors imposed taxes on an improved parcel of land owned by the taxpayer. The Appellate Tax Board denied the taxpayer an abatement. The taxpayer appealed, alleging that the Board improperly calculated the equalized tax rate and that the Board's interpretation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 58A, § 14 denied him a constitutionally mandated adequate remedy for a disproportionate tax assessment. The court held that, as equalization studies were done only in even-numbered years, the Board correctly determined that for even-numbered fiscal years, for which the assessment date was January 1 of the preceding odd-numbered year, the equalized value for January 1 of the preceding even-numbered year was to be used in calculating damages under § 14. The court found that the taxpayer failed to demonstrate any inadequacy in the abatement remedy afforded him. The court affirmed the decision of the Appellate Tax Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Appellate Tax Board denying the taxpayer an abatement of taxes imposed by the town board of assessors.

 

336 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


International Marathons, Inc. v. Attorney Gen.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


392 Mass. 376; 467 N.E.2d 55; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1625


March 8, 1984, Argued  
July 3, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 6, 1983.

The case was heard by Steadman, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff solicitor appealed the decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which affirmed a decision of defendant division of public charities of the Attorney General's office. The division disapproved a contract between the solicitor and intervenor charity, because the contract provided that the solicitor would have received over 15 percent of the total money raised in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 68, § 21.


OVERVIEW: The solicitor and the charity's president entered into an agreement whereby the solicitor was to solicit sponsors for the charity to fund the charity's annual marathon. The charity's board of governors learned of the contract and filed an action to declare that the president lacked authority to enter into the contract. The division disapproved the contract because the solicitor was likely to receive compensation in excess of 15 percent in violation of § 21. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order affirming the division's decision. The court ruled that because it had, in a separate decision handed down on the same day it decided the solicitor's appeal, held that the president lacked the authority to enter into the contract, it was void ab initio. Thus, the court determined, there was no longer a contract between the charity and the solicitor. The court further held that the solicitor's activities were commercial in nature, rather than charitable solicitations under § 21, thus, it was to be compensated for the fair value of its services, and § 21 was not violated. The court concluded, therefore, that the solicitor's challenge to the constitutionality of § 21 was moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision dismissing the solicitor's appeal of the division's decision on the ground that the court's concurrent decision declaring the contract between the solicitor and the charity void ab initio rendered it moot.

 

337 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. White


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


392 Mass. 282; 467 N.E.2d 79; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1595


January 9, 1984, Argued  
June 25, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court on March 3, 1971.

The case was tried before Tomasello, J.

A motion for a new trial filed on December 22, 1981, was heard by Steele, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Middlesex Superior Court (Massachusetts) convicted defendant of murder in the second degree. On defendant's first appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court then granted defendant's motion for a new trial, based on new caselaw that applied retroactively. The Commonwealth appealed. The court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant knocked the victim unconscious, left, and then returned to shoot the victim three times so that the victim would not report the crime. The court found that because the case was tried on the theory that a murder was committed, the issue as to whether the burden of proof shifted impermissibly to defendant for any element of the crime was waived at trial. The court found, based on the facts, that if there were an error it did not prejudice defendant. In reversing, the court held that the trial judge did not confuse liability for felony-murder with liability for criminal joint venture. The court found that the jury instructions did not create an impermissible presumption with regard to liability for criminal joint venture. The court held that the trial judge's felony-murder instruction allowed the jury to find defendant guilty of murder without first finding that he acted with malice aforethought only if the jury first found that defendant was involved in an armed robbery. The court found that there was no suggestion that defendant could be found guilty of murder in the second degree without a finding that he acted with malice aforethought.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment to grant a new trial to defendant who was convicted by a jury of murder in the second degree.

Commonwealth v. Knight


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


392 Mass. 192; 465 N.E.2d 771; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1601


February 7, 1984, Argued  
June 15, 1984, Decided

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 15, 1981.

The case was tried before Roger J. Donahue, J.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Superior Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Massachusetts), which reversed defendant's conviction for armed robbery while masked.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction because the trial judge failed to exercise discretion in ruling on defendant's motion to exclude evidence of his prior convictions from being used to impeach defendant's credibility. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the record supported a determination that the trial judge knew he had discretion to exclude defendant's prior convictions but chose to exercise his discretion to permit the prosecutor to use them. When the record was viewed as a whole, the court found that the trial judge was aware that he had discretion to bar the use of the defendant's prior convictions for impeachment and considered the impact of admission of the convictions. Therefore, reversal of defendant's conviction was not required.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for armed robbery while masked was affirmed and the appellate court's judgment was reversed.

Planned Parenthood League, Inc. v. Attorney Gen.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 709; 464 N.E.2d 55; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1469


January 10, 1984, Argued  
April 23, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 24, 1982.

The case was heard by Fine, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state attorney general sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in Suffolk County (Massachusetts), which declared that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 68, § 28 was inapplicable to certain recruitment and fundraising activities carried on by appellee nonprofit organization. The lower court also declared that the statute was facially unconstitutional under U.S. Const., amend I.


OVERVIEW: A nonprofit organization sought declaratory and injunctive relief against the state attorney general. The nonprofit organization wished to continue its recruitment and fundraising campaign without subjecting itself to prosecution under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 68, § 28, which prohibited the use by nonprofit organizations of paid telephone operators to solicit funds. The lower court held that the statute was inapplicable to the activities of the nonprofit organization, and that the statute was facially unconstitutional under the First Amendment. The state attorney general appealed. On appeal, the court recognized that the state had the authority to protect its citizens from undue annoyance by restricting solicitation. The court also recognized that state action could be upheld only if the prohibition on free speech was a reasonable time, place, or manner regulation, or was in furtherance of a substantial governmental interest; and the restriction on First Amendment rights was no greater than necessary to promote that interest. The court found that the challenged statute abridged First Amendment rights and was not drawn to further a substantial governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

342 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Bible Baptist Church, Inc. v. Board of Assessors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 1015; 462 N.E.2d 1368; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1466



April 13, 1984 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed applications for abatement for the years 1981 and 1982 after he had failed to receive his tax bill for 1981. The taxpayer challenged the decision of an appellate tax board (Massachusetts), which on jurisdictional grounds dismissed the taxpayer's appeal from a decision of defendant, a board of assessors, to disallow the taxpayer's applications for abatement.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was church. The pastor did not advise the town of its change of address and, thus, did not receive a notice of the 1981 assessment until late in 1981 when the pastor went to the assessor's office to complain about the 1982 tax bill. At that time, the pastor filed the applications for abatement for 1981 and 1982. The court determined that the abatement for the 1981 assessment was not timely filed. There was no statutory requirement that the bill actually be received by the taxpayer. Because the application for abatement was filed late, the assessors had no jurisdiction to consider it. The board, therefore, had no jurisdiction to review the disallowance of the application. Thus, the 1981 appeal was correctly dismissed. Further, the court determined that because the 1981 assessment was not successfully appealed, the taxable valuation filed by the assessors stood. As a consequence of the effect of the valuation under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 59, § 64, as amended through 1978 Mass. Acts ch. 580, § 34. Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 59, § 65, the late payment barred an appeal of the 1982 assessment. The 1982 appeal was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the board.

Salhanick v. Commissioner of Revenue


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 658; 463 N.E.2d 1163; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1461


November 7, 1983, Argued  
April 13, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review of a decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts), which affirmed the refusal of defendant Commissioner of Revenue to abate taxes paid by her.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer owned certificates of interest in a trust whose only income was royalty income from the companies to which it leased its land for the purpose of mining iron ore. For three years, the taxpayer reported her trust income as long term capital gains on her federal income tax returns and as Part B income on her state tax returns. Part B income was income other than interest, dividends, or net capital gains. Based on the length of time that the taxpayer owned the certificates of interest, the commissioner reclassified the trust income to capital gains income and assessed additional taxes. The court held that the commissioner's application of the income tax statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62, was unconstitutional because it resulted in the imposition of different rates of taxation on income derived from the same class of property in contravention of Mass. Const. amend. art. 44. Article 44 required uniformity of tax rates with respect to income derived from the same kind of property and the court concluded that there was no difference in kind between the iron ore held by the taxpayer for one period of time and iron ore that was held for another period of time.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the board's decision that affirmed the commissioner's refusal to allow the taxpayer's applications for abatement and ordered the commissioner to refund all amounts collected in excess of the tax appropriately imposed, with interest from the date of collection.
