Guardianship of Doe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 614; 463 N.E.2d 339; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1451


January 12, 1984, Argued  
April 3, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Barnstable.

Petition filed in the Barnstable Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on January 4, 1983.

Orders appointing a temporary guardian were made by Lewis J., and Harvey, J. An order appointing a permanent guardian was made by Farrell, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner ward sought review of the orders from the Barnstable Division of the Probate and Family Court Department (Massachusetts), which appointed the ward's father as a temporary guardian and later a permanent guardian, pursuant to the alternative commitment procedure under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 201, § 14.


OVERVIEW: The ward challenged the probate court's guardianship orders, arguing that commitment pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 20, § 14 was unconstitutional because it violated her rights to due process and equal protection, and, alternatively, that the probate court did not comply with the statute. On appeal, the court found that the order appointing a temporary guardian was invalid, and vacated the probate court's order appointing a permanent guardian. Although the court agreed that the probate court's guardianship orders were invalid, the court concluded that ch. 201 was not unconstitutional. Under the court's interpretation of the guardianship statute, it was not deficient in a due process sense because a temporary guardian was authorized to treat or commit a ward only upon specific written findings that there was so extreme an emergency that the procedures of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123, § 12 were not sufficient, and when the ward could not be present, she had to be represented by counsel. The court held that the temporary and permanent guardianship orders were not issued in accordance with the statutory provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 201, §§ 7, 14, and therefore were invalid.


OUTCOME: The court found that the probate court's order appointing a temporary guardian of the ward was invalid, and vacated the probate court's order appointing a permanent guardian, in the ward's appeal challenging the alternative commitment procedure under the Massachusetts guardianship statute.

 

345 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


United States Jaycees v. Massachusetts Com. against Discrimination


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 594; 463 N.E.2d 1151; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1450


March 7, 1983, Argued  
April 3, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 31, 1981.

The case was reported by Hallisey, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner organization challenged a decision of respondent, Massachusetts Commission Against Discrimination, which determined that petitioner was a place of public accommodation as defined in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 92A and concluded that petitioner's refusal to treat women as members of equal standing was sex discrimination that violated of Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 272, § 98. A superior court (Massachusetts) reported the case to this court.


OVERVIEW: Fourteen women brought a complaint before respondent, Massachusetts Commission Against Discrimination, alleging that petitioner organization was "a place of public accommodation" within the meaning of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 92A and that its men-only membership policy amounted to unlawful sex discrimination in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 98. Respondent determined that petitioner was a "place of public accommodation" because petitioner met in physical places within Massachusetts, albeit a large number of different ones, and ordered that women be accorded equal membership status. Petitioner argued that the statutory category of a "place of public accommodation" was never meant to include nonprofit membership organizations such as petitioner. The court found that petitioner was not a "place of public accommodation," based upon the plain wording of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 92A and a survey of the relevant case law. The court reversed the decision of respondent because "place" was not a "technical" word and had no narrowly defined, special meaning aside from its common definition that a "place" was a "physical environment."


OUTCOME: The court ordered the decision of respondent, Massachusetts Commission Against Discrimination, that petitioner organization was a "place of public accommodation" and that, therefore, its policies amounted to unlawful sex discrimination, set aside. The plain meaning of the word "place" required a physical location and petitioner did not fall within the general or specific definition of a "place of public accommodation" provided by the statute.

 

346 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Emerson College v. Boston


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 415; 462 N.E.2d 1098; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1432


November 8, 1983, Argued  
March 14, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 27, 1983.

The case was heard by Nixon, J., and was reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Massachusetts trial court found a charge imposed against the owners of certain sized building by appellant city for fire protection unconstitutional and invalid as applied, and prohibited its application against appellee university. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 190, § 30 (1982), the city was allowed to charge for fire protection against the owners of certain buildings that by reason of their size, type of construction, use and other relevant factors required the city to employ additional firefighters and deploy additional equipment in the case of fire. The charge was mandatory for qualified property owners and was assessed regardless of whether or not any fire ever occurred on the premises. The university had several buildings which qualified by size under the statute and the charges were requested by the city accordingly. The university brought the current action for injunctive relief and claimed that the statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found the statute invalid where the charges had to be paid irrespective of whether the fire department's services were actually utilized. The charge was more like a tax, and not a fee, where it was not for services voluntarily requested, but was mandatory regardless of whether any service was ever received. On these facts, the statute more closely resembled a disproportionate real property tax and, as such, was not valid.


OUTCOME: The trial court ruling was affirmed.

 

347 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Fitta


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 394; 461 N.E.2d 820; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1428


November 10, 1983, Argued  
March 13, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Taunton Division of the District Court Department on July 16, 1982.

After the defendant claimed a jury trial in the Second Bristol Division, questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by Anderson, J. The Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct review on its own initiative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with open and gross lewdness and lascivious behavior, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 16. Defendant requested a jury trial in the Second Bristol Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts). The district court reported questions of law to the Appeals Court. The court on its own initiative transferred the report to itself.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sitting in his parked car at night. He called out to 2 10-year old boys and told one of them "you have nice legs" and asked what the boy was doing. The boys approached and defendant exposed his penis. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment. Longstanding judicial interpretation clearly conveyed sufficient definite warning as to the conduct proscribed as measured against common understanding and practice. Section 16 required conduct similar to that of indecent exposure, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53, but the former offense also required conduct that produced shock or alarm. The fact that defendant's conduct was punishable under either law did not render vague Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 16 because, the court held, § 16 required the aforementioned element not found for indecent exposure. The fact that § 16 provided a greater penalty than that for indecent exposure did not create impermissible uncertainty as to which may have been charged and the possible penalty imposed, as long as each statute clearly defined the prohibited conduct and the punishment.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the district court for trial of the charges against defendant for open and gross lewdness and lascivious behavior.

 

348 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Massachusetts Asso. for Blind v. Board of Assessors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 384; 462 N.E.2d 86; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1427


November 7, 1983, Argued  
March 13, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association appealed from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board (board), which dismissed the association's appeal from defendant assessors' denial of an abatement of a real estate tax assessed on property acquired by the association, based on a finding that it did not have jurisdiction over the action.


OVERVIEW: The charitable association filed a complaint against the assessors, appealing the decision of the board that dismissed its appeal from the denial of a real estate tax abatement. The board found that it did not have jurisdiction over the appeal of the denial because 1980 Mass. Acts ch. 560 did not revive its rights. The court remanded the action to the board for further proceedings. The court found that the board did not had jurisdiction over the appeal pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 59, § 59 prior to its amendment by 1977 Mass. Acts 198 because the charitable organization was a non-assessed owner which had not paid the entire tax at the time it initiated the appeal of the denial of the abatement. However, the court held that 1977 Mass. Acts ch. 198 validated the charitable association's claim of appeal. Act 198 applied retroactively to such appeal because of the remedial nature of the statute and because it would not interfere with the rights of the assessors. Therefore, the board had jurisdiction over such appeal. The court remanded for a determination of whether the charitable association'sailure to certify that a required form had been filed affected the board's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court found that the board had jurisdiction over the charitable association's appeal of the denial of its abatement of a real estate tax by the assessors and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

349 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Milligan v. Tibbetts Engineering Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 364; 461 N.E.2d 808; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1392


December 6, 1983, Argued  
March 6, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 22, 1982.

Motions for summary judgment were heard by Bennett, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.

The case was submitted on briefs.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff truck driver brought suit against defendant construction company and city for negligent design and maintenance in a public way. The city cross claimed against the construction company. The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) granted summary judgment to the construction company on the claim and cross claim, citing Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 260, § 2B. When the truck driver appealed, the court ordered direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: On March 19, 1981, the truck driver's tractor-trailer collided with a stone wall at the end of a road, seriously injuring him. On March 22, 1982, he filed his complaint. The city had accepted the extension of the road as having been completed and assumed full possession of it on October 31, 1973. The court explained that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 260, § 2B was a statute of repose which limited the time within which an action could have been brought and was not related to the accrual of any cause of action. The court ruled that the word "improvement" in the statute included road construction, adding that whether the improvement involved a road or a building, long lapses in time between the date of completion, the date of injury and, finally, litigation would have led to the same problems of proof, incomplete or lost records, unavailable witnesses, and defective memories. Because the extension of the road did constitute an "improvement to real property" as that term was used in the statute and the truck driver did not file his claim until nine years after the construction company had completed its work, his claim was barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted the construction company in the suit brought by the truck driver for negligence in designing a road extension as time barred.

Bannerman v. Fall River


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 328; 461 N.E.2d 793; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1388


December 6, 1983, Argued  
March 1, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 30, 1982.

The case was heard by Ponte, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipality sought review of a decision from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) granting summary judgment for plaintiff trustee and partners of a corporation on plaintiffs' action contending an ordinance adopted by the municipality which purported to regulate the conversion of rental apartments to condominium units violated § 7(5) of the Home Rule Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The trustee and partners of a corporation filed suit against a municipality challenging an ordinance adopted by the municipality which purported to regulate the conversion of rental apartments to condominium units. The ordinance created a Housing Conversion Board, which was authorized to issue or deny permits for the removal of multifamily housing from rental use. The trustee and partners contended the ordinance was invalid because it was a private or civil law governing civil relationship, thus violating § 7(5) of the Home Rule Amendment (HRA). The municipality contended the ordinance did not govern civil relationships and was within the powers reserved to local governments by HRA § 6. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for the trustee and partners and concluded that the ordinance was not within the powers reserved to the municipality by the HRA. The court held the ordinance affected the landlord-tenant relationship and thus was a private or civil law governing private relations and thus, a violation of HRA § 7(5). The court found the ordinance was not incident to an exercise of an independent municipal power to regulate and supervise public health.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for the trustees and partners and concluded the ordinance purporting to regulate the conversion of rental apartments to condominium units was invalid since the ordinance was a private or civil law which attempted to govern civil relationships.

 

351 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Workers' Compensation Rating & Inspection Bureau v. Commissioner of Ins.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 238; 461 N.E.2d 1178; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1381


October 6, 1983, Argued  
February 23, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 21, 1980, November 24, 1982, and December 6, 1982.

The cases were reported by O'Connor, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner group of employers sought review of respondent insurance commissioner's (commissioner) decisions on December 31, 1979, approving workers' compensation rates, and on October 15, 1982, disapproving proposed rates. The group sought to amend its complaint to challenge a decision approving revised rates effective January 1, 1983. Petitioner bureau of insurers sought to review the October 15, 1982 decision.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner approved the introduction of unlimited payrolls as the measurement of exposure to which the manual rates are applied. The court held that the commissioner's approval of the unlimited payroll program had reasonable support in the evidence: the bureau presented evidence that the existing limited payroll exposure system was not well suited to wage and benefit inflation. The court denied the group's motion to amend its complaint, as well as the commissioner's and bureau's motions to dismiss the complaint, because the group could raise these issues as an intervenor in the bureau's action. The court held that the commissioner's failure to find that the surplus flow methodology would lead to "not excessive" rates had reasonable support in the evidence; allocation of surplus according to reserves of coverage lines was not a well-refined method of surplus allocation. The court held that the testimony supported the commissioner's finding that the predicted loss cash flow proposed by the bureau based on simulated loss cash flow would lead to excessive rates. The commissioner's decision on the issue of a hypothetical tax rate was reasonably supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court denied employers' group's motion to amend its complaint. The court denied bureau's and commissioner's separate motions to dismiss the complaint, and their joint motion to dismiss group's complaint for review of the December 31, 1979, decision. The court ordered judgment affirming commissioner's December 31, 1979, decision and the deputy commissioner's October 15, 1982, decision.

 

352 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Boston v. Rockland Trust Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 48; 460 N.E.2d 1269; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1325; 37 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 1338


October 7, 1983, Argued  
February 2, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 31, 1980.

The case was heard by Connolly, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and city treasurer, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which held that appellee creditor maintained a perfected security interest in certain personal property of city taxpayers and that the city's seizure and distraint of that property were invalid.


OVERVIEW: City taxpayers took a certificated motor vehicle, on which the creditor had a perfected security interest, to another state and re-registered the vehicle in that state. The city eventually seized and distrained the vehicle because the taxpayers were delinquent on real estate taxes. The lower court found that the city's seizure and distraint were invalid. The city appealed and the court reversed. The court looked to the plain language of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 106, § 9-103 (as appearing in 1979 Mass. Acts ch. 512, § 7) and determined that the creditor's perfection lapsed automatically when the vehicle was relocated to another jurisdiction for more than four months and was reregistered, regardless of the taxpayers' intent or lack of intent to change their domicile. The court also determined that the creditor had no standing under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 60, §§ 24, 29 (as amended by 1980 Mass. Acts ch. 64, §§ 2, 4), to challenge the validity of the city's seizure and distraint. The court concluded that the city's seizure and distraint were valid with respect to the creditor and that the city acquired a valid lien on the motor vehicle.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, that the creditor maintained a perfected security interest and that the city's seizure and distraint were invalid, was reversed and the trial court was ordered to enter judgment for the city.

Commonwealth v. Varney


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


391 Mass. 34; 461 N.E.2d 177; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1324


October 5, 1983, Argued  
February 1, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on October 14, 1980.

A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Cameron, J., a District Court judge sitting under statutory authority, and the case was tried before Dwyer, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, entered in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), and subsequent sentence for cocaine possession and for intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress, failed to strike certain portions of the state's summation, that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C §32E(b)(3) was unconstitutional, and the sentence imposed upon him was invalid. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and held that denial of defendant's motion to suppress was proper because, as law enforcement authorities lawfully obtained a package address to defendant, a field test of white powder present in the package was not a Fourth Amendment "search." The court so held because defendant did not have a legitimate expectation of privacy in visible white powder contained in a glassine bag. The court found that by promising not to characterize defendant as a drug dealer, the state did not surrender its right to argue that evidence introduced, largely by defendant, supported an inference adverse to him. The court ordered that defendant be resentenced under the general provision of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C § 32E(b) because the sentencing statute was flawed, as it did not contain provisions for minimum and maximum sentences the basic structure of sentencing in Massachusetts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated his sentence and remanded for resentencing because of a flawed sentencing provision.

Commonwealth v. Burgos


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


390 Mass. 763; 459 N.E.2d 469; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1306


December 7, 1983, Argued  
January 17, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on December 21, 1981.

After the case was heard by Pierce, J., a motion for resentencing was heard by Moriarty, J., and a question of law was reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Massachusetts trial court convicted defendant to a second offense of distribution of heroin and convicted him pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32(b). Defendant filed a motion for resentencing. The appellate court was questioned whether a prior holding that the sanctions imposed by Mass. Gen. Law ch. 94C, § 32(a), were void for vagueness. The matter was transferred to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for the distribution of heroin, a second offense. Defendant filed a motion for resentencing and asserted that the second offense statute could not be applied because conviction thereunder was limited to a prior conviction under the unconstitutional first offense statute, § 32(a). The court stated that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32(b), was not dependent on the portion of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32(a), that had been held unconstitutional. The court stated that the penalty provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32(b), were clear and unambiguous. The court stated that defendant's conduct in distributing heroin after prior convictions for heroin offenses fell within the plain meaning of § 32(b), and that he was subject to sentencing under the enhanced penalties provisions of § 32(b). The court held that the sanctions enumerated in § 32(b) were not unconstitutional and that the defendant was not entitled to resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for resentencing.

Opinion of Justices to Senate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


390 Mass. 1201; 458 N.E.2d 1192; 1984 Mass. LEXIS 1262



January 3, 1984 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] We answer the first question, as we have limited it, "No." We answer the second question, "No."


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Massachusetts Senate submitted a question concerning a proposed law that would insert the words "sexual preference" into Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, §§ 92A, 98, providing criminal penalties for discrimination. The question was whether the proposed law lacked sufficient definiteness to meet the requirement of Mass. Const., Declaration of Rights art. XII that a stated criminal sanction convey a definite warning of proscribed conduct.


OVERVIEW: The court ruled that the words "sexual preference" were not unconstitutionally vague with reference to the standards established under article 12 of the Declaration of Rights. The court noted that the words had been used elsewhere intelligibly without definition. Further, words could acquire sufficiently definite meaning through judicial use and interpretation. The court had used the phrase in recent years. Accordingly, the proposed language was sufficiently definite to meet the standards in issue.


OUTCOME: The court held that the words "sexual preference" did not lack sufficient definiteness to meet the requirement of the Declaration of Rights of the Massachusetts Constitution.

Paisner v. Attorney Gen.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


390 Mass. 593; 458 N.E.2d 734; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1787


November 9, 1983, Argued  
December 14, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on September 14, 1983.

The case was reported by Liacos, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens brought an action against defendant attorney general in the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging a decision of the attorney general not to certify an initiative petition. The trial court entered a preliminary injunction to allow the citizens to gather additional signatures. The case came to the court by way of reservation and report without decision.


OVERVIEW: The citizens presented an initiative petition that proposed significant changes to discrete aspects of the procedures conducted in the Massachusetts legislature. The attorney general declined to certify the petition because he ruled that the petition did not propose enactment of a "law" as required by Mass. Const. art. 48, the Initiative, II, § 3. The citizens commenced an action for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the decision of the attorney general and his authority to have made such decision. In upholding the attorney general's decision, the court ruled that the attorney general had the authority to decline to certify the petition and that the petition did not propose a proper subject for the popular initiative. The court reasoned that where the petition was aimed at the internal procedures of the branches of the legislature, that indicated that the petition was one that established "rules" rather than "laws" because its principal purpose was to order the internal operations of the state senate and house rather than to alter the legal duties of persons outside the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the preliminary injunction, and it upheld the attorney general's authority and decision not to certify an initiative petition presented by the citizens.

Real v. Superintendent, Massachusetts Correctional Institution


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


390 Mass. 399; 456 N.E.2d 1111; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1748


March 10, 1983, Argued  
November 10, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 8, 1982, and May 4, 1982, respectively.

The cases were heard by Mitchell, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.

The case was submitted on briefs.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On its own initiative, the court ordered direct appellate review of a judgement of the superior court department (Massachusetts) construing plaintiff's habeas corpus petitions as complaints for declaratory judgment and declaring that plaintiff's due process rights were violated by procedures instituted by defendant correctional department's hearing board, thus invalidating the board's confinement of plaintiff to administrative segregation.


OVERVIEW: The board denied plaintiff's request for two inmates as witnesses in his defense at a disciplinary hearing. He was found guilty of the disciplinary infractions and confined to administrative segregation. The court held that although plaintiff filed petitions for writs of habeas corpus, his challenge to the constitutionality of the regulations pertaining to the right to call witnesses as set forth in Mass. Regs. Code tit. 103, § 430.14(6) properly stated a claim for declaratory relief. The court concluded that the failure of § 430.14 to require an explanation for the denial of plaintiff's witnesses abridged his federal due process rights. Accordingly, the trial judge properly concluded that the sanctions resulting from a constitutionally flawed disciplinary hearing were invalid, and correctly ordered the return of plaintiff's good time credits. While declining to reach the question whether the statutes and regulations create a protected liberty interest respecting administrative segregation, the court concluded that the trial judge improperly ordered return of plaintiff to the general prison population as a form of declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: To the extent that the trial judge's form of relief in entering two judgments, one returning plaintiff to the general prison population and one restoring good time credits, was wrong, the court reversed the judgments and remanded the case for an entry of judgment declaring the rights of plaintiff and ordering relief consistent with the opinion.

Lamoureux v. Superintendent, Massachusetts Correctional Institution


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

March 10, 1983, Argued  
November 10, 1983, Decided

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 4, 1982.

The case was heard by Mitchell, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.

The case was submitted on briefs.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State sought a stay of judgment pending appeal, which was granted by a Justice of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts). The court transferred the case from the Appeals Court on its own motion. The underlying question was whether plaintiff inmate was denied due process by the corrections department in the disciplinary hearing on his administrative segregation.


OVERVIEW: The inmate in a state correction facility filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, contending that he was denied the protection of due process of law in a disciplinary hearing in which the disciplinary board of the State's Department of Correction relied on informant information in finding the inmate guilty of the alleged misconduct. The inmate lost good time credit and was placed in administrative segregation. In affirming the part of the order that returned the inmate's good time credits, the court held that the State regulations governing the use of informant information in disciplinary proceedings did not provide adequate precautions to protect the accused's Federal due process rights against potential abuse of informant information. In reversing the part of the order that returned the inmate to the general population, the court found that the procedures governing the inmate's administrative segregation were sufficient to satisfy due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the lower court's order that adjusted the inmate's good time credits. It reversed and remanded the portion of the judgment removing the inmate from administrative segregation.

Commonwealth v. Bongarzone


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


390 Mass. 326; 455 N.E.2d 1183; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1716


May 2, 1983, Argued  
October 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 17, 1981.

A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Irwin, J., and the cases were tried before Roger J. Donahue, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for violating the marihuana trafficking statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(a)(2), from a Massachusetts trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted for violating the marihuana trafficking statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(a)(2). Defendants appealed their convictions on the ground that the indictments should have been dismissed because a police officer gave false testimony before the grand jury; the trial judge should have granted motions to sever; the substantive or penalty provisions of the statute were invalid; the trial judge failed to instruct the jury correctly; and the motion to suppress evidence should have been granted. The court reversed the indictments against two of the defendants. The court held that the defendants failed to show that the false testimony was calculated to procure any indictments. However, severance should have been allowed as to two of the defendants because while there was sufficient evidence from independent sources to support findings against the defendants concerning possession, the error of allowing one of the defendant's statements was not harmless. Thus, the court held that the error required reversal because absent those statements, the jury may have retained some doubt, especially as to whether the two defendants possessed the marihuana jointly.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the indictments against two of the defendants.

 

363 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Bianco


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


390 Mass. 254; 454 N.E.2d 901; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1680


June 13, 1983, Argued  
September 27, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Berkshire.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 9, 1981.

The cases were tried before Simons, J., who ordered the indictments placed on file. After the decision of this court in 388 Mass. 358 (1983), sentences were imposed by him.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.

The case was submitted on briefs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Seven defendants were convicted of assault and battery following a jury trial in a Massachusetts superior court. The superior court sentenced defendants to 18 months imprisonment. Defendants sought review of their convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted on charges of involuntary manslaughter and assault and battery. The jury found defendants guilty as charged. The superior court sentenced them on the manslaughter convictions and filed the assault and battery convictions. The court vacated the manslaughter convictions and held that defendants were entitled to be discharged from, or sentenced on, their assault and battery convictions. The state filed motions for sentencing. The superior court granted the motion and sentenced each defendant to 18 months imprisonment. The court affirmed, holding (1) the superior court committed no error in removing the assault and battery indictments from the file, (2) defendants' right to be sentenced promptly was not violated because the superior court imposed the sentences only eight days after the remand, (3) the superior court's removal of the indictments from the file, and the subsequent imposition of the sentences, implicated no due process concerns, (4) there was no indication that the superior court considered the deaths in sentencing defendants, and (5) the sentences were not disproportionate to the crime because defendants' conduct was willful and deliberate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences on charges of assault and battery.

 

364 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Cepulonis v. Secretary of Commonwealth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 930; 452 N.E.2d 1137; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1625


March 9, 1983, Argued  
August 16, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 11, 1982.

The case was heard by Kelley, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court (Massachusetts) issued judgment for defendant state in plaintiff inmates' action challenging the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 51, §§ 42-47B and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 54, which required the inmates to appear in person to register to vote by absentee ballot.


OVERVIEW: Under the statutory framework requiring a voter wishing to vote by absentee ballot to register in person, an inmate in a municipality other than his own domicile was not able to register to vote while in prison. The inmates claimed that their inability to register to vote was an unconstitutional deprivation of their right to vote in state elections. The court reversed the judgment upholding the constitutionality of the statutes requiring registration in person for those inmates, who were domiciled in the state. Each state inmate who was a duly qualified, registered voter in a municipality had the constitutional right to vote in state elections. The state failed to present evidence that the statutes promoted a compelling state interest because there was no evidence that a statutory procedure could not be enacted that would guard against voter fraud while permitting the registration of the inmates. There was no basis for disenfranchising the inmates by failing to provide them with some form of registration procedure. The court refused to order affirmative relief, allowing the legislature to provide a process for registration according to the constitutional requisites.


OUTCOME: The judgment declaring that the statutes requiring persons to register in person in order to vote by absentee ballot was reversed.

Commonwealth v. United Books, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 888; 453 N.E.2d 406; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1621


April 6, 1983, Argued  
August 15, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Central Worcester Division of the District Court Department on January 22, 1982.

The case was tried before Kelleher, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Verdict set aside.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Central Worcester Division of the District Court (Massachusetts), which convicted him of disseminating obscene matter in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29. Defendant contended that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29 was unconstitutional under the state and federal constitutions and that the trial court erred with regard to several evidentiary rulings and portions of the jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: The court found that defendant failed to meet its heavy burden of demonstrating the unconstitutionality of the obscenity statutes and that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 31 was not unconstitutionally vague. The court determined that defendant's allegations that attitudes varied with individual differences among viewers were insufficient to prove that there were no statewide standards of patent offensiveness. The court rejected defendant's argument that differing verdicts on other complaints against it involving allegedly comparable films revealed that there were no statewide standards. The court rejected the state's contention that defendant was required to make an offer of proof when the testimony of a defense expert was excluded based on the judge's determination that the expert was not qualified. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for a new trial finding that the trial court's exclusion of the expert's testimony on the artistic value of the subject material constituted reversible error. The court found that defendant's remaining contentions were meritless and the trial court did not err with regard to the challenged evidentiary issues and jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, set aside defendant's conviction, and remanded for a new trial. The court found that the exclusion of expert testimony regarding the artistic value of the allegedly obscene material constituted reversible error.

Commonwealth v. Dane Entertainment Services, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 902; 452 N.E.2d 1126; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1622


April 6, 1983, Argued  
August 15, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Chelsea Division of the District Court Department on February 26, 1981.

On appeal to the jury session of the Boston Municipal Court Department the case was tried before Colicchio, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation was convicted of possessing obscene matter with intent to disseminate it in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29 in the Boston Municipal Court (Massachusetts) based on a film shown at defendant's movie theatre. The corporation appealed its conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court held that: (1) the fact that many citizens of the commonwealth viewed a variety of X-rated materials did not mean that there was no rational basis for the Legislature to conclude that there were ascertainable statewide standards and defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint was properly denied; (2) a magistrate did not have to view the film in order to find probable cause to seize it and a properly detailed affidavit provided a sufficient factual basis to allow a magistrate to focus searchingly on the question whether there was probable cause to believe that the film was obscene; (3) any error in the admission of a movie poster was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt; (4) the trial court properly denied defendant's pretrial motion to sever the trial; (5) comparison evidence was admissible in the trial judge's discretion if the proper foundation was laid; (6) the trial court properly prohibited defense counsel from making reference to censorship; and (7) defendant was not prejudiced by defense counsel's inability to refer to the First Amendment and freedom of speech in his closing argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's obscenity conviction.

Commonwealth v. Beverly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 866; 452 N.E.2d 1112; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1618


March 7, 1983, Argued  
August 12, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on October 7, 1980.

The cases were tried before Alberti, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgments of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which convicted them of unlawfully and knowingly possessing, with intent to distribute, heroin in excess of two hundred grams, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(c). Defendants each were sentenced to 15 years in prison pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(c)(3). The court granted a request for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: When police officers entered defendants' apartment pursuant to a search warrant, one defendant put a glassine bag containing heroin in her mouth and the other defendant threw a paint can filled with glassine bags of heroin out the window. The court found that the indictment correctly stated the crime charged and that defendants were not prejudiced in their defense. The court held that a mixture of heroin and other substances that weighed more than 200 grams was sufficient to convict defendants of the crime charged. A defense counsel's pending disciplinary proceeding did not deny a defendant effective assistance of counsel. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to warrant the jury's finding beyond a reasonable doubt that both defendants possessed, with intent to distribute, the heroin that was contained in the paint can that was thrown out the window. The court held that, taken as a whole, the trial court's charge to the jury on reasonable doubt was sufficient. The court held that the trial court was required to resentence defendants pursuant to the general provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(c) because Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(c)(3) was no longer valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of unlawfully and knowingly possessing, with intent to distribute, in excess of two hundred grams of heroin. The court vacated the sentences and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

Massachusetts Auto. Rating & Acci. Prevention Bureau v. Commissioner of Ins.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 824; 453 N.E.2d 381; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1616


May 4, 1983, Argued  
August 4, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 12, 1983.

The cases were reported by Abrams, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, insurance bureau and insurance companies, challenged a decision from defendant Commissioner of Insurance, which fixed and established automobile insurance rates for a particular year.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against the commissioner alleging automobile insurance rates set by the commissioner were not adequate, just, reasonable, and nondiscriminatory as required by Mass. Gen. L. cg. 175, § 113B. Plaintiffs also alleged the rates were unconstitutional because they were confiscatory. The court upheld the commissioner's decision in part and remanded in part. The court determined the commissioner did not abuse its discretion by modifying the statutory/regulatory company investment model to include a more realistic tax rate because evidence indicated the new tax rate provided a more precise calculation of the insurance companies' investment profits. The court held the commissioner's use of a surplus allocation model that resulted in a different rate of return was not erroneous because the actual riskiness of investing in the various lines of insurance was not comparable. The court concluded the commissioner's assumption that the Hospital Cost Containment Act would result in a reduction in hospital costs was not reasonably supported by the evidence because the Act did not specifically provide for a reduction and the effect of the Act was not immediately known.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the commissioner's decision with respect to the allowance for profits. The court remanded for an entry of a judgment reversing the decision of the commissioner and directing him to fix and establish the automobile insurance rates, redetermining the allowance for losses in accordance with the opinion.

Commonwealth v. Elder


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 7, 1980.

The cases were heard by O'Neil, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court, Hampden County (Massachusetts) of rape and abuse of a minor child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape and abuse of a minor child. Finally, the trial judge did not err in excluding evidence of the complainant's prior sexual conduct as relevant evidence of bias or nonvirginity.


OUTCOME: The rape and abuse of a minor child convictions were affirmed.

Taunton Eastern Little League v. Taunton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 719; 452 N.E.2d 211; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1578


March 8, 1983, Argued  
July 18, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 24, 1981.

The case was heard by Staff, J., a District Court judge sitting under statutory authority.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which upheld the decision of defendant municipal council to rescind its approval of the applicant's request for a beano license. The licensee had filed an action under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 249, § 4, seeking to quash the council's rescission decision on the ground that the decision violated the Establishment Clause of the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The council granted the applicant's request under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 10, § 38 for a beano license to conduct a beano game. Before it was delivered to the applicant, on the petition of the members of a parish, which had a license to conduct a beano game on the same day, the council rescinded its approval. It stated that the rescission was to protect the revenues, which were used to support the parish's private, grammar school, received from the games, and to prevent an influx of students and closure of the grammar school. The applicant sought to quash the council's decision under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 249, § 4 on First Amendment grounds. The trial court upheld the decision. On direct appellate review, the court affirmed the judgment, held that, under a three-part test, the rescission did not result in an impermissible government entanglement with religion under the Establishment Clause, and found that: (1) the rescission had a secular purpose because it was to prevent a substantial impact from the influx of students if the grammar school was to close; and (2) there was no advancement of religion because the decision did not provide public funds to the parish or to the school.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment upholding the council's decision to rescind its approval of the applicant's request for a beano license, in the applicant's action against the council seeking to quash the council's decision.

Habeeb v. Retirement Bd. of Quincy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 634; 451 N.E.2d 704; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1569


April 7, 1983, Argued  
July 8, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 23, 1981.

The case was heard by Abrams, J., on motion for summary judgment.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Superior Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff veteran sought review of the judgment by the Massachusetts Appeals Court, which reversed the trial court's judgment for the veteran in his declaratory action against defendant city retirement board. The trial court had held that the veteran's national guard service did not qualify as employment under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 60 as his service occurred prior to July 1, 1939, and thus, the veteran was entitled to retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: The veteran, who was a public school teacher for more than 30 years within the state, sought a declaratory judgment that his service in the Massachusetts National Guard prior July 1, 1939, did not qualify as benefit prohibiting employment within the meaning of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 60. Section 60 barred veterans from receiving noncontributory retirement benefits if their public employment began after June 30, 1939. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment that the service did not qualify as employment and held that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 33, § 94 had no applicability to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, §§ 56 - 60. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the veteran. The court held that although the legislative history of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 33, §§ 88 and 94 indicated that officers and enlisted persons were to be included in the bar to benefits enumerated in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 60, National Guard members were not "employees" within the meaning of the law. Thus, the veteran, who performed service as a national guardsman, was not an employee was not covered by the bar to noncontributory retirement benefits under § 60.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the veteran in his declaratory action against the board for noncontributory retirement benefits.

 

372 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rhodes


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 641; 451 N.E.2d 1151; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1570


May 2, 1983, Argued  
July 8, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Boston Municipal Court Department on July 10, 1981.

On appeal to the jury session of that court, a motion to dismiss was heard by Cratsley, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty in the district court of unlawfully carrying a firearm without a license, Mass. Gen. Laws § ch. 269, § 10(a). He appealed to the jury session of the Boston Municipal Court (Massachusetts). The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint. The state appealed pursuant to Mass. R. Crim. P. 15(a)(3)(b).


OVERVIEW: The conviction was based on defendant's carrying on his person a .177 caliber air-powered BB pistol. The court affirmed and held that Mass. Gen. Laws § ch. 269, § 12B contained the exclusive regulatory scheme for the use of air rifles and BB guns, and no violation of that law had been charged. Section 12B barred minors from possessing BB guns without an adult or proper license. For defendant to have been found in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 10(a), none of the four exceptions to the statute could have applied. But one exception, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 10(a)(4), related to those who carried an air-rifle or BB gun within the requirements of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 12B. Section 12B, however, did not regulate possession of BB guns by adults. Thus, an adult in possession of an air gun could not have been in violation of § 12B. To have applied, § 12B to adults would have unreasonably subjected adults to imprisonment for taking away from a minor a BB gun the minor was using dangerously unless that adult fell within one of the other three exceptions to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 10(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which dismissed the charges against defendant for unlawfully carrying a firearm without a license.

La Pointe v. License Bd. of Worcester


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 454; 451 N.E.2d 112; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1530


February 8, 1983, Argued  
June 14, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 6, 1981.

The case was heard by Meagher, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff junk dealer sought review of an order of the Superior Court (Massachusetts) that affirmed a decision of defendant License Board of Worcester (board) revoking the junk dealer's license to deal in junk, old metals, and secondhand articles. The junk dealer also requested that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 54, and City of Worcester, Mass., Rev. Ordinances ch. 12 (1974), be declared unconstitutional for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: In revoking the junk dealer's license, the board determined that stolen merchandise was purchased which, with reasonable proper investigation, could have been determined to be stolen, and that the junk dealer had failed to keep proper and complete records as required by City of Worcester, Mass., Rev. The statute was not impermissibly vague because it provided the junk dealer with sufficient notice of his duties as a licensee and the board with sufficient guidelines for its decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that upheld the board's decision to revoke the junk dealer's license.

Marshfield Family Skateland, Inc. v. Marshfield


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 436; 450 N.E.2d 605; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1528


February 10, 1983, Argued  
June 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 12, August 16, September 1, and October 6, 1982.

The cases were consolidated for trial and were heard by Ford, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant merchants challenged consolidated judgments from the Plymouth Superior Court (Massachusetts), which denied injunctive relief against the enforcement of General By-Law No. 48, which was a total prohibition by appellee town on the commercial operation of coin-activated amusement devices. The town agreed not to undertake any enforcement proceedings pending appeal.


OVERVIEW:  Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 177A (1948) permitted the use of automatic amusement devices, which were previously illegal lotteries, if duly licensed and for amusement only. The court asserted that General By-Law No. 48 did not prevent that purpose from being achieved, asserting that a licensing board, which could not go beyond its statutory grant and adopt a broad policy of denying all licenses, was different from a local community, which could supplement the statutes as long as its by-laws were not inconsistent with state law and, therefore, could totally prohibit legal business activities within its borders. The court asserted that the legislative intent was to permit automatic amusement devices, but not to require them. The court found that video games did not contain sufficient communicative elements to be entitled to free speech protection. The court did not find the by-law overbroad, asserting that the right to pursue a business was not a fundamental right warranting strict scrutiny, but only the rational basis test, which the by-law passed, as it was rationally related to public safety. The by-law furthered a legitimate state interest, and the court affirmed the judgments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments. The basis for the classification was not more fanciful than real, nor was it arbitrary or irrational and, therefore, the court could not invalidate it. The court rejected the merchants' arguments based on both equal protection and due process and upheld the validity of the by-law.

Thomas v. Massachusetts Bay Transp. Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 408; 450 N.E.2d 600; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1525


February 7, 1983, Argued  
June 10, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Dorchester Division of the District Court Department on March 8, 1982.

Upon removal to the Superior Court Department, a motion to dismiss was heard by Linscott, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger appealed a decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendant Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority (MBTA) in the passenger's contract action against the MBTA.


OVERVIEW: The passenger filed a complaint against the MBTA alleging that she was a passenger on the MBTA's trolley when she was injured as a result of the negligence of its employees. The passenger filed a motion for leave to amend her complaint to make it clear that she sought recovery under contract law. In response, the MBTA argued that the passenger's claim violated the statute of limitations under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 161A, § 21. The judge failed to consider the passenger's motion for leave to file an amended complaint and granted the MBTA's motion to dismiss. The superior court denied the passenger's subsequent motion to set aside its order. The passenger appealed the superior court's decision. She argued that § 21 referred to tort liability. She maintained that she was excluded from § 21 because she sought recovery for personal injuries in contract. On appeal, the court affirmed the superior court's decision. The court held that § 21 applied to actions in contract for personal injuries. The court concluded that that § 21 contained the only statute of limitations applicable to a claim for personal injuries against the MBTA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that granted the MBTA's motion to dismiss the passenger's contract action to recover damages for her personal injuries.

Hearn v. Massachusetts Bay Transp. Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 404; 450 N.E.2d 602; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1524


February 7, 1983, Argued  
June 10, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 14, 1982.

A motion to dismiss was heard by Carey, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted defendant transportation authority's motion to dismiss on the ground of the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiff was struck by a bus, the property of the transportation authority. Approximately two years and ten months after the accident, he filed a complaint against the transportation authority alleging the bus operator's negligence and seeking damages for his resultant injuries. The action was dismissed because it was brought after the two year statute of limitations for bring actions against the transportation authority had expired. Plaintiff appealed arguing that he had been denied the equal protection of the laws guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment because, by the wholly adventitious misfortune of being struck by the transportation authority bus, he was required to bring his action within a period of time which was one year shorter than would be required if he had been struck by any other motor vehicle. The court rejected this argument. It found that the legislature could have concluded that there was a rational basis for treating the transportation authority differently from others because of its special public obligations. Thus, the shorter statute of limitations for actions brought against the transportation authority was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing plaintiff's personal injury action was affirmed.
