Page v. Commissioner of Revenue


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 388; 450 N.E.2d 590; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1476; 36 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 941


April 4, 1983, Argued  
June 8, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth.

Civil action commenced in the Plymouth Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on February 17, 1982.

Questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by Lawton, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action came before the court on a reservation and report by the Probate and Family Court Department, Plymouth County (Massachusetts), of certain questions of law arising from plaintiff executor's petition for an abatement of estate taxes assessed by defendant commissioner of revenue (commissioner). The probate and family court reported the questions pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 215, § 13.


OVERVIEW: The executor challenged the commissioner's decision to include in decedent's taxable estate securities that were held by a trust company in Maryland. The executor also challenged that commissioner's decision to include the value of a gift made in contemplation of death as part of the Massachusetts gross estate. The decedent, who died while domiciled in Massachusetts, made the gift of securities 30 months before her death while she was domiciled in Maryland. The court concluded that the commissioner properly included the securities and the transfer as part of the Massachusetts estate. The court held that investment securities within the meaning of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 106, § 8-102(1), which were physically held by a bank in Maryland, were not tangible personal property having an actual situs outside the commonwealth for purposes of ch. 65C, § 1(f), the estate tax statute. The court also held that the gift in contemplation of death was properly the object of the Massachusetts estate tax. The court found no constitutional infirmity in the estate tax statute and no constitutional impediment to including the gift in the Massachusetts taxable estate.


OUTCOME: The court considered the questions reported by the probate and family court and concluded that the commissioner was correct to include securities held by a trust company in Maryland in decedent's estate. The court also concluded that the commissioner was correct to include the value of a gift made in contemplation of death as part of the Massachusetts gross estate and that the executor, therefore, was not entitled to an abatement.

 

379 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Murphy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 316; 451 N.E.2d 95; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1470


March 7, 1983, Argued  
June 7, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Third Eastern Middlesex Division of the District Court Department on September 20, 1982.

A motion for amendment of the complaint was heard by Nixon, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cambridge District Court (Massachusetts) struck a portion of the complaint against defendant which referred to a prior assignment to an alcohol education program and opted to treat the current driving while intoxicated charge as a first offense. The commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving while intoxicated previously. That charge resulted in assignment to an alcohol education program and once that program was completed the guilty findings were revoked. Defendant was later charged with a subsequent driving while under the influence charge, and the issue became whether defendant's prior assignment to an alcohol education program could constitutionally be the basis for imposing the enhanced penalties prescribed by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24(1)(a)(1) if he was convicted on the latter charge. Defendant admitted to sufficient facts to warrant a finding of guilty on the first charge, and a finding of guilty was entered, but the guilty finding was revoked upon completion of the education program. Defendant opposed any enhanced sentence based largely on ex post facto principles and also relied on due process of law considerations. The court reversed the trial court ruling and found an enhanced sentence proper, however, because the court found that persons who admitted guilt fell within the standards set forth in § 24(1)(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court order reducing the complaint against defendant because the court found that the prior assignment to an education program was sufficient so that an enhanced penalty was proper following a subsequent driving while intoxicated conviction.

 

380 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Adams


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 265; 450 N.E.2d 149; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1465


January 4, 1983, Argued  
May 18, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Brockton Division of the District Court Department on May 28, 1980.

The case was heard in the Fourth Plymouth Division by Collari, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Finding set aside.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wareham District Court (Massachusetts) convicted defendant of open and gross lewdness and lascivious behavior under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 16. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after a witness observed him masturbating while driving on a public way. After initially choosing a jury trial, defendant waived it and was tried before the bench. He was convicted of open and gross lewdness and lascivious behavior. Defendant appealed. The court reversed the conviction. The commonwealth did not demonstrate that defendant was fully advised of his Miranda rights. Specifically, the officer's testimony did not show that defendant was advised that any statements he made could be used against him, which was an absolute prerequisite to interrogation. Because defendant was not given his full Miranda rights, his statements should not have been admitted in evidence. Defendant's alleged conduct was included under the commonly understood meaning of open and gross lewdness and lascivious behavior so as to give him fair warning that his conduct was proscribed. Thus, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The protective provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 218, § 27A (d) were not applicable here because defendant did not originally choose a bench trial. Thus, the judge properly declined to recuse himself.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction, and a new trial was granted.

 

381 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Stowell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 171; 449 N.E.2d 357; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1457


January 6, 1983, Argued  
May 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester.

Complaint received and sworn to in the Central Worcester Division of the District Court Department on October 14, 1980.

On appeal to the jury session, a motion to dismiss was heard by Greenberg, J., and questions of law were reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of adultery in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 14. Prior to trial, defendant filed a motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to her conduct. The trial court reported the case to the Appeals Court (Massachusetts). Subsequently, the court granted defendant's application for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: Police officers observed defendant having sexual intercourse with another person in a van. Both occupants were adults and told the officers that they were married but not to each other. Defendant argued that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 14 was unconstitutional on its face because it violated the fundamental right of privacy guaranteed by the United States Constitution. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional on its face. There was no fundamental personal privacy right implicit in the concept of ordered liberty barring the prosecution of consenting adults committing adultery in private. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant's conduct. The court took judicial notice that the act of adultery frequently had a destructive impact on the marital relationship and was a factor in many divorces. The state had a right to regulate the institution of marriage under its police power as long as it did not infringe on fundamental rights.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Massachusetts adultery statute was not unconstitutional on its face, that it was not unconstitutional as applied to the facts of the case, and that it was proper to have applied it to consensual acts between adults in private.

 

382 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Decker v. Black & Decker Mfg. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


389 Mass. 35; 449 N.E.2d 641; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1416; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P9762


January 5, 1983, Argued  
April 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Berkshire.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court on August 16, 1976.

A motion by the third-party defendant for summary judgment was heard by Urbano, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, manufacturer and supplier, appealed from the grant of summary judgment by the Superior Court (Massachusetts) in favor of third-party defendant employer in defendants attempt to seek indemnity from third-party.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee brought a negligence action against defendants, manufacturer and supplier, for injuries he suffered at work while using one of defendants' products. Third-party defendant employer sought to dismiss defendant's third-party complaint that alleged it had impliedly agreed to indemnify defendants for any losses they incurred as a result of plaintiff's injuries. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of third-party defendant. On appeal, the court held that there was no contract between defendants and third-party defendant. The only contract between the parties was an agreement for sale of the product, and a sales agreement alone was not a sufficient basis on which to imply a contractual obligation on the part of third-party defendant to indemnify defendants for damages paid to plaintiff. Nor was there any evidence that the relationship between the parties was a special relationship that carried with it an obligation to indemnify defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of third party defendant employer because there was no evidence that third-party defendant had agreed to indemnify defendants, manufacturer and supplier, in plaintiff employee's negligence action.

 

383 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. B & W Transp., Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


388 Mass. 799; 448 N.E.2d 728; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1404


December 7, 1982, Argued  
April 15, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester.

Complaints received and sworn to in the Western Hampden Division of the District Court Department on September 24, 1980; in the First Southern Worcester Division of the District Court Department on December 9, 1980, April 24, 1981, May 6, 1981, June 11, 1981, and June 23, 1981; and in the Central Worcester Division of the District Court Department on May 1, 1981.

The cases were heard in the Central Worcester Division of the District Court Department by Greenberg, J., on a motion to dismiss.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed from an order of the Central Worcester Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendant interstate common carriers and held that Mass. Regs. Code tit. 730, § 4.02(1978), which provided that a tandem tractor trailer using the Massachusetts Turnpike could not exceed a total maximum gross weight of 127,400 pounds, was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that all the vehicles cited exceeded the regulation's gross-weight limitations and that the primary purpose of the administrative regulations was to preserve the integrity and safety of bridges under the control of the turnpike authority. Because the turnpike authority's regulation was supported by evidence that it preserved the safety and integrity of the turnpike bridges, the regulation bore a reasonable relation to its goal, and the carriers' equal protection claim failed. The Commonwealth demonstrated that the regulation was not arbitrary but was rationally related to the purpose of preventing excessive stress on the turnpike's long-span bridges. The fact that the tandem gross-weight limitation was not drawn with "mathematical precision" or that a better means of protection might have been available was not fatal. Therefore, the regulation did not violate due process. The regulation was clear that trucks with gross weights in excess of the 127,400-pound limitation were forbidden, therefore the regulation was not unconstitutionally vague. Also, there was no showing that the regulation discriminated against or substantially burdened interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the cases for trial.

 

384 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Franklin v. Spadafora


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


388 Mass. 764; 447 N.E.2d 1244; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1364; 39 A.L.R.4th 77


January 3, 1983, Argued  
April 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 18, 1981.

The case was heard by Hallisey, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which entered judgment in favor of defendant trustees and upheld a condominium trust by-law limiting to two the number of units which could be owned by any one person or entity. The Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.


OVERVIEW: The trustees amended the by-laws of the condominium trust limiting the number of units that could be owned by any one person or entity. The owners, who were in the midst of a sale to one another, sought declaratory relief. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the trustees. The by-law was a reasonable restraint on alienation because the trustees possessed an interest in the land. Although the amendment was not limited in duration, it could be amended at any time by the trustees, thereby creating a reasonable duration on the whole. The by-law had a worthwhile purpose in promoting continuity, and only a minute number of persons would be affected. The curtailment of the power of alienation was so slight that no social danger was implicated. The amendment did not pose a constitutional problem because purchase within the condominium was voluntary, and strict scrutiny was not required where no fundamental rights were impinged upon. The by-law amendment served a legitimate purpose and was rationally related to the achievement of that purpose, thus, it passed constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the trustees.

Borden, Inc. v. Commissioner of Public Health


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


388 Mass. 707; 448 N.E.2d 367; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1360; 38 A.L.R.4th 1036


November 1, 1982, Argued  
April 12, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by C.P. Chemical Co. v. Commissioner of Public Health, 464 U.S. 923, 78 L. Ed. 2d 296, 104 S. Ct. 323, 1983 U.S. LEXIS 2034 (1983)
Writ of certiorari denied Formaldehyde Institute, Inc. v. Frechette, 464 U.S. 936, 78 L. Ed. 2d 312, 104 S. Ct. 345, 1983 U.S. LEXIS 2125 (1983)
Related proceeding at Anderson Insulation Co. v. Department of Pub. Health, 39 Mass. App. Ct. 1118, 659 N.E.2d 288, 1995 Mass. App. LEXIS 904 (1995)
Related proceeding at Anderson Insulation Co. v. Department of Pub. Health, 47 Mass. App. Ct. 1107, 713 N.E.2d 404, 1999 Mass. App. LEXIS 899 (1999)
Related proceeding at Anderson Insulation Co. v. Department of Pub. Health, 48 Mass. App. Ct. 80, 717 N.E.2d 662, 1999 Mass. App. LEXIS 1104 (1999)
Related proceeding at Anderson Insulation Co. v. Dep't of Pub. Health, 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 937 (Mass. App. Ct., Aug. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department, two on November 16, 1979, and one each on May 9, 1980, February 9, 1981, and July 31, 1981.

The cases were heard by Ronan, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted requests for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Massachusetts Commissioner of Public Health was granted a direct appeal from the decisions of the Suffolk County Superior Court (Massachusetts) that ruled in favor of appellees, manufacturers, dealers, and installers of urea-formaldehyde foamed-in-place insulation (UFFI), in consolidated cases that invalidated in their entirety the regulations that banned UFFI.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Massachusetts Commissioner of Public Health Commissioner promulgated regulations that banned the sale, distribution, and all uses of urea-formaldehyde foamed-in-place insulation (UFFI) in the Commonwealth, and that required the manufacturers, dealers, and installers of UFFI to remove it from any building where it was installed, restore the house or other building, and refund the purchase price. Appellee manufacturers, dealers, and installers of UFFI challenged the regulations. The lower court invalidated the regulations in their entirety. The court allowed appellant to bring a direct appeal. The court concluded that the lower court erred in holding that the commissioner's ban and repurchase regulations were illegal, arbitrary, and capricious. The court upheld the regulations with one exception. Insofar as the regulations did not require the legal referee to conduct an adjudicatory hearing with respect to whether the named supplier in fact supplied the UFFI to be repurchased, the court concluded that the regulations violated due process principles. The judgments of the lower court were reversed and remanded with instructions to grant declaratory relief .


OUTCOME: Upon direct appellate review, the court reversed the decisions of the lower court that held that the urea-formaldehyde foamed-in-place insulation ban and repurchase regulations promulgated by appellant Massachusetts Commissioner of Public Health were illegal, arbitrary, and capricious. The court remanded the case with directions to grant declaratory relief consistent with this decision.

Commonwealth v. Walter


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


388 Mass. 460; 446 N.E.2d 707; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1312


December 6, 1982, Argued  
March 14, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Complaints received and sworn to in the Third Eastern Middlesex Division of the District Court Department on February 25, 1981.

In the jury session, the cases were tried before Murphy, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Third Eastern Middlesex Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted her, after a jury trial, of engaging in common, indiscriminate sexual activity for hire, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53, and of advertising the business of massage without being licensed, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 51.


OVERVIEW: A police officer, under his detective's supervision, called a number advertising massage and went to defendant's apartment to receive a massage. After taking payment from him, she massaged him, then took off her shirt and began to massage his genitals. The officer arrested her and she was convicted after trial. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court concluded that prostitution under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53 includes performing masturbation on someone else with the hands. The court found that defendant's right to privacy was not violated because commercial sex acts were not protected as private, sexual activity would be. The court concluded that § 53 was not vague because a person of common intelligence would know that masturbation was included in the definition of sexual activity. Relating to defendant's conviction under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 51, the court concluded that the advertisement was properly admitted as evidence that the officer had called the number, that defendant had answered and met with the officer, and that defendant was the woman the officer met, rather than to prove the truth of the advertisements contents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of prostitution and of advertising massage without a license.

Langone v. Secretary of Commonwealth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


388 Mass. 185; 446 N.E.2d 43; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1277


June 29, 1982, Argued  
February 16, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 2, 1982.

On transfer to the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk questions of law were reported by Liacos, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, candidate and his supporters (candidate), brought an action against defendant Secretary of the Commonwealth (secretary) and alleged that by refusing to print the candidate's name on the Democratic state party primary ballot, the secretary violated the candidate's state and constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: This action arose after the secretary, pursuant to Article Six, Section III of the Charter of the Democratic Party of the Commonwealth, refused to place the candidate's name on the ballot because he had not received at least 15 percent of the vote at the Democratic Convention. The candidate argued that as he had complied with the state statutory requirements, he was entitled to have his name appear on the ballot. The court found that as Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 53 (the statute) was not expressly preemptive of the party rule and constitutional difficulties would be avoided by permitting the party rules to supplement the statute. The court concluded that the statute would substantially infringe the Democratic party's fundamental right of association if it eliminated the 15 precent rule, thus necessitating strict scrutiny, which it did not survive. The court determined that the statute as augmented by the 15 percent rule would not deprive the candidate or voters of rights of free speech and association guaranteed to them by the U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV or state law because the statute as supplemented was rationally related to legitimate state interests.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the secretary's decision to not place the candidate's name on the ballot.

 

388 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Graham


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


388 Mass. 115; 445 N.E.2d 1043; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1255


November 3, 1982, Argued  
January 31, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 20, 1981.

Questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by Linscott, J. The Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted by a grand jury for a violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 7, which prohibited anyone from deriving support and maintenance from the earnings of a prostitute. The indictment was found and returned in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictment on double jeopardy grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried, convicted, and sentenced for violating § 7 in a municipal court. Subsequently, the commonwealth filed a motion to vacate the conviction on the ground that the municipal court lacked jurisdiction to try the felony case. The motion was granted and the grand jury indicted defendant for the same offense in the superior court. On appeal, the court remanded the case with instructions for the superior court to dismiss the indictment. The court held that further prosecution by the superior court was barred by the constitutional double jeopardy provisions because a trial on the merits was conducted by the municipal court. The court held that the municipal court and the commonwealth's district courts had original subject matter jurisdiction, concurrent with the superior court, over the felony described in § 7. The court found that the fact that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 218, § 27 prohibited the municipal court from sentencing a felon to a state prison did not limit its jurisdiction over the § 7 offense.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case with instructions for the superior court to dismiss the indictment of defendant the offense of deriving support and maintenance from the earnings and the proceeds of a prostitute.

1001 Plays, Inc. v. Mayor of Boston


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 879; 444 N.E.2d 931; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1205


September 13, 1982, Argued  
January 11, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 15, 1981.

The case was heard by Hallisey, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff video arcade business appealed an order from Middlesex Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which affirmed the administrative decision of defendant, licensing division of the city mayor's office, to deny the business's application for a public amusements license under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 181, as amended by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 351, § 84 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The business presented its application to the division, which denied it on the basis of community opposition, unreasonable increases in traffic and disruptive conduct, and the lack of off-street parking. The business revised its application to present a smaller arcade with a decreased occupancy and video game capacity. The division again denied the license and rejected the business's proffered comparison with another area where an arcade was located. The business sought judicial review of the decision. The superior court affirmed the division's decision on the ground that substantial evidence supported the division's determinations that the proposed arcade would have increased traffic, noise, and the incidence of disruptive conduct. On appeal, the court noted that a license for an arcade might have been required under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, §177A as well. Using the substantial evidence test to examine the weight and sufficiency of the evidence, the court concluded that the division's evidentiary determinations were not unreasonable. The record contained no evidence presented by the business that was of such weight as to make the division's conclusions unwarranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court, holding that the division's decision to deny a license to operate an entertainment center to the business was supported by substantial evidence.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee commenced an action in the superior Court Department (Massachusetts), for declaratory relief, and for relief in the nature of certiorari against defendant, licensing commission. New England Merchants Nat'l Bank v. Groswold


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 822; 444 N.E.2d 359; 1983 Mass. LEXIS 1200


October 8, 1982, Argued  
January 5, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Petition filed in the Essex Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on June 22, 1981.

The case was heard by Macdougall, J.

Petition filed in the Suffolk Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on July 2, 1981.

The case was heard by Warner, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review of the first case, and consolidated the cases for appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant adopted relative, citing Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 210, § 8, appealed decisions of the Essex and Suffolk Divisions of the Probate and Family Court Department (Massachusetts), which issued orders striking her appearances and entered judgments ordering trust assets distributed entirely to defendant natural relative in an action by plaintiff trustee seeking to distribute the assets.


OVERVIEW: The adopted relative contended that the court should give effect to the modern and enlightened policy expressed in an amendment to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 210, § 8, of treating natural and adopted children equally, by retroactively applying the amendment to the case. The court affirmed the judgments. The court noted that passage of the amendment to § 8 did not impliedly repealed the prior statutory provisions which set forth a rule of construction concerning when adopted children would take. The court determined that the amendment, taken together with later amendments, indicated the legislature's intent to draw the date of the amendment as a bright line for application of § 8. The court stated that, assuming no constitutional impediments, it would not give retroactive effect to the policy of the amendment under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial courts striking the appearances of the adopted relative and ordering the distribution of trust proceeds to the natural relative in the trustee's actions seeking to distribute trust assets.

 

392 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Attorney Gen. v. Colleton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 790; 444 N.E.2d 915; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1819


October 4, 1982, Argued  
December 28, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 3, 1981.

The case was heard by Ronan, J.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Attorney General sought review of a decision of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which denied plaintiff's petition for an order to compel defendant to testify pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 93A, §6(7).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff Attorney General served a civil investigative demand on defendant, president of a yacht chartering company (company), for information related to possible unfair or deceptive acts in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 93A, § 2. Claiming protection under the federal and state constitutions, defendant refused to give answer any questions relating to the company unless granted immunity under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 233, § 20E. Petitioning for an order to compel defendant to testify, plaintiff argued that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 93A, § 6(7) granted immunity adequate to displace the constitutional privilege against self-incrimination. The petition was denied, and the court affirmed on appeal. The court determined that immunity under § 6(7), barred only the use of compelled testimony, directly or indirectly, in a narrow range of criminal prosecutions and still left defendant open to potential criminal prosecution as a consequence of a disclosure he might be called upon to make.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of plaintiff Attorney General's petition to compel defendant to testify, finding that the limited immunity offered by plaintiff was inadequate to displace defendant's constitutional privilege against self-incrimination.

 

393 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices to Senate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 1209; 443 N.E.2d 1293; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1820



December 27, 1982 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] We answer the first question, "No." We answer the second question "No," subject to what we have said concerning the lack of authority of a county to act in relation to cities and towns pursuant to the purported delegation of legislative power in § 13 (b) of the proposed act.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court submitted answers to the following questions propounded to it by the Senate of Massachusetts: 1) Would the enactment into law of a bill establishing procedures for the adoption of home rule charters by counties violate Mass. Const. amend. art. 19? 2) Would the enactment into law of the bill violate Mass. Const. amend. art. 89?


OVERVIEW: The bill provided that every county would have the power to adopt and amend a charter. It granted the counties the authority to assume any power that the general court could lawfully confer on a county. The court held that there was no inconsistency between the bill and Mass. Const. amend. art. 19. Article 19 empowered the general court to prescribe the term of office for sheriffs, registers of probate, and clerks of the courts, and the bill purported to limit terms of office to not more than four years. Article 19 in no way prevented such a legislative decision. The bill did not purport to affect any city or town individually but rather affected all cities and towns equally. Therefore, the general court had the power to enact the bill and the power was unaffected by § 8 of the Home Rule Amendment, Mass. Const. amend. art. 2. However, § 8 did prohibit a county from acting in relation to cities and towns pursuant to a purported delegation of blanket authority to legislate. The general court could empower the inhabitants of any county to erect a form of government, but its authority to act could not be given to counties by a non-specific delegation.


OUTCOME: The court answered no to the first question, finding that the enactment of the bill would not violate the Massachusetts Constitution. The court also answered no to the second question subject to what it said concerning the lack of authority of a county to act in relation to cities and towns pursuant to the purported delegation of legislative power in the proposed act.

 

394 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gagnon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 768; 443 N.E.2d 407; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1816



December 23, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department, one on February 18, 1981, and two on March 9, 1981.

Following its decision ante 567 (1982), the Supreme Judicial Court considered a petition for rehearing.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the court's decision on appeal from judgments finding defendants guilty of violations of Mass., Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32(a), the court granted the Commonwealth's petition for rehearing, to consider whether defendants could have been resentenced under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 34, which punished for possession of heroin.


OVERVIEW: The indictments of the Commonwealth charged defendants with knowing or intentional possession of heroin with the intent to manufacture, distribute, or dispense it. The court decided that the issue was whether defendants received adequate notice under the former Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32(a), of the penalty for their misconduct to afford them with due process. The court reversed the judgments against defendants under the indictments charging them with violating § 32(a), and set aside the superior court findings to the extent that defendants were convicted of those violations. The court remanded the cases to the superior court to render a dismissal of the indictments except as to the lesser included offense of possession of heroin. The court directed that defendants could have been held guilty of that offense and could have been sentenced under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 34, which penalized them for the possession of heroin. The court rejected a suggestion that precedent existed in support of the "rule of revival." The court found that applying the "rule of revival" was unconstitutional. The court found that application of the "rule of revival" was a form of judicial lawmaking.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments against defendants under the indictments asserting that they violated the former statute. The cases were remanded for entry of a dismissal of the indictments other than for the lesser included offense of possession of heroin. The court directed the resentencing of defendants under the new statute for the lesser included offense.

Raymond v. Board of Registration in Medicine


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 708; 443 N.E.2d 391; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1783; 34 A.L.R.4th 600


May 4, 1982, Argued  
December 8, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on August 12, 1981.

The case was reported by Liacos, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician sought review of an order of defendant Massachusetts Board of Registration in Medicine (board), which revoked his license to practice medicine pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 112, § 5 (1977) after he was convicted of illegal arms dealing.


OVERVIEW: The physician was convicted of illegal arms dealing in violation of federal law. The board revoked his license to practice medicine pursuant to ch. 112, § 5, finding that (1) the physician had been convicted of a crime; (2) he lacked good moral character; and (3) he engaged in conduct that undermined the public's confidence in the integrity of the medical profession. On appeal, the court affirmed the board's order. The court held that the board had the authority to revoke the physician's license pursuant to ch. 112, § 5, and that, although the crime did not relate to the physician's medical practice, his conviction reasonably called into question his ability to practice medicine. The court held that the discipline of physicians for lack of good moral character and conduct undermining public confidence was reasonably related to the promotion of public health, welfare, and safety. The court held that the board's procedures did not violate the physician's due process rights because the fact that the board was exposed to certain evidence in its investigation of the physician was insufficient to call into question the board's fairness at the subsequent adversary hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's order revoking the physician's license to practice medicine.

 

396 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Diatchenko


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 718; 443 N.E.2d 397; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1784


October 6, 1982, Argued  
December 8, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Commonwealth v. Eagles, 419 Mass. 825, 648 N.E.2d 410, 1995 Mass. LEXIS 129 (1995)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Diatchenko v. DA, 466 Mass. 655, 2013 Mass. LEXIS 986, 1 N.E.3d 270 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on June 12, 1981.

The case was tried before Brogna, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Suffolk County Superior Court (Massachusetts) convicting him, after a jury trial, of murder in the first degree and sentencing him pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 2 to the mandatory term of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of stabbing to death an individual while in the course of robbing him. The jury answered special questions which revealed they found deliberate premeditation, extreme atrocity and cruelty, and felony murder. Defendant maintained that the mandatory sentencing provision of § 2 was unconstitutional as cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII, XIV and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 26, but the court disagreed. The court found that although discretionary sentencing was an accepted practice, it was not constitutionally required in cases not involving the death penalty, and the fact that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 2 did not allow consideration of mitigating circumstances, including the fact that defendant was a minor, did not render the statute constitutionally infirm. Further, the court found defendant failed to meet his burden of proving the mandatory sentence was so disproportionate to the crime that it shocked the conscience under the tripartite test the court utilized to evaluate this. Nor had the trial court erred in refusing to grant a 30-day continuance after the jury had been empaneled so that defendant could change counsel.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Beeler v. Downey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 609; 442 N.E.2d 19; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1770


April 8, 1982, Argued  
November 12, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 5, 1979.

The case was tried before Byron, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother challenged the judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which held in favor of defendant physicians in a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought a medical malpractice action alleging that her daughter's death was the result of respiratory suppression and other injuries proximately caused by the negligence of the physicians. At the medical malpractice tribunal hearing held pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 60B, the mother submitted an offer of proof consisting of a file review prepared for her attorney by a physician whose curriculum vitae was included and various documents relating to her daughter's treatment and death. The tribunal determined that the offer of proof and the evidence were sufficient to raise a question of liability appropriate for judicial inquiry. Prior to trial, the physicians submitted a motion in limine seeking the exclusion of the "finding" of the tribunal from jury consideration. The trial judge granted the motion. After a verdict in favor of the physicians, the mother appealed. The court held that exclusion from evidence of the determination of the tribunal was not error.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court in favor of the physicians was affirmed.

 

398 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gagnon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 567; 441 N.E.2d 753; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1766


September 15, 1982, Argued  
November 4, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex.

Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department, one on February 18, 1981, and two on March 9, 1981.

Motions to dismiss were heard by Brady, J., and the cases were tried before Flaksman, J., a District Court judge sitting under statutory authority.

After review was sought in the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative upon defendants' appeal of the denial of their motions to dismiss their indictments for the unlawful distribution of heroin under the Controlled Substances Act, and their subsequent convictions. Defendants claimed that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous in that its penalty clause comprehended two inconsistent penalty schemes.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted on charges of the unlawful distribution of heroin in violation of the Controlled Substances Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32 (a). Their motions to dismiss the indictments were denied and they were convicted and sought review. The court ordered direct appellate review on its own initiative. Defendants claimed that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous because its penalty clause comprehended two inconsistent penalty schemes. The court held that: (1) the second sentence of the statute, which required a "mandatory minimum" term of imprisonment, was inconsistent with the optional language of the first sentence, which allowed punishment by imprisonment, fine, or both, and made the statute unresolvably ambiguous; and (2) the statute afforded no notice as to the potential penalties for its violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for the unlawful distribution of heroin and remanded the cause for the entry of an order granting defendants' motions to dismiss.

 

399 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Boston Gas Co. v. Department of Public Utilities


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 531; 441 N.E.2d 746; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1749


May 6, 1982, Argued  
October 28, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on December 8, 1981.

The case was reported by Liacos, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gas company filed a complaint in the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against the enforcement of 1981 Mass. Acts ch. 604 (Act). Following a hearing, a single justice denied the company's request for a temporary restraining order. Defendant Department of Public Utilities (department) filed a motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The company served customers in Boston as well as in 73 cities and towns near Boston. On January 13, 1981, the company notified state officials that its gas supplies were critically low. On that day, the governor declared an energy emergency. As to the increased costs associated with purchasing supplemental gas supplies on an emergency basis, the chairman of the department indicated that the department would determine the manner in which any extraordinary costs incurred as a result of the emergency would be borne, either by the customers or the shareholders of the gas companies involved. Subsequently the department entered an order enforcing the Act prohibiting the company from recovering undercollections of billings to its customers. The company filed its complaint. The court held that § 1 of the Act did not violate the standing laws provision of the Massachusetts Constitution. However, the court left undecided the constitutionality of § 2 of the Act. The court concluded that the Act was to be given prospective effect only and did not require the company to refund the undercollections from 1980-1981, which it collected between September 1, 1981, and December 7, 1981.


OUTCOME: The court gave the Act prospective effect only and remanded the case to the county court for further proceedings.

 

400 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Sheppard


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


387 Mass. 488; 441 N.E.2d 725; 1982 Mass. LEXIS 1746


December 8, 1981, Argued  
October 26, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 14, 1979.

Pretrial motions to suppress evidence were heard by Ronan, J., and the case was tried before him.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Verdict set aside.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for first-degree murder. Defendant filed pretrial motions to suppress evidence. The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) denied defendant's motions and convicted him of murder in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The question on appeal was whether the exclusionary rule required the suppression of incriminating evidence obtained in the course of a police search conducted in good faith, but pursuant to a warrant that, although issued on probable cause, violated the constitutional and statutory requirement that search warrants describe the things to be seized. The trial court concluded that the warrant was defective because it failed to list the items to be seized or to incorporate a list of those items by reference. However, the trial court concluded that the actual search undertaken was within the limits of the authority the police thought reasonably had been granted. Therefore, the trial court denied the motion to suppress. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that not only was there a lack of reference, but also the warrant listed a different set of items to be seized, and no further description was attached to the warrant. The court held that that the question was whether an error of a magistrate, unrelated to police error, called for the application of the exclusionary rule. The court concluded that it did.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that denied defendant's motion to suppress and convicted him of first-degree murder. The court held that the verdict was set aside.
